185.2 hrs on record
Posted: 29 September, 2021
Spoiler-free review.

Technical
Finally a console ported game worth buying on pc - in three playthroughs I've only run into two crashes and a couple of glitches here and there. The game's well polished and not the buggy mess, I've come to expect by now, when going for AAA games. I suppose it helps, that the game has been out on console for ages now and yes, also running top end hardware. Nevertheless I'm usually very sceptical when it comes to ported games. Hence: BRAVO.

Story
Complemented with the soundtrack and visuals, the story was absolutely breathtaking. Been a long time I invested emotionally into a game. Give them writers a raise :) Even on third playthrough I still had shivers running down my back on some scenes.

Gameplay
The (story) missions themselves are pretty linear, with some hidden side rooms, if you want to explore and get some background infos to the lore/history. The map is, after a first/short walled of segment, open. Side missions and objectives scattered all over the place. Its left up to the player, how he wants to deal with the world. You ain't forced into specific areas and not even forced to complete every side quest. Overall you can get around 80 hours of gameplay, if you want to collect all, listen to all datapoints and so on. If you just focus on the main-missions, I estimate it'll last 40+ hrs ez.

Price
Well worth the 60 bucks on pc.

Addendum
I don't expect Sony's gonna read this, but just in case: This game was one of my favorite games this year. I'd even hand over more of my hard earned $$$ for quality products like this. I will not buy a console however, just to get access to exclusive games - even if they all as good as this one (looking at you there "God of War" or "The Last of us"). So why don't you do us all, and frankly yourself, the favor and learn from this - ease up on exclusives and seize the potential cash cow that is pc gamers ;)

Cheerio
PO3T

THE IDEAL OPEN WORLD GAME

What could have been better:

Optimization:
‚Ä¢ Its kinda iffy still. It took me a while to get the perfect settings. There's a pretty big dip in fps on everything on high or ultra at certain areas. So i put everything at medium to high and everything was smooth. (My specs - Ryzen 5 3600, GTX 1660 super, 16GB RAM)
‚Ä¢ Also there's something wrong with the anti-aliasing, its noticeable on certain sections of the map with a lot of foliage.
‚Ä¢ I had 2 hard crash and it was in the last mission, but it was just after a save so i didn't mind that much.
‚Ä¢ Sometimes when you launch the game it says "Optimizing Shaders" in the main menu (it takes about 3-4 min) if you don't wait it do its thing, its gonna be laggy as hell.
‚Ä¢ About 3-4 times the weather just completely changed in a instant for no reason.

Lip syncing / Conversation cut scene / Facial Animation:
‚Ä¢ All these are a hit or miss. Most times its really good, but other times its distracting or funny.

Audio logs:
‚Ä¢ Hear me out. I love the audio logs in this game, the're very well voice acted and I've listened to almost all of them. They are the one of the major sources for world building and is used heavily throughout the game. But when you put me in a room with 5-6 audio logs, each of which is 1 min long it forced me to stand there and listen to each one. I know you can listen to them later but most use the area where it was scanned to tell the story. At least I would have liked these audio logs to be spread around so I could at least go from point A to B listening to it.

Spoiler:



WHY ITS SO GOOD:

Aloy:
‚Ä¢ I really like her. Character design wise and how shes written. What I love is that she's not perfect. She has selfish goals and at times act childish just like any real person.
‚Ä¢ But she's also strong and independent and isn't afraid of calling people out. (I especially love it when she calls people for being sexist, its hilarious)
‚Ä¢ Alloy strikes a good balance between being strong but vulnerable.

The World:
‚Ä¢ Probably one of the most unique open worlds I have explored. Every new location had me in awe to see this future where nature and machine co exist.
‚Ä¢ It is of perfect size with lots of verticality which I really enjoyed.
‚Ä¢ You can see the remains of the old ones while exploring like old tanks, buildings and so much more which creates this immersive world where your intrigued to know what happened there.
‚Ä¢ Also it has almost no loading screen, except a few areas, but its amazing considering the size and details of the world.

The Story:
‚Ä¢ I loved the story. Its such a breadth of fresh air.
‚Ä¢ It has a pretty slow start (The first 5 hour or so was pretty slow, but after "The Proving" sh*t gets real, real fast).
‚Ä¢ The lore was interesting and made me wanted to know more about this weird world.
‚Ä¢ Overall the writing is solid. The way the characters interacts with each other, alloys random one liners etc were all a treat and genuinely got a few chuckles out of me.

ENEMIES:
‚Ä¢ HOLY SH*T ITS AMAZING. ITS ANIMALS BUT MACHINES!! Such a simple concept but done with such elegance.
‚Ä¢ There were quite a few surprises along the way with made my JAW drop ;)
‚Ä¢ The audio queue for each machine is distinct and clearly understandable even when they' are off screen.
‚Ä¢ Also the dismemberment is oh so satisfying and looks freaking cool.

Side Quests:
‚Ä¢ There aren't a lot which is actually a big plus. I would have hated if they went with the ubisoft copy past missions.
‚Ä¢ But here there are a few and most are amazing with unique and interesting motive like in the witcher 3 but less in number.

NPC:
‚Ä¢ Every single NPC is interesting and has their own opinion, believe and motive. Everyone won't accept you even if you prove yourself which is great because some people are just d*icks, and the game doesn't change that.

The Combat:
‚Ä¢ It will seem pretty basic at first, but it builds on those concepts and makes a system that all feels cohesive together. Whatever load out you carry, everything synergies really well.
‚Ä¢ The game has a good combat loop
‚Ä¢ Even after maxing out everything and having good gear the game was pretty challenging which is a plus.

Costume Design:
‚Ä¢ I have to praise this. Its amazing! Everything Alloy and the other main characters wear are so aesthetically pleasing and appropriate to the respective tribes.
‚Ä¢ Each tribe's believes and customs are visible from what they wear.

Photo Mode:
‚Ä¢ I have to put this here, I'm a big sucker for virtually photography and this game was a treat. Every single location looks stunning and the photo mode was the icing on top. *mwah*

DLC - The Frozen Wilds:
‚Ä¢ A completely new section of the map to explore? A new Story with even more interesting sh*t to do? New machines? OH IT COMES WITH THE GAME AND YOU DON'T HAVE TO PAY EXTRA!?? SOLD
‚Ä¢ Shout out to the amazing snow physics in this section
‚Ä¢ Also most of the issues I had with the main game are greatly improved here, so they are going in the right direction.

Misc:
‚Ä¢ Thank you Guerrilla games for not charging full price for the port.

HYPED FOR HZD: FORBIDDEN WEST !! WO-WO !!

Recommended
125.5 hrs on record
Posted: 7 March, 2021
OVERVIEW ‚Ü¥
Horizon Zero Dawn is a third person/single player action game set in post-apocalyptic land ruled by mechanical creatures, in which the remains of humanity are split into warring tribes and kingdoms that dwell among the ruins of ancient times. And so here we are, in a regressed to a primitive state Earth, where we take on a role of a young huntress, an outcast of the Nora tribe, Aloy, who's forced by a series of events to go on a journey to not only uncover her past but also the origins of the world she currently lives in therefore the fall of the previous civilization.

GRAPHICS AND AUDIO ‚Ü¥
People can say a lot of different things about this game but we can all agree that as funny as it sounds, an apocalypse was never more beautiful and so visually stunning as it is in HZD which results in it being an absolute design masterpiece. I know, who would have thought.. Okay, I'm not kidding. The graphics alone can blow your mind. Sure, there are some tiny buggy things you can notice if you try hard enough (and you're a screenshot hoe) but it still doesn't diminish the fact that this apocalyptic world is simply breathtaking. From the lush and seemingly alive forests of Sacred Lands amongst the rippling of shining creeks and endlessly flowing rivers where sunlight strikes and glints on the gliding surface to the incredibly detailed snowy mountains from the great plateau to the captivating contrast between the days and nights which brings in a truly otherworldly lighting effects to this extraordinary environment.. Add now to this immersive graphics, an also impressive sound design which let's you with it's combination of flowing/soothing instrumental beats and mechanic sounds, draw you into a prehistoric yet futuristic life on Zero Dawn's Earth.

GAMEPLAY ‚Ü¥
The most pleasant surprise to me was how fluid and fun the gameplay actually is and beacuse of this, it simply went beyond my expectations. You've got an open world were exploration is always good and any kind of combat, whatever it be with machines, animals or humans is extremely rewarding but progressivly gets tougher the longer you get into the storyline which in itself is a pretty cool aspect. The mechanics of the combat are basically giving us a healthy challange in which we cannot always relay on one weapon through the whole game and makes us realize that it's sometimes best to switch your fighting style between stealh and full head-on attacks or just simply figure out each machine's attack pattern, capabilities and weaknesses to get a successful outcome without failing in the process or worse dying. Plus the fact that we can only save our progress in a campfire makes it all more exciting even if a bit cumbersome at times. The only thing that could deserve a criticism in this interesting game style would probably be the melee combat that feels like it has been added last minute as an afterthought from the devs to balance the heavy push on the player to use a long range combat instead.

STORY ‚Ü¥
We're set to immerse ourselves in a bit of self discovery mission for the main protagonist in this bizzare new world, all while trying to also uncover the truths about this strange corruption that's plaguing machines and wreaking havoc among Earth's remaining population. It's an exciting journey from the very start that leaves us with lots of interesting questions to the end where most of them are finally answered; it's filled with enough twists and turns to make it fun and immersive for any player dubbing themselves an RPG ethusiast. And to add a cherry on the top, the game offers us a large amount of side-missions, collectibles and challenges around the world to complete that in turn makes us stronger, thanks to a very generous XP and item rewards which doesn't leaves us with the impression of grinding for futher progress. Truly, a pretty well written story with a good dose of mystery to make the player enjoy and especially want to slowly piece together what happened to the Ancient Ones and the impacts of theirs decisions on the current state of Aloy's world but foremost what it means for her future. Ps. The atmposphere in this game is to die for, lol.

PERFORMANCE, BUGS AND GLITCHES ‚Ü¥
Ughh, there was the common problem that comes with a console games ported to pc which is the optimization. It was a bit of a problem since it resulted in lots of visual glitches, pretty low fps and some crashes that I've gotten to experience a lot when I started playing the game. But I can honestly say that since the last patch 1.06 HZD is running as smoothly as possible on my medium/high settings so I don't think anyone should have problems with running the game as it is right now 'cause it performs exceptionally well... But if you still get some crashes, it might help if you run the game .exe as admin instead of booting it up straight from steam and maybe putting the graphics on medium/low to balance the fact that this game loves to eat up players CPU like it's candy, no matter if you reach the minimum or high specs... I won't say anything about the camera having a mind of its own 'cause I truly didn't had any problems with it, so ¬Ø\_(„ÉÑ)_/¬Ø.

CONCLUSION ‚Ü¥
Horizon Zero Dawn: To hate it or to love it? In my opinion... love it. It's an amazing open world action game and a real treat that will give you a lot of hours to explore the vast and enchanting world of Zero Dawn with it's dangerous machines, and maybe not groundbreaking but very interesting storyline to follow; an absolute must play for action game fans that want an exciting journey to keep them at the edge of theirs seats with some of the best visuals available in gaming period.


Horizon Zero Dawn | March 7, 2021 | [‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ‚òÖ]

I was apprehensive to get this game initially on launch because I heard about it crashing/bugs etc on PC. I would highly recommend anyone who loves RPGs to get this game now. I haven't had any issues with this game with over 50 hours played and it is easily one of the best open world games I have ever played. The combat is amazingly satisfying and the game is absolutely gorgeous. If anyone reading this is considering buying it I would say stop wavering and purchase it. It is totally worth it and you will be amazed by the world you experience. I would put it in my top 5 favorite games of all time.

Recommended
42.0 hrs on record
Posted: 26 November, 2020
‚ô¶Ô∏è Horizon Zero Dawn
Horizon Zero Dawn is one of Sony‚Äôs few first party IPs to make its way to PC and the Steam platform. For years throughout the Ps4s lifecycle we heard critics and fans alike rave about Horizon and what an experience it is. Now we get to test their claims at a high resolution with unlocked framerates.

Story & Characters
Narrative
‚Üí Horizon starts off by giving us a taste at this strange new world. The feelings of excitement and awe during my first couple hours were at an all time high. Part of the story is fully grasping and immersing yourself in Horizons bizarre world. The narrative is a relatively basic one, and takes a little while to get up to speed. But once it does get the ball rolling it really starts laying the real truth behind Aloys past and how this future of Earth came to be.
‚Üí Aloy is on a mission to find out her true purpose, all while this strange corruption is plaguing machines and wreaking havoc among Earth's remaining population.I won‚Äôt go into detail but the second half of the game really starts answering questions about the truth of this world. Horizon‚Äôs story is a really exciting journey from start to finish, filled with enough twists and turns to keep you at the edge of your seat.

Characters
‚Üí Through the roughly ~40 hour campaign you will learn with Aloy about her past and fall in love with her as a person. Aloy is an amazing protagonist who reacts believably to shocking events. And through the journey you will come across supporting characters some good, some bad, some outright mysterious. Each and every one of them play a big role one way or another to progression Aloy to her goals. All have their own personal goals and missions with a unique personality

Rost a lovable father figure, who will do whatever it takes to protect and help Aloy. 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: NotASpy


Gameplay
Combat
‚Üí The main form of fighting off these ferocious machines is through meleeing with your spear or shooting one of dozens of projectiles. Aloys hits make an impacting clash as her weapons clang off monstrous machines. And retreating back with a bow is always a viable strategy if that is more your jist. If you want an idea of how the combat plays it‚Äôs similar to how Monster Hunter: World feels, where you must use all tools at your disposal to take down gigantic beasts. The machines attacked are heavily choreographed and require you to learn attack patterns for almost every machine. And pressing ‚Äòv‚Äô to turn on your focus will highlight weak points and show weaknesses for whichever machine you highlight. This turns combat into this fast paced in and out game where you strike with your spear, dodge, and try to fire at its weak points with your bow.
‚Üí Aloy also has a roll to dodge enemy attacks which is difficult to master but is necessary to take on some of the biggest machines: There is also a stealth option to get the first strike on unsuspecting machines, and useful for taking out camps of humanoids Metal Gear Solid style.

Difficulty
‚Üí Horizon offers six different difficulty settings ranging from ‚ÄòStory‚Äô to ‚ÄòUltra Hard‚Äô depending if you just want to focus on the story or if you want to stay awake at night in fear of saw-toothed robotic pumas. I played on ‚Äònormal‚Äô and I feel it gave a great experience, where combat was hard enough to make me focus but wasn‚Äôt easy enough to zone out and just wait for the next cutscene to play.

Weapons & Tools
‚Üí You have your usual bow, bigger bow, and spear but unique weapons like the tripcaster, sling, or rope gun. Your bow can of course be equipped with many different status ailments for use depending on the enemies weakness. This can be from fire arrows to armor piercing ones. And the tripcaster can lay status ailment lines that cause damage when enemies walk through them. The ropecaster can pin enemies to the ground leaving them vulnerable to heavy damage. Horizon offers many types of enemies to battle with more than enough different ways to defeat them, and no option is more right than any other.

Stealth is quite a viable play style in Horizon. Using distractions and a sharp spear you can methodically take out packs of enemies. 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: NotASpy


Upgrades
‚Üí Throughout your journey you will come across merchants that will trade you new armors and weapons in return for your resources. This provides incentive to kill machines to get all their drops as many machines provide an individual ‚Äòcurrency‚Äô to trade for unique armors and weapons. You‚Äôre also given the option to craft upgrades to your ammo pouches, carrying capacity on health potions. Etc. Meanwhile you will get modifications from defeated enemies that can be slotted in your armor and weapons for powerful buffs. This can be from +armor piercing to better handling.

Skills
‚Üí Not only are you tailoring your gear and weapons best suited for your playstyle, you also gain skill points on leveling up to enhance certain aspects of Aloy. If you want to rely heavily on your bow then upgrade its ‚Äòslow-mo‚Äô time and learn how to fire three arrows at once. If you want to be up close and personal enhance your weapon damage with deadly finisher attacks.

Enemy Design
‚Üí One of Horizons many eye catching design choices, is of course the various machines you will encounter. I can say that each machine fights differently with their own fighting styles. With over twenty plus different enemies you will encounter, each being as thrilling as the other. Think of each enemy as a sort of Dark Souls (Are we still comparing games to Dark Souls in 2020?) boss where they each have an attack pattern to learn and large attacks to avoid.

Side Content
‚Üí Besides the main story there is a load of side content to get lost in. From interesting side missions with their own little arc and of course uninteresting fetch quests. Also including exploring ‚Äòruins‚Äô to gain important knowledge on certain enemy types. It even has timed trials if that is more of your thing. Most importantly Horizon on PC comes with a whole extra fifteen hours of story in the form of its expansion ‚ÄúFrozen Wilds‚Äù.

Visuals & Sound
Visuals
‚Üí The world design rivals Red Dead 2s visual quality. Filled with high quality textures with an amazing day/night cycle that brings in otherworldly lighting effects. There were many points across my playthrough where I had to take a good minute and pause in photo mode to admire the visual fidelity offered by Gorilla Games. I will say that at the launch of Horizon on PC performance was quite rocky and my 1080ti struggled to get playable frame rates and constantly crash. But I have played Horizon recently with my 1080ti and I will say the many patches made, it is finally at a really acceptable level of port quality.

Sound
‚Üí To accompany the amazing visual design there is also an impressive sound design. Each enemy sounds viscous in its own right, their attacks crack with explosions and really sound scary. And on the opposite end there is blissful music that pairs perfectly with Horizons stunning vistas. The music is a combination of free flowing beats with robotic sounds spiking at times, it really sells this prehistoric yet futuristic world of Horizon Zero Dawn.

From highly detailed mountain ranges to the harshest snowfalls. Horizon Zero Dawn offers a variety of detailed environments. 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: NotASpy


‚ô¶Ô∏è Conclusion
In conclusion Horizon Zero Dawn mostly lives up to the hype of a first party Playstation exclusive. Now nothing was groundbreaking, but it offers an above average narrative mixed with tense combat against monstrous machines, and some of the best visuals available in gaming period. It is truly a must play for anyone with a capable machine and no doubt worth its price, especially on sale!
Overall Score 8.5/10

Recommended
60.3 hrs on record
Posted: January 2, 2021
Intro
(100% Spoiler-Free Review)
Horizon Zero Dawn (HZD) is an open-world action-adventure game with a post apocalyptic setting. After a great catastrophe, humanity was nearly wiped out and regressed to a primitive state, as nations have been replaced by warring tribes and kingdoms. Survivors dwell among the ruins of ancient times, populated by animal-like machines that threaten human life daily. Players impersonate Aloy, a tribe outcast fostered by Rost, who found and cared for her since infancy. A series of events forces her to embark on a quest of legendary proportions, destined to change the world.

üü© The Good Side
The Apocalypse never was more beautiful
Visually and more importantly artistically, HZD is an absolute masterpiece. Aside from the incredibly detailed graphics, spectacular vistas and scrumptious light effects, the art direction behind each NPC, machine and environment is truly one of the best I've ever seen in 22 years of gaming. The care and research behind each animation, location, animal, plant and just about anything else is phenomenal. The world always feels vibrant, alive thanks to dynamic weather and independent NPCs going about their business as time passes.

Thrill of the Hunt
This game emphasizes like no other the concepts of preparation and knowing one's enemy. Each adversary, be it machine or human, has different attack patterns and weaknesses to exploit - that may as well change as the battle progresses. Resource gathering and crafting play a vital role in Aloy's journey against more and more dangerous foes: picking her fights wisely and using the correct tool for the job among the many available will be key to victory. Skill and preparation are equally rewarded in a combat system that always feels challenging and satisfactory.

Everything has a meaning
HZD offers a large amount of side-quests, collectibles and challenges around the world for Aloy to complete and in turn become stronger, thanks to generous XP and item rewards. Not only that, but such missions often unlock unique weapons, gear pieces or other quests, while even collectibles offer special rewards if entire "sets" of them are found in the world. Certain missions may even influence the endgame parts, as some secondary characters may ally or abandon Aloy depending on her actions. Every single side activity is worth doing, varied and rewarding.

The complete journey
This PC port of HZD includes all DLC ever released, as well as the Frozen Wilds expansion which offers much greater challenge, and the Ultra Hard difficulty setting for NG and NG+ modes - which brings a masochistic level of brutality. Along with visual improvements compared to console, this is really the best version of this title one could possibly hope to play. Porting issues have been fixed since release, and the game runs brilliantly now.


Visually, HZD is out of this world tier. Seriously. However, such beauty comes at a high price in terms of hardware resources. 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Tamaster


üü• The Bad Side
404: bad sides not found
I couldn't think of any bad sides worth mentioning for HZD. That's the first time in 10 years of writing reviews this has ever happened. Any flaw the game has is at worst minor and is not nearly severe enough to mention as a standalone issue. Well played Guerrilla Games, well played indeed.

It took me around 60 hours to complete the main story, Frozen Wilds DLC and all side activities everywhere on Very Hard difficulty. For the price of 50‚Ç¨ and exceptional quality, I can recommend buying this game for full price.

Melee, ranged, stealth or traps are all viable approaches to any fight. Whatever one may choose, combat is always exciting. 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Tamaster


In-Depth Breakdown
üéÆ Gameplay Analysis
Gameplay is divided into Exploration, Combat, Quests and Character Management.

Exploration
Is initially performed on foot, while later on also by mounting certain machine types once able to do so. The world is immense, but thankfully dotted with Campfires acting as fast-travel points, that however costs Travel Packs to enable - more based on larger distances. While initially limited, the map becomes soon fully explorable, with each biome housing diverse machines, some far too dangerous initially. Quests, collectibles, challenges and lore entries are scattered evenly throughout, making exploration of each corner rewarding and interesting. New quests and important locations are automatically highlighted once found, as well.

Combat
Is the core of HZD's gameplay, and is based mainly on knowing each machine's attack pattern, capabilities and weaknesses to succeed. Timing dodge-rolls well, laying out traps before starting a fight, and having a steady aim are equally important factors in surviving attacks that, on high difficulties, may very well one-shot Aloy in some cases. Machine enemies are highly adaptable and change their attack style based on damage they sustain: removing an enemy's ranged weapon may provoke it to use new attack strategies not seen before, for example. This brilliant system makes combat unpredictable and interesting.

Elemental damage resistances and weaknesses, along with unique weakpoints such as ranged weapons, that can be detached and used against Aloy's enemies, all come into play depending on the enemy faced. A wide array of tools ranging from bows to technologically advanced bolt-casters opens up to plenty of approaches, while skill tree evolution goes a long way from start to end of the adventure. Enemy variants with even more deadly skills sum to the normal counterparts in due time, making combat all the more varied.

Quests
Ranged from the ordinary fetch task to more exotic ones such as Hunter Challenges or uniquely crafted missions with standalone parameters. Between challenges, regular quests and collectible-related tasks, there is really a whole lot to do, and it's interesting each time. Each quest is always indicated on the map, but in some cases a wide are is displayed and is up to player to think over how to progress. In the case of collectibles only the general area is hinted at, while the location remains hidden

Character Management
Can be performed on the fly at any moment, even in combat. Materials gathered from slain machines, hunted animals, herbs or containers all come into play in keeping Aloy stocked with munitions, potions and other supplies. Crafting is a regular task, and more exotic ammunition types will incur into higher expenses to make. Picking fights wisely, looting everything and selling unnecessary surplus are all key to not run out of materials.

Modding weapons and armor can make them much more powerful, while mods can adapt to a particular purpose or damage type: one can choose between a stronger but slower weapon, or favor DPS over raw damage, all depends on the mod configuration.


Weapon and gear mods can emphasize a specific type of damage, or increase rate of fire and resistances. They are essential later on. 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Tamaster

- Average RAM Usage: 4.5 GB [Average]
- Settings Used: Custom (All High, Textures Ultra, Models Ultra, Clouds Medium, FX CAS OFF), 1440p 60Hz.
- Overall Optimization Rating: Average

Bugs & Other Issues
None.

Recommended
291.6 hrs on record
Posted: January 26
I need to preface this review by noting that I am an adventure/puzzle gamer and avoid titles with combat. I also rarely play RPGs (although I played them frequently 'back in the day.'). So, HZD was a big step outside of my comfort zone.

I fell in love with the game within the first few minutes. You play Aloe (from a 3rd person perspective), a remarkable woman warrior who is an outcast from her tribe. You build skills, harvest resources, obtain weapons/armor, craft potions and ammo, gather collectibles, run errands, and do quests (side quests and the main story-line). The world is post apocalyptic with killer machines patrolling the landscape. Humans try to survive in a primitive culture.

The art is beautiful and the voice overs and overall sound track are exceptional. There is enough to see and do that I can play for hours (and hours) and always have a new experience to find. The world is truly 'open' and the map is vast, with settlements, ruins, vistas, and a host of mechanical creatures. A quick travel feature allows you to jump to points previously visited and you can save (as often as you like) at any campfire you have activated.

Since I am an admitted wuss at combat, I am playing with the difficulty set to 'Easy.' This means that I stand a chance of survival and can reap the full benefits of the game without constantly screaming in frustration. For me, however, the game is still challenging and requires stealth, strategy, and perfect execution of my plans. In HZD, brute force (charging into the fray) is not very effective and wastes a lot of resources.

The game has an intuitive interface and, although there are quite a few hot keys, most of the interface can be accessed through a single screen (map, inventory, crafting, quests, and notebook). The notebook is invaluable as you catalog the machines you've encountered and it provides an assessment of the strengths and weaknesses of each. For me, playing with a keyboard and mouse is most effective. The interface assists you by noting quest tasks, locations, etc. This may seem like hand-holding to some, but it is a nice feature to keep me on track.

My approach has been to initially invest in building XP, skills, and weapons/armor before moving to the main story quest. This requires gathering collectibles (which can be sold), doing lower level errands/side quests, and generally improving my character. I focused on building my health capacity and obtaining stealth skills/armor - two areas quite helpful to an adventurer. Although I am normally a completionist, I am not even thinking about Steam achievements at this phase of the game.

I highly recommend HZD to those who want to test the waters of a beautiful and engaging RPG with stealth/combat. There is no shame in playing with the 'Easy' setting if you are not a combat veteran. My only complaint is that HZD is very addictive. I keep returning to the game to do 'one more quest' and it is impacting my sleep schedule!

EDIT 1:

System specs:

GPU: GTX 1070
CPU: Ryzen 5 3600
RAM: 16 GB

Here are some suggestions that I have gotten from other users that have helped me in the meantime for anyone that does have the game. As suggested by Steam User Jom, I put Shadows at low and Ambient Occlusion at medium (the lowest it can go without turning it off) while leaving other settings at high. This greatly reduced the amount of stuttering and hiccups that I got.

As suggested by Tiny Rick, I went into the game folder and ran the .exe in Admin mode. This is supposed to help prevent crashes. I've been out of the starting area for a while and am running around the world. There is still some pretty nasty pop-in that happens now and then, but I haven't had any crashes while doing this, and I tried upping my graphics to ultra. So far, no hitches that I've been able to see so far because of this. Will continue to test it out to see if it runs better.

Recommended
27.0 hrs on record
Posted: June 13, 2021
Where to even start with this game. I won't add spoilers, but even though the gameplay is great, and the graphics are top notch, it's the story that really hooks me and makes me think about the game even after having beat it several times.

To say that Horizons story is epic is like saying The Matrix was cool. It's an understatement. I've played a lot of games, and it is difficult to surprise me with plot, story, voice acting, motion capture. After hundreds of games, after awhile their stories start (rightly) looking like bad soap opera scripts, where the villain is as likely to monologue you to death as they are to fight you. Where you're forced to listen to endless manifestoes by the bad guys trying to justify their decisions.

Horizon is not like that. While it's story is fantastical and unbelievable, it is also not a soap opera. It's dramatic, but not fake hollywood drama. The writing of this game is more on par with a Nebula Award wining scifi novel. The team that wrote this game should write a book because as a fervent scifi reader, I would have put this story up there with The Three Body Problem, with A Deepness in the Sky, with Children of Time, with The Diamond Age. It's that level of writing and world building and just wow.

And the way the story unfolds, it's not forced exposition and narration that reveals the world of Horizons like a movie. Instead your own curiosity and need to know drives you to uncover the evidence, and to piece the puzzle together. Later in the game, much later, it is eventually made more clear what happened, but it never felt forced or boring. I never got the urge to skip a cutscene.

The Acting. The people in the game, the voice actors, the animators, the directors, they managed to make the characters feel like living, breathing people, not like video game characters. When a character does something, when they befriend you, or fight you, they do so for reasons that make sense to them, not because the story demands they do those things. As such, you feel like these are real people, flawed, doing the best they can. Aloy especially is one of the greatest video game protagonists of the last 20 years. She is more badass than Master Chief and yet she isn't a slow walking away from an explosion badass, she's an approachable, grounded, empathetic hero that feels like a person trying to do actual good in the world, not some stick figure killing machine that action games usually use as a place holder for actual heroics. It is also refreshing to see a female character whos armor is not a string bikini and who has free agency in their life. Aloy doesn't have a B story where she falls in love, she's not wooed or wooing, she's not sexualized in any manner, and feels like something that video games could direly use more of.

Then there are the NPCs in this world. Big, elaborate, organic, robo dinosaurs. You never get tired of seeing a walker the size of a skyscraper walk by and scaling it to get the lay of the land. Robo T-REX chasing you is the scariest thing in this game. Even when you can survive fighting them one on one, or learn the tame ability, encountering one of those things is always a heart attack. They just look so badass. I'm sure a real Trex never looked so incredibly deadly.

I have become a jaded video game player, and I seldom get excited for games anymore, especially big budget AAA games that all look and feel the same, the repeat sequels every year, new far cry, new assassins creed, etc, so boring. But Horizon is THE best game I have played in the last 10 years at least. At least it's the most enjoyable game I've played in a very long time.

Recommended
83.8 hrs on record
Posted: July 24
Fighting the backlog

A typical way of increasing the backlog is to put open-world games there since they require a lot of time for completion while others not so much. I did the prologue and some missions in HZD then added it to my collection named "backlog" on Steam. I left it there for a year. Just recently I have decided to pick it up and I did not regret it. Not one bit. After clocking 80 hours with it I can safely say I've had most fun with this game in recent years.

A world overrun by machines

Initially HZD looks like a game taking place in prehistoric times. With your hero you use spear, bows and other ranged weapons to fight enemies. And while enemies include humans representing various tribes another group consists of machines. A lot of machines. Machines that look like huge lizards, crocodiles, hawks, bulls, crabs, panthers and even ostriches.

But who are these machines and where did they come from? The remains of old buildings and rusted out vehicles confirm something went wrong decades ago. Our protagonist, Aloy, initially wants a place for herself (acceptance is important as she is considered an outcast) but beside trying to improve the relations between various factions she is interested in exploring the story of the machines.

As one would expect from such an open-world game HZD has beautiful graphics, lots of cutscenes and great voice acting. Fans of Lance Reddick will rejoice as he plays an important part in the story. But then again the side missions and other activities will contribute mostly to your playtime as the story missions can be done in 10-20 hours.

Exploring the world

The world of HZD is huge and sports a lot of different locations. You can sprint along the river in barren wastelands or hunt for foxes, turkeys and boars in lush forests. Vantage points can often be accessed high up in snowy mountains and Aloy also infiltrates many bases - some found exclusively underground. Hunting animals (including fish in the river!) and gathering wood and all kinds of flowers will be important as crafting is required for almost everything be it the creation of special ammunition to your weapons or pouches to ensure you have increased capacity for all items. Inventory management can be pain and it requires some getting used to. You will also find a lot of unnecessary items only good for trading and finally we get to play a game where the collectibles can actually be given somebody, a collector, who is willing to reward you in return.

Skills

As expected this wouldn't be a real open-world game without skills to purchase and levelling up regularly. Abilities you buy can affect your melee combat, your stealth-based attacks and you can learn not only to override enemies but to mount some of your allied, machinery companions. Both missions and tougher combat give you a lot of XP - to fully max out Aloy you really need to do everything in the world HZD has to offer.

Focusing on highlighted areas

Combat is interesting. Rarer weapons will allow you to use new types of ammunition. You will soon learn as you explore that damage output alone cannot win you any combat. Aloy has a little bluetooth-like device called Focus - its special scanning technology will highlight weaker parts of the enemies. But you have to catalog all monsters during your first encounter to see what type of ammunition is their weakness.

For instance, those attacking you with fire-based liquid are almost completely fire resistant. Use freezing arrows here. Always look for highlighted parts that can be removed. An interesting type of arrow causes tearing which means no damage, at all, but a very high probability of removing components from the beasts.

Some parts explode after continued firing, others reveal additional (weaker) parts and various body parts act as weapons which means once removed you can actually use them against their previous owners. Each robot requires a different tactic which means encountering a herd with 3-4 different machines can easily be deadly for you. HZD can be enjoyed best when you triumph in such combats. You also have to bear in mind that Aloy can roll away to evade attacks but spamming the button allows the more perceptive enemies to figure out where you'll land so that they can attack accordingly. You can begin playing HZD as someone already familiar with the genre but this game will still give you many challenging encounters.

DLC

The Steam release of HZD comes years after its original release on the PS which means we get a DLC included. In The Frozen Wilds Aloy travels up north to more snowy areas where you'll face more difficult combat. It's fun how Lance Reddick laments that you really shouldn't enter the new region before completing your current task (referring to the main story); as long as you've met the needed level requirement you'll be fine. And if you still aren't bored of HZD after all this there's New Game+ and higher difficulty levels offering you even more options for character customization.

Summary

HZD is an exceptionally great game with challenging combat, interesting story and a built-in photo mode that allows you to demonstrate your creative abilities. While the story feels cheesy sometimes and some side missions are repetitive your time in this dystopian future will definitely be well spent. Hope you'll have a powerful rig as HZD can be very demanding.

Recommended
246.7 hrs on record
Posted: February 20
I waited to write this review until I had enough time in the game to really assess it.

Broken down, here is my opinion. This is only an opinion.

First the world: It's amazing, beautiful and immerses you into the story. The story line is engaging and pulls you in. You look forward to your next clue. It is well designed and written. It creates emotion in the player as you feel what Aloy is experiencing. The voice acting for the main quest and story are done very well.

The Main Quest: Engaging and makes you want to continue on. It is well voiced and the dialogue makes sense and is worth listening to.

Combat: The machine AI and game AI are some of the best I have seen. Machines will learn as the fight progresses and will learn from the players play style so that they will attack when they have the advantage and hide when the player has the advantage. Strategy before engagement is the key. Using the tools provided the player, prior and during combat will usually end with success. not using the tools given, or jumping in without a strategy for each combat situation will usually end in defeat. Bandit camps are engaging and challenging and again strategy is the key when infiltrating a bandit camp. I really enjoyed the combat in this game. It never felt cookie cutter or static. It always felt fresh and challenging. Every situation is completely different. Even during the second play through, when I thought I knew what was going to happen, the machines and situation changed. It was never dull. I enjoyed the challenge and the overall combat experience.

Combat Mechanics: As far as the player character or Aloy goes, the mechanics in combat are fantastic. They are varied and unique. They make you want to learn and perfect the harder moves in combat to see the effect and damage they do. Animations for Aloy, in combat, were very well done and they make you want to try different things in a fight. Again no cookie cutter combat here.
As far as the machines and enemy NPC‚Äôs go, combat mechanics again are incredible. You can actually see the machines think and work together, their animations are very well done and make the machines look alive. Human enemy NPC‚Äôs are the same way, they work together and can be very challenging to fight.

Side quests: Some are well done, some are a bit out of context and don't really make sense. Voicing in the side quests can get a bit sub-par, the dialogue in some cases feels forced and awkward.
Errand quests: Mostly sub-par and awkward and don't really fit the story very well, although some are necessary for the end game conflict. Voicing again in errand quests feels forced and awkward. It's almost like the errand quests and some side quest were after thoughts just to add content, that really didn't fit. None of which detracted from the game either, they just didn't add anything useful to the experience.

The Frozen North DLC: The world up north is amazing and beautiful, very immersive. Combat up north is incredible. I loved the challenge and the experience. The game, up north, again, makes you feel what Aloy is experiencing. You almost feel the cold, the dark and the loneliness. You can see and feel the harshness of the environment and feel for the Banuk, who have chosen to live there.
The main quest in the Frozen North, is well done and voiced very well, it makes you want to complete it. It makes sense and adds to the main game in an immersive way.
Side quests and errand quests in the Frozen North, are well done as far as voicing and dialogue. They make sense and are on par with the level of voicing and dialogue of the main game. I really enjoyed the time spent in the Frozen North.

Overall: I highly recommend this game, it is an experience that most will enjoy and probably will play for a long time. I am sure most people will play through this game multiple times.

At the time of this writing I have about 200 hours in the game and have completed the regular game and a Game+ play through to the end. I will play it again. In my humble opinion, this game is well worth the price.

It takes a lot of convincing for me to invest in any AAA title of this size, but my god it was worth it. Horizon Zero Dawn left a lasting impression.

This is one of those games that may be worth delaying progression through the main story, if you don't want to run the risk of losing interest upon completion of the final mission. My only gripes, which don't have much of an impact on my overall experience, would be:

- Not much range with the facial expression, all the models look like they've had about 50 botox injections
- The game is well balanced, but be careful of levelling up too fast too early on, as it does make some missions slightly easier than they should be
- Hilariously unconvincing death animations/acting!

Overall I'd give this a solid 9/10. Probably a 10 if it weren't for all of the above. Would recommend üëç

Recommended
61.0 hrs on record
Posted: October 20, 2020
Horizon Zero Dawn is a third person action game set in a post apocalyptic open world where the Earth has been overrun by machines and the remains of Humanity live in small tribes with primitive technology. The player character, Aloy, must go on a quest to investigate the origin of the machines and the fall of the previous civilization.

Gameplay

‚Ä¢ Along her journey, Aloy will fight against machines and Human bandits. The design of the machines is really cool. Their appearance and behaviour is similar to animals such as horses, cows, tigers, bulls, crabs, crocodiles, hawks, or dinosaurs like the velociraptor, brontosaurus and t-rex. As well as melee attacks, some of them have laser weapons mounted on their back, or can spam fire or frost projectiles at you, and one machine even has a cloaking device.

‚Ä¢ Most bandits are armed with axe or bow, but their leaders have powerful heavy weapons like a minigun or grenade launcher, which you can pick up and use until they run out of ammo.

‚Ä¢ Aloy can wield a staff for melee attacks and various different types of bows which can shoot arrows enhanced with elemental damage. Fire does extra damage over time, frost will slow enemy movement and increase damage taken, while shock will stun them for a few seconds leaving them vulnerable to a critical melee attack. There‚Äôs also a really useful skill which lets you load up two or three arrows to fire simultaneously with any bow.

‚Ä¢ There‚Äôs a strong focus on using stealth, hiding in long grass to sneak past groups of powerful enemies, or getting close enough to perform a melee takedown on weaker enemies.

‚Ä¢ Combat can be quite tactical. One of my favourite weapons, the Tripcaster, lets you place explosive or shock tripwires on the ground, which will detonate when a machine runs over them. Before the start of a fight, I liked to place a few tripwires in strategic locations, between trees or rocks, then I‚Äôd stand with the tripwires between myself and the machines, shooting the machines with arrows while trying to lure them into charging through the tripwires.

‚Ä¢ Some machines have weak points that can be targeted to deal extra damage, or you can destroy their weapon components to reduce their threat to you, although this can be tricky when fighting against fast moving or flying enemies. Its actually easier when fighting bosses because of their huge size and slower movement.

‚Ä¢ You can unlock the ability to override machines to make them fight each other, or to use them as a mount to travel around the world quicker. I didn‚Äôt use mounts often because I quickly discovered that this will draw aggro from lots of nearby enemies (similar to driving a car in a Far Cry game), so its less stressful to just sneak around on foot.

‚Ä¢ You can buy several outfits from traders which change Aloy‚Äôs appearance. Weapons and outfits can be upgraded with modifications which provide bonuses to various damage types, damage resistances, or stealth.

Story

‚Ä¢ Story is very well written with an interesting sense of mystery, and I enjoyed slowly piecing together what happened in the old world. The conflict between Humans and machines has similarities to the likes of The Terminator and The Matrix.

‚Ä¢ Most side quests have unique stories which are of a similar quality level to those in Witcher 3, and much better than the copy and paste tasks usually found in open world games. Sometimes you‚Äôll wander across machines and Humans fighting each other, while clearing bandit camps will allow friendly tribes to move in. All of these elements help to bring the world to life.

‚Ä¢ Voice acting is fantastic, especially Ashly Burch (who previously voiced Chloe in Life is Strange) as Aloy and Lance Reddick (Fringe, Quantum Break) who plays an important supporting character.

‚Ä¢ Lip syncing during cutscenes is the best I‚Äôve seen since Hellblade Senua‚Äôs Sacrifice.

Technical

‚Ä¢ The environment looks fantastic, from the forests, rivers and snowy mountains to deserts and ruined buildings of the old world.

‚Ä¢ I had a smooth framerate during combat with machines and while exploring the world. The only significant problems I encountered were around a few bandit camps where my framerate dipped into the 40s, I‚Äôm assuming this was caused by columns of smoke because I didn‚Äôt see them anywhere else. I had some minor framerate drops in large settlements of NPCs, which wasn‚Äôt the end of the world because it didn‚Äôt affect any fast paced gameplay.

‚Ä¢ It took me 61 hours to complete the main quest, expansion, and lots of side quests. During this time I only crashed twice, so the game was very stable for me. Both crashes occurred before the release of patch 1.06 so it seems that whatever was causing the problem has been fixed.

‚Ä¢ Controls are fully rebindable and work great with mouse and keyboard.

‚Ä¢ The camera has a mind of its own, sometimes changing position by itself. By default, Aloy will be slightly offset to the left of screen, like most third person games. However, there are times when the camera drifts so that Aloy is almost all the way to the right of the screen, which feels slightly disorienting. Its not an issue that makes the game unplayable, because you can immediately reset the camera position by aiming the bow. This also means its not a problem during combat because you‚Äôll almost always be aiming. Its just a really strange design decision that doesn‚Äôt serve any purpose, and I can‚Äôt think of any other game I‚Äôve played in the last few years where I‚Äôve felt like I‚Äôm fighting the camera.

Recommendation

Horizon Zero Dawn is an amazing game and I rate it as an absolute must play for action game fans. Combat and story are both excellent and while there are some technical flaws, they aren‚Äôt big enough reasons to avoid playing. The amount of content makes this easily worth a full price purchase.

Let me say this first. I've been holding off on the purchase due to technical issues ppl have been reporting. After about a week I came to conclusion that from what I can see the negative reviews are of a technical nature so ... I decided to use my 2hrs refund option - if required.

Oh boy, let me say that. It was worth the risk. I had maybe 3 stutters in last 20 hours of play, but given, I'm not playing on a potato.

For comparison my specs:
CPU: Inter i5-9600K 3.7GHz
RAM: 16GB
GPU: RTX2070 (as pointed out by generals of internet and comments)

In the fist 2 hours of the game there is no chance in hell you will be able to stress test your computer. The first 5-10 minutes the game takes it sweet time to detect your graphical settings. Mine were set to MEDIUM. Hands down the slowest auto detection process I've seen in my life so far. Then you have slow introduction to the story and game mechanics. I definitely wasn't rushing but even if you do I doubt you get to the city where majority of users are experiencing issues (low fps etc).

What I'm trying to say, give this game a chance. If you are having problems in the first 2 hours then refund. If you are unsure refund. But you MUST set the timer for 1hr and 55 mins. I did that and did not realise how quickly these 2 hours passed. I would compare this game to Far Cry 3 which I enjoyed the most in the series. All the sneaking can get quite tedious but there are different ways you can play this game (various armour types + skills, makes this possible).

22 hours in and I discovered half of the map. I'm taking it easy and doing some side quests.

Oh, and I haven't seen any macro transactions in the game so that is also good.

To summarise it is an enjoyable experience that pulled me in. I can't stress how much I recommend the game. I would easily trade 100 titles from my library to play this.

DISCLAIMER: This 'Review' is only about performance settings/recommendations

If you haven't watched the Digital Foundry video on this game, I highly recommend doing so -

YouTube‚Ñ¢ Video: Horizon Zero Dawn PC: An Amazing Game Gets A Disappointing Port 
Views: 656,661
After a stunning debut in Death Stranding, the Decima Engine is back - this time with a port of Guerrilla Games' stunning Horizon Zero Dawn.


I've gone ahead and copy pasted their recommended/optimized settings for those that just want the TLDW:

Medium Textures
Ultra Model Quality
Driver Enforced 16x AF
High Shadows
Medium Reflections
High Clouds
TAA
Motion Blur On
Medium Ambient Occlusion
Dynamic Resolution OFF
V-SYNC OFF
Exclusive Fullscreen ON
They also recommend putting your PCIE to x16 in your bios ( This looks to be the first game to care about that )

**My personal recommendation: Use RTSS ( Rivatuner Statistic Server. It comes with MSI Afterburner ) to cap the FPS to 60 to stabilize frametimes. Don't use the in-game limiter. It sucks.

I do want to emphasize that the PS4 version uses the 'Original' preset AKA 'Medium'. The game already looked fantastic on PS4 so if all you care about is framerate
and don't want to mess with settings, that is the preset I'd use unless your PC is weaker than a PS4. I'd still turn off Dynamic Resolution though since it seems to suck.

And of course, download the latest drivers for your GPU.

With the above settings I get 83 avg FPS @ 1440p on the built-in benchmark. You can see full details in my screenshots.

Specs: 2700x, 16GB ram, 1080ti

Will update this 'review' if needed.

EDIT on 11/27/20: Nominating this for my GOTY in the Steam awards. Even though this released years ago on PS4, I feel it deserves it. I enjoyed it so much that I 100% it on both PS4 and PC.

Recommended
72.1 hrs on record
Posted: August 28, 2020
FIX FOR A LOT OF CRASHES!

Right click on Desktop -> Display Settings -> scroll at the bottom -> click on Graphics Settings -> Click the button to be ON at the 1st section called Hardware Accelerated Gpu Scheduling

This fixed all crashes for me and was experiencing one every 20 minutes at least.

Now the actual review:

The game is fantastic. Despite all the crashes I endured, I plowed through at least 1/3rd of the game and the feeling was "man if it only worked". With my fix, it works.

There are 3 main elements to talk about:

1. The visuals
This game looks amazing. A high end pc will probably make this game into a work of art, but I'm running it on an I7-4790 CPU, 16GB RAM and a GTX 1070. I run it on High, it does 60 FPS constantly with no problems:
DO NOT USE ADAPTIVE PERFORMANCE FPS! It's a BAD feature and it makes the game look worse than all low settings and run under 25 FPS. Look for a nice sweetspot, and it will look amazing.

2. The gameplay
This is the Atlas of this game, as it Carries it on it shoulders. The world is fantastic to explore. The hunting of machines is great, the bigger ones actually evolve over time and methods used to get kills start to not work so well. Walking the world.. just feels fun. You constantly interact with an everchanging world. What it does lack... is variety in it's main missions. But despite eventually seeing a pattern in design choices, it still doesn't matter that much. Why fix what isn't broken.

3. The story.
The story is fantastically hit and miss. Both of em. The main mistery of the game will keep you captivated, enthralled, fascinated by truly being a SCI-FI wonder, comparable to the first Mass Effect Game. In fact, with it's post apocalyptic plausible scenario, based on personal preference it might even be better. I won't spoil it, but the main quest is fantastic.
The miss comes the strong and powerful woman. Perhaps it's just 2020, the year and time where Strong and powerful bland pieces of wood are pushed to the forefront, but playing this game you can't help but notice it. The men in this game are either a**holes, incompetent, ignorant, soft, malicious, capricious, or just plain dumb. No. Exception. Which either sets them up as bad character archetypes or ... actually interesting flawed characters with pros and cons. The women however.... are Jesus. All of them. Without exception (in 47 hours of gameplay) all women have no flaws. They're all strong. They're all powerfull, and while always being presented as good at what they do, and you could deduce flaws by proxi - aka Oh she's a politician, so she might not be much of a fighter, for example - this is never outright said. Men on the other hand: here's a great warrior, who's also a drunken manchild. Or here's a wise rules who seeks piece, but he he's kind of incompetent and in absolute awe of his Strong And Powerful female bodyguard.

It's not AS bad as something like Captain Karen, but it is there. Whether intentional or not, weather the current political climate makes these flaws more apparent.. they are there. And once you see them, you can't unsee them. Case and point: Humanity is in a hunter gatherer phase. Ok so this tribe is a Matriarchy. Ok, women are lifegivers, so they are seen as leaders, hell even the game points out that this is not a criteria for leadership... but wait most hunters are women? The warchief is a woman? Her second in command happens to be a male who is incompetent and deuchy? Wait what?!

That kind of thing.

As a conclusion:
I cannot recommend this game enough. It's flaws are there. Are visible, but what it can deliver, it blows out of the water. It's a fantastic gameplay experience with a great overarching story, and at end of the day, a competently written cast of colorful men and bland women. (exception: Sobek. They give this charater one good moment of being flawed. I thing they should have doubled down on that moment, but that's me)

From an industry standpoint: Buy this game, find the fix that works for you and let's show the world that "exclusivity" is not the smart way to go.

Recommended
51.3 hrs on record
Posted: December 23, 2020
This is probably stuff that has been covered by everyone else, but I've been enjoying this game a lot overall and wanted to cover some of the good and bad aspects.

Performance/Technical

From a technical point of view, this is not the best PC port. I started playing this with an Intel 4790K and 5700XT and the experience was good overall on a 1440p high refresh monitor. but this is the first game I've played that has actually hit 100% CPU usage from time to time on that processor, which resulted in occasional minor stuttering.

I have since upgraded to a Ryzen 5600X and Geforce 3070 and I have not experienced any stuttering at all with a 12-thread CPU and am getting an average 80-100 fps at 1440p using the optimised settings recommended by Digital Foundry.

There are some animations such as leaves/foliage and certain cutscenes that run at 30fps, but I personally didn't find this particularly distracting.

In a nutshell, if you're using a modern PC with a CPU with 12+ threads and a fairly modern GPU (e.g. Radeon 5700XT or beyond) and you're playing at modest resolutions like 1440p or 1080p then you'll have a very good experience. On a CPU with 8 threads you'll find the experience to be overall mostly good, but if you're using an older i5 that doesn't have hyperthreading, I'm going to say the game probably won't run well.

I did originally purchase this game on PS4 and found it to not be very enjoyable at 30fps / 1080p on console, so I will say that this is definitely a big improvement overall on the PS4 experience in my opinion.

EDIT: additionally, I've noticed that when playing the game on an SDR monitor, it sometimes can be very dark, and sometimes very bright. I'm guessing this has something to do with the way that HDR is getting tonemapped down to SDR. I found that I ultimately had to turn the in-game brightness up at certain points and it was kind of annoying.

EDIT 2: After playing more I have experienced a couple of glitches which I consider to be very minor. Firstly, when hunting wildlife, occasionally when you make a kill the animal will spin really fast before dying. It's kind of funny and immersion breaking but not a big deal imo and happens infrequently.

Additionally, in the final mission some smoke/fog was much more opaque than it should have been for a brief segment, and in one instance when Aloy was in shadow the shadows blocked up to full black rather than shades of grey. Both of these glitches impacted only a very small segment of gameplay.

Also, the first time I booted up the game I had to wait for shaders to optimise which was kind of annoying, but this is only a one time thing.

I have not experienced any other major glitches or crashes myself but YMMV.

The game itself

I've been thoroughly enjoying my time playing this game. Generally speaking, I tend to play games in shortish (~1-2 hour) bursts and it can take me a few months to finish a game like this. Because of my limited gaming time, I only tend to finish games if they can really hold my attention over such a long period, which is quite infrequent.

With that in mind, I will say that so far I have been playing this game on and off for 2-3 months and am about 80% through the main story. The fact that the game has held my attention for this long and that I want to keep going back and playing more I think is credit to the quality of the game itself.

I do have some criticisms of the gameplay, mainly that the inventory system is quite convoluted and you have to collect certain arbitrary items to buy weapons, craft upgrades, etc. (e.g. to craft an ammo capacity upgrade might cost 500 metal shards, a boar bone and a fox tail) and you can only climb things if there are handholds which you have to go searching for.

The gameplay loop is also not exactly unique or groundbreaking, it is quite similar to other open world games such as Assassin's Creed, however the story, art style, and world building made this one of the more engaging open world games that I've played personally.

I did find Aloy kind of annoying at times. She sometimes acts like a petulant child, though I suppose it maybe makes sense that she's not well adjusted considering her upbringing... (I'm trying to justify this)

I know that there has also been some criticism of the game for appropriation of aspects of Native American culture -- I don't feel qualified to write about this at length, but wanted to mention it and would recommend reading into that from other writers.

EDIT 3: Some relevant articles include "What We Talk About, When We Don‚Äôt Talk About Natives" by Dia Lacina and "Horizon Zero Dawn DLC The Frozen Wilds Uncomfortably Borrows from Native Cultures" by Holly Green.

Overall

If you like story driven, scifi-ish open world games and you have a fairly modern PC, then you will most likely enjoy this game.

Recommended
103.3 hrs on record
Posted: September 2
Highly recommended for explorers who also enjoy a good story!

Beautiful and interesting world to explore. Characters are actually memorable - even ones that you only meet during small side quests. The stories and lore are intriguing and it's hard not to get emotionally invested when doing quests. The game has both made me shed a tear and laugh out loud. Combat is fun and varied - it's satisfying when you manage to take out a tough machine by utilizing the information you have about weakpoints and making use of your arsenal of different weapons and ammo. There are several different difficulties you can choose from and you can change it at any point (except in New Game +). If you want to just focus on the story and want combat to be easy then Story mode is great - for the most part you don't have to worry about hitting weakpoints on machines. You can take them down without. The higher the difficulty the more important it gets to be strategic about your attacks. I especially enjoyed the stealthy features of the game, but usually it's up to you how you handle each situation. I played through on story mode (since I expect to go for the Ultra Hard New Game + achievement, so nice to just focus on the story the first time around), so often taking the stealthy approach isn't technically needed - I just found it fun. :) But it's likely a much more needed strategy at times on higher difficulties - unless you enjoy being overrun and trampled by a herd of machines. :D

A thing I really love about the game is the mix of high action combat, stealth and more chill exploration. Even if there are many machines to take on, there are also plenty of areas in the world where you have room to just relax and enjoy the scenery. I love how well the character animations are done - not just on Aloy (the character you play), but also on all the different characters that you interact with. All dialogue is voice acted and the character animations actually follow what is said - both in speech and expressing emotions. When Aloy moves around in the world her animation changes depending on the terrain - whether she's sliding down a steep slope or hiking through deep snow and so on. It's just all very well made and all helps to increase the level of immersion while playing. Small details that all add up. :)

For achievement hunters it should be noted there's no "point of no return" - once you finish the main questline you'll load the last save before that quest and can then choose to finish up anything you might have missed or intentionally skipped. It will take 2 playthroughs to get all achievements though, since you can't access New Game + until you finish the game the first time. But the second playthrough should be much faster if you completed everything else the first time around. :)

Gorgeous scenery, intriguing story, fun combat, lots of collectibles and lore elements to find, great exploration including some parkour - what's not to like??? HZD is definitely in my Top 10 of favorite games.

Not Recommended

Posted: August 13, 2020
I am stupid. I read the reviews. I knew the truth. But I told myself, "I keep my gaming machine clean. I don't have the problems others often complain about with games. It'll run fine for me". Of course, it didn't. This isn't the worst game I've ever played, but it's definitely the worst PC port. You will spend more time trying to get it to run acceptably than you will playing it.

Forget about getting 60 FPS. You probably can't. I don't care what kind of system you have. This game is far too poorly optimized. But it doesn't matter anyway because framerate will be the least of your concerns. The CONSTANT studdering and "skipping" during gameplay and cutscenes would make the game unplayable even if the crashes, audio cutting out, and HDR not working properly didn't already do so.

Even if you manage to get 60 FPS, all you're really going to get is 60>studder>60>studder>60>studder>59>studder>60>studder.

It takes a LOT for me to leave a negative review for a game. But this is in no way enjoyable. After another night of alt-tabbing and switching from borderless to full screen and back again over and over just trying to get HDR to not look worse than SDR, for literally an hour, I stopped to type this review. I go to work early and come home late. I shouldn't be typing a review right now. I should be gaming.

There is absolutely zero chance that they didn't know this was absolutely awful, and they just released it anyway. They deserve all the bad reviews they get. This is the 2nd time I've paid Guerilla for this game (I really enjoyed it on PS4 Pro the first time), and I will never give them another dime. Not because the game isn't perfect, but because it's completely, absolutely, totally, obviously unenjoyable in its current state... and they took my money anyway. Never again. Not on PC; not on PS4; not on PS5.

EDIT: User logan5 informed me after writing this review that Guerilla Games did not handle this port internally. I did not know this (especially since their logo and SCIE's are the only logos which appear the splash screen), so maybe I shouldn't be so hard on Guerilla in particular. However, their name and logo is on this port. They (and Sony) had the final say on its release. So I still think much of the responsibility still falls on them-- they are where the "buck stops", so to speak.

Not Recommended
31.8 hrs on record
Posted: August 10, 2020
Edit 1 is up and you will find it below the dotted line, i am leaving the original up so people can see what was originally rated helpful.

I, personally, have not run into as many crashes or glitches as others have but i do have a few critiques to give other than the terrible port.

Cons:
1. The game needs a aim sensitivity slider ASAP, its not a big problem if you have a mouse that has an adjustable sensitivity button but for those that don't it makes aiming a chore.
2. The UI is obviously made for controllers and is frustrating to use with a keyboard and mouse. the mouse constantly goes to where you don't want it to if you use any navigation method other than it, and crafting is annoying when you are in your inventory.
3. when you are running around as Aloy it almost feels as if she moves independently from the mouse, which cause me to run into walls constantly and creates a feeling of suggestion rather than control. for me this also dampens the cinematic experience the game offers because i am forced to always be mindful that forward is not always forward.

Pros:
1. The visuals are stunning, and definitely benefit from 60fps and pc graphics
2. The story is spectacular, i found myself bonding with Aloy and caring for characters i had only just met, and scenes actually emotionally impacted me throughout.
3. Combat is dynamic and rewards you for experimenting with different play styles and tools. The skill tree is a nice accent to this already flushed out system
4. The world is not only vast, but also deep unlike most current open world games that have been released. i find myself searching through each area for collectibles and ruins to immerse myself deeper into this world
5. collectibles actually have meaning, either through providing backstory or rewarding the player.
6. Sidequests are fun and provide compelling dialogue most of the time, i have only run into one that i haven't liked.
7. The factions in the game are interesting and feel fully fleshed out, with each having their own specialties and reasons for why they developed in that way.

Thats all i have to say for now, for people like me who were lucky enough to not have run into a lot of bugs or poor performance the game is spectacular, but until the developers can guarantee that for everyone i am going to have to not recommend this game. i Will update my review in the future if i end up running into such issues or the developers fix them.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Edit 1: Hello all, thanks for liking my review! I have quite a few more hours in the game so i would like to provide more feedback along with clarify some of my points which seem to have confused some people. I would also like to add that in my reviews i do not include bugs since they either get patched out quickly or change too often, for this reason i will add a bug rating at the bottom of the pros and cons to give a rough idea.

Aim: Firstly, i would like to address aim sensitivity, as i have seemed to have confused some people with my wording. I know there is a general aim sensitivity slider in game and that it adjusts overall sensitivity. When i was talking about aim sensitivity i was referring to ADS, or Aim Down Sights sensitivity when aiming with the bow. Sorry for the confusion.

Movement: The second point of confusion was with Aloys movement, when i mentioned it felt more like suggestion than direction. To go more in depth with this idea i will try and describe it as best i can and leave you guys to judge. When moving as Aloy the camera is in a third person perspective and follows her around, using WASD you can move the player model around but the camera will not follow her movements precisely. sometimes Aloy will move closer to the center of the camera while other times she will move further away. This problem is only noticeable when traversing the map, since in combat ADS is locked to a certain spot over her shoulder.

Now, i would like to revise my pros and cons list to include what i have experienced in the extra play time i have gotten. New pros and cons will appear at the bottom of their respective lists and be identifiable with an indention along with the bottom paragraph being added to them since some people missed that, and some of them may also be edited to improve their wording

Cons:
1. (changed) The game needs an aim down sights sensitivity slider ASAP, its not a big problem if you have a mouse that has an adjustable sensitivity button but for those that don't it makes aiming a chore when using the bow. You can get used to it after a while, but the moment you play another game with your proper sensitivity you can feel the difference.
2. The UI is obviously made for controllers and is frustrating to use with a keyboard and mouse. the mouse constantly goes to where you don't want it to if you use any navigation method other than it, and crafting is annoying when you are in your inventory.
3. (changed) When you are running around as Aloy It feels like the camera and movement system are tied together by a rubber band. You have full control over the camera but Aloys position relative to it can vary, making you have to be constantly aware that forward is not always forward. This mostly happens during navigation and not combat.
-4. The game, as of now, has poor performance for most and is poorly optimized for pc. I have only crashed twice, both after leaving the game on for a long period of time, but if the
game cannot run properly for everyone with the proper equipment then that is a con in my
book.

Pros:
1. The visuals are stunning, and definitely benefit from 60fps and pc graphics.
2. The story is spectacular, i found myself bonding with Aloy and caring for characters i had only just met, along with scenes emotionally impacting me throughout.
3. (changed) Combat is dynamic and rewards you for experimenting with different play styles and tools. The skill tree is a nice accent to this already flushed out system along with the various arrow types you eventually gain.
4. The world is not only vast, but also deep unlike most current open world games that have been released. I find myself searching through each area for collectibles and ruins to immerse myself deeper into this world.
5. Collectibles actually have meaning, either through providing backstory or rewarding the player.
6. (changed) Sidequests are fun and provide compelling dialogue most of the time, i have only run into two that i haven't liked.
7. The factions in the game are interesting and feel fully fleshed out, with each having their own specialties and reasons for why they developed in that way.
-8. Its hard to word this, but the game never feels like you are in a play area. I never looked at a mountain and said "yup there is the border" because it never crossed my mind to think
of it that way. This feeling is helped by the various people you meet that bring back story to
almost every area, making locations feel like homes and towns instead of a checkpoints.

Bug rating: Likely to run into a few minor bugs, Examples of minor bugs: Glitched faces, skipped dialogue, brief broken terrain, etc.

Once again i will update this as i feel the need to. I really hope they fix the issues with the port so that everyone can have as much fun as i have with the game. I cannot stress enough that in its current state you are likely to run into game breaking problems even if some of us have not, BUYERS BEWARE.
