Recommended
226.4 hrs on record
Posted: November 16, 2021
THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS

This was a beautiful game. It's a game you could theoretically finish without much effort and time, but the world, the side characters, and the cultures played so deep a part in the story that I found myself sinking 200+ hours into it and not thinking twice. There is so much here in lore picked up in scraps and holograms hidden on your travels.

The thing that stuck out to me the most here was the relationships. Helping the people of the world was as important to the story as anything else, and it comes full circle . There are as many opportunities to show compassion and to be human as there are to kill things. It is such a human story that sets itself apart from your run-of-the-mill first-person shooter. It's exploration and mystery as much as it is combat. It's learning about people and cultures as much as it is learning about the machines, the world, and the secret of what Zero Dawn really is. This is not to distract from the story which was absolutely unique and incredible in how it unfolds, especially as you get closer to the heart of the truth.

The cultures Aloy interacts with throughout her travels are also shown in such a nuanced light. No one culture is shown to be bad or good, or "backwards" and the belief systems that each one possesses (which can cause tension) are shown to be what they are, all truths in some way, just seen from different angles or metaphysical alignments. Each one is well thought-out and sketched in intricate detail, whether it's the lumbering town of Pitchcliff nestled in the Northern mountains, or the sweeping mesa of Meridian, each place is important in some way.

I think this all ties into a larger point. The story itself felt so full of life, emotion, and meaning. Aloy finds and loses loved ones, makes and loses friends, makes enemies, explores the world, and finds herself swept up into a bigger purpose, but that purpose never grows so large that it leaves behind the reason that Aloy is fighting in the first place: People, and not just her own. Everyone. In the end, 

The combat was also engaging and skill-intensive. I played through the game on ultra-hard and it was such a challenge, but in a good way. Each machine is different, and figuring out how to handle each one was a game in and of itself.

I'm excited to see where they take the sequel. The post-credits scene made me excited to explore the world more, which is a tall order for someone who just spent 200+ hours doing just that.

Recommended
140.5 hrs on record
Posted: April 18, 2021
Horizon Zero Dawn is an amazing adventure game where prehistoric meets futuristic.

Visually stunning with a story rich settled on an open world, it's quite astonishing what Guerrilla reached with it considering that at the time they developed it they still were just a game studio with few games released.

Aloy is a very charismatic character and while the story develops you learn with her what happened with this land based by robotic animals, a script that pretty much could set a sci-fi movie.

Rather than spin a story about naive tribes battling the evils of encroaching technology, this game had the gut to weave a tale that encompasses complex themes. A mature storytelling that we don't always see, it addresses abandonment issues, ethnic cleansing and touch on things we usually face as a modern society.

As far as the gameplay goes, it's pleasant how fluid it is, the mechanics of the combat are intuitive and at the same time it gives a healthy challange in which we cannot always relay on just one weapon through the whole game.

During the game you realize that sometimes it's best to switch your fighting style between stealh and agressive, you need to figure out how to beat each machine's attack pattern, capabilities and weaknesses to get a successful outcome without failing in the process or even dying. Extremely rewarding but progressivly tougher the longer you get into the storyline which in itself is very driven.

The game offers us a large amount of side-missions, collectibles and challenges around the world to complete, if you are a completionist get ready to a deep run that will consume your time for several hours.

To wrap it up, very recommended. An exciting journey from the very start that leaves us with lots of interesting questions all while the development of Aloy as a person happens, what it means for her future trying to uncover the truths about this strange world.
When most of them are finally answered there's yet much to come.

Worth mention that it came very chaotic to PC but nowadays it runs great, a good addition to your library if you like adventure games.

Recommended
56.8 hrs on record
Posted: September 10, 2020
I bought this game on PS4 originally when it came out, and had a great time playing it. Since then, Sony has shifted focus to putting their original exclusive titles on PC after launch.

This game in particular has had a bumpy start with hardware compatibility issues, however it's worth noting that they have patched 4 times already since launch, and the game is more stable and better performing each time.

On my particular hardware setup, the game runs very smoothly. I have a relatively high end PC (9900k, 2070 S) but my friend who uses this game from my library (Yay steam sharing on this game!) has a lower end but very common PC (Some I7, GTX 1660) and it also runs great on his machine post updates! So for anyone who was worrying if the hardware was in the way, I think it's very safe to say most rigs now should be able to run without crashing or severe performance issues!

And outside of hardware, the game is a gem for the start of a series. It definitely has it's own issues, cheese dialogue, weird hand made facial animations (no mocap for realism) kind of gives it an uncanny valley feeling. These were just some of the issues with this being an original title and the developers only having so much time and budget.

But the gameplay is fantastic, killing and hunting giant robots is a blast regardless. They keep getting stronger, but so do you. And the main story is an interesting engagement with the idea of radicalized corporatism, letting companies and their technologies evolve to a point of no return. That idea isn't new on its own; however the way it's explored in Horizon: Zero Dawn is entirely unique. Worth a shot at any price, for open world lovers looking for a cool series to get involved in.

Happy hunting.

Looking forward to the release of Horizon Forbidden West on steam store :)

Recommended
75.5 hrs on record
Posted: August 21, 2020
UPDATE (08-12-2020)

This game is one of the best action RPG's to date. I've finished the game on PS4. It has great graphics, very cool story and the setting is very creative and memorable.

At release the game was plagued with technical issues like Stutters, frame pacing problems, Crashes. At that time I could not give the game a positive review. Today patch 1.09 arrived and the game plays a lot better.

I'm now able to play this game at 4k Ultra on a 3090 on a C9 Oled. The game runs beautifully and has steady framerate between 70 and 90 fps.

If you like a story driven adventure with light RPG elements and action oriented gameplay than this is the game for you. Don't expect any deep RPG mechanics. You have a skill tree and in the end you will have all skills unlocked. There is a variety in armors and weapons. The main story is great and memorable. You'll finish it within 25 hours.

ORIGINAL REVIEW (RELEASE)

Let me say that this is one of the best action RPG's to date. I've finished the game on PS4. It has great graphics, very cool story and the setting is very creative and memorable.

That being said; I unfortunately can't recommend the game in its current state for PC. The game is plagued with stutters, frame drops, bad frame pacing and a very rough playing experience.

I'm playing on high-end hardware (2080ti, 9900k, LG C9 TV) on 4k with g-sync enabled and still experience very bad stutters. I've adjusted the image quality settings to recommended settings and even lowered the resolution to 1440p. I've also made sure the pci-e bandwidth is 20 Gbps.

In my experience this is a great game, but has a very bad port. I know the devs are working to get things fixed. But right now it leaves a bad taste in my mouth. The game should not have been released in it's current state.

Wait a couple of months and check back if the game is fixed. Time will tell...

Recommended
18.6 hrs on record
Posted: December 17, 2021
If you've ever wanted to blow up giant robot dinosaur things with primitive weaponry, this is probably the game for you.

Simply an amazing game. The storyline is intriguing enough to make you want to follow it, and the world itself is full enough that aimlessly wandering through it is fun and often satisfying in its own rite. The variety of weapons allows you to cater much of the game to your play style, whether you prefer to sneak and snipe, run in with guns (or, I guess, arrows) blazing, or use traps to ambush your enemies (although you'll probably do all that and more).

The variety of enemies is pretty great. There are several human bandit types that you'll need to kill, but for the most part you'll be fighting various machines, mostly designed with inspiration from the animal kingdom. Each 'species' behaves in its own way, which can lead the way to some really creative combat styles, making the journey both challenging and fun.

Otherwise, the game on a whole is beautifully designed. The landscapes, people, and machines are all fantastically rendered. It's not a difficult thing to get lost wandering the land, whether you're en route to a mission, scouring for resources, or hunting down machines ...or rabbits. The variety of landscapes is pretty unrealistic, as your character can walk from a jungle area to a forest and then an icy tundra in a matter of minutes, but that variety keeps the settings from growing repetitive, and at least for myself, helps to give a sense of where in this world I'm wandering without needing to keep going back and forth to the map.

The story is pretty good (so far), and provides a pretty good set up to explain why humans are living in this sort of primitive world surrounded by deadly technology.

( ' ‚Ä¢ o ‚Ä¢')

2 people found this review funny 12

Recommended
46.6 hrs on record
Posted: January 2
Horizon Zero Dawn is, for the most part, a solid, middle-of-the-road, generic open-world action-adventure game. It is perfectly competent in basically all areas, but doesn't really do much to innovate or stand out from the extremely crowded, extremely saturated field of generic open-world action-adventure games. Thankfully, it is saved by its one actual innovation: fighting giant robot animals using bows.

HZD does an excellent job of making the robots feel threatening and dangerous at every stage of the game, no matter how high your level or how powerful your equipment, while still making them feel like surmountable challenges that can be overcome with tactics and cunning. Obviously, blindly firing arrows at robots will do next to nothing, even with the best bows in the game, and you will find yourself getting smacked around like a giant cat toy. First, you will need to scan a new robot type while staying hidden to learn where all their weak points are, whether it be optic cameras, batteries or fuel canisters. Often, these parts will be protected by armour plating, which you will have to first remove by shooting them with armour-stripping arrows. Then, you will need to shoot at the exposed area to deal critical damage to the robot. If you use the correct ammo type, such as flaming arrows for fuel canisters or electrified arrows for batteries, you can cause elemental explosions which will damage all nearby robots, which will be useful if you are hunting multiple robots at once. If you are able to ambush a robot, you might be able to set up tripwires ahead of time to damage or stun robots. If a robot is too mobile to deal with, you can use harpoon ropes to anchor them to the spot. In all scenarios, there is always an element of strategy and finesse when hunting robots, and you never feel like you're trivialising the game with sheer firepower. Every encounter with a robot, even when doing mundane things like farming components for weapon upgrades, feels fun and exciting.

If there's one thing to criticise about the bow combat system, it's the lack of evolution in weapons as the game progresses. Very early on in the game, you gain the ability to craft the starter form of every ranged weapon in the game: three different types of bow, crossbow, slingshot etc. At that point, you basically have every combat option you will get in the game. You can get upgraded bows which deal more damage and can use more elemental arrows, but 90% of using elemental arrows is just "shoot arrow type A at weakpoint type A," so your experience in using these weapons basically remains unchanged for the entire game. This is alleviated somewhat in the DLC story, which allows you to unlock 4 new weapon types that function completely differently than your other weapons, but the DLC is targeted at a pretty high level, so you will still go through most of the game with the same few weapons.

As for why there are highly advanced robot animals in a post-apocalyptic world of primitive humans in the first place, HZD does a surprisingly excellent job with its plot and worldbuilding. The story of HZD is well-written and well-paced, first starting small with the protagonist Aloy wondering about her mysterious origins and trying to save her tribe, then gradually expanding to learning about the origins of the current state of the world they live in and trying to save the entire world. The game could have very easily shrugged its shoulders and said "we're giving you freaking ROBOT DINOSAURS with freaking LASER BEAMS on their heads, are you really going to question where they came from" and most people would have been perfectly understanding, but instead they chose to craft a rich, believable setting in which to populate all manner of mechanical beasts.

However, while the plot of the game is consistently good throughout, the same cannot be said for the character writing. Thankfully, the important characters are all done well: father figure is fatherly, mysterious ally is mysterious, antagonist is a constant insufferable ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•, and Aloy herself is a sympathetic protagonist. However, almost every other NPC in the game is a flat cardboard sign meant to point you towards your next objective and disappear forever. This is the kind of game story that you will find more fun diving into in a fan wiki than actually playing reading about in game.

Unfortunately, that is where the accolades for this game end. Everything else in HZD is painfully generic open-world filler content. You got your three fighting styles of ranged, melee and stealth, where melee and stealth are painfully underbaked compared to the game's bow combat. You got your bandit camps scattered around the map to liberate, populated entirely by human enemies, which are so much more boring to fight compared to robot sabertooth tigers. You got your Uncharted-style traversal system, where you can only climb on special yellow-coloured rocks and ledges and it's really just a glorified linear path, which feels so dated and restricted now that we've experienced BotW's freeform stamina-based climbing system. You even have grinding random forest critters to farm drops to craft new weapons, which feels so extremely lame and out-of-place when compared to hunting down a giant robot crocodile to extract a machine core. It feels like a lot of these were added to the game because they couldn't think of anything better to pad the game out with and they decided to go with what everyone else is doing, instead of truly making design decisions to support a truly wonderful core gameplay hook of hunting bus-sized killer machines with caveman tools.

Overall, Horizon Zero Dawn is a good game. I don't want my criticisms of it to detract from that fact. However, it is certainly not the second coming of Jesus that the hype surrounding the game would have you believe. Everything that makes this game unique is a truly shining experience, but unfortunately everything else is painfully generic and fails to help the good stuff reach its full potential.
 

AKTKWNG
73 products in account
3
44 people found this review helpful 4

Recommended
137.0 hrs on record
Posted: August 6
In Short
Great choice for every RPG fan. Memorable game. Worth the original price. If you find it on sale, don't delay and enjoy the ride!

Positives
+ EXCELLENT post-apocalyptic world. Mix of prehistoric age and sci-fi. Diverse beautiful biomes ranging from deserts to snowy mountains with many breathtaking views. There are several human tribes which are well established and have a fair share of history with each other. These tribes struggle to survive in a world filled with machines. The thing that impressed me the most is the connection to the old world (before the apocalypse). It's not there just as a filler. It plays an important role in the story and gives many good reasons for how the world developed. I struggle to remember any other game, or even movie/TV show, where I would appreciate flashbacks as much as here. The world-building is definitely strong with this one and it even manages to carry other parts of the game.

+ Good story. It starts slow with more focus on prehistoric aspect, Aloy (main character) and her tribe. Later it shifts to sci-fi and focus is on the past, present and future of the world and Aloy's place/part in it. Aloy is an outcast fighting against all odds and trying to find out about her family past. It's cheesy sometimes. It feels like a generic story you have seen a few times before. However, later you discover how she fits the overall story of the world and it gets very interesting. The second half of the game where many secrets, twists and connections are revealed/explained is AMAZING.

+ The map size is just about right. No vast empty spaces or spaces filled with meaningless sh*t. Imagine AC game level of icons and halve the amount. IMO developers hit the sweet spot with amount of collectibles and side content. Good middle ground between story driven and open world design.

+ I loved the combat and TBH it raises my expectations of combat systems going forward. There is some stealth and melee combat, with fast/strong attack, stealth executions, hiding spots and whistle - but it has a minor role. This is mainly ranged game done right. Most of the time, you fight machines aka 'robotic dinos'. There are about 30 well-designed types of machines (get hyped for likes of Onyx, Zapdos, T-rex, etc.) with various strengths, weaknesses, weak spots, attacks and abilities. Your knowledge about them is key (yes, read the damn 'bestiary'). Combat is always fresh because you fight something ACTUALLY different all the time. In order to fight these various enemies, Aloy acquires about 12 or so different weapon types throughout the game (with different ammo types). Emphasize on different. You NEED to analyze the situation and use correct combination of tools for different enemies. You will feel the pushback if you play sloppy.

Machines can ACTUALLY be dealt with in different ways because of its components and your weapons/tools. And I mean it, you won't cruise through the game with just one bow type. I used regularly all three types of bow and 4 other weapons (two types of slings, tripcaster for traps and ropecaster). And these have different ammo types (usually 3) and yes, you switch between them all the time too. Moreover, there is other fancy and more weird stuff like flamethrower, lightning gun, ice gun etc. if that is your thing. This is very different from Witcher or AC games where you can spec one (best) way and beat it all, repeating the same sh*t over and over without any motivation to ever change anything.

Overall, you need to exploit weaknesses and minimize strengths of the enemy. Preparation is important. No headless running in and smashing keyboard. No infinite health bars of generic enemies. You will get destroyed. The game is hard to learn, but also rewarding. It makes you think and use different tools in your arsenal. You will feel good when you see your progress and efficiency fighting each type of enemy improve over time. Enemies also become improved after some kill count, which is nice detail.

Min-maxing in the game is limited. You can't really 'outgear' the game difficulty. There are stat limits. You can optimize, but in the end, it will be about your decisions and actions. I would suggest to start on very hard (UH wasn't even in the game at release) and switch to ultra hard later (there are some functional changes in addition to number increases).

After 130h in HZD I decided to go back to AC:Odyssey where I had 240h already. A game which I had mathematically beaten because my gear is so min-maxed beyond the difficulty curve it's not even funny. I can spam left click and use 2 abilities over and over to beat ANYTHING in the game. Close to no pushback. Just mindless gameplay. Same 3 to 8 not so different enemy types. No motivation to change playstyle or even weapons I use. It was a stark contrast to HZD. I just laughed in despair.

+ Great DLC (Frozen Wilds). Definitely worth it. Beautiful snowy region (even better than the base game), great new weapons, decent story for a DLC, great side quests and interesting characters. Good (read as challenging) new enemy types.

Negatives
- On PC you will see issues with AA and grass. Game has lots of flora and it makes TAA choke. If you have DLSS, just enable it and enjoy. Otherwise, accept that you will see shimmering. Don't use FSR 1.0 (even more shimmering) - the performance increase is big, but your eyes will bleed out.

- Some areas feel out-dated: facial animations (the usual), water surfaces and climbing system.

- The inventory management is kinda ass. You can upgrade up to 120 capacity, but it's not a safe amount by any means and there is no stash (which would fix the issue). In my experience, even after going through reddit and guides, I was constantly at 100 to 110 load leaving only small space left for new items. The game has a crafting system with materials and lots of "trophies" from enemies you collect, basically you should keep a lot of stuff. Then there is stuff you can sell, no problem. Being a responsible and organized person myself, I still had issues with clearing the inventory and being comfortable.

- No transmog. It's not such a loss, but still.

- There are two main villains (generally speaking). One is very interesting, the other is... let's say under-developed.

Nitpicking
- Aloy is not a Mary Sue character. She is not perfect and makes mistakes. No worries there. She is however, presented as 'the chosen one' archetype (there is even story explanation for it). Just a warning if that's not your thing.
- As mentioned, melee combat and stealth plays only small part. It's not an issue as the ranged combat is excellent, but be aware.
- There are 3 options in dialogues (heart, brain, fist) which is basically good/neutral/evil Aloy response. I don't really like this approach because of AC:Odyssey. Luckily, these choices are occasional in HZD and you don't have to choose every 5 seconds. In case you think these choices have impact on story - they don't. This game doesn't have multiple endings.
- Controversy alert. The final battle at the end is nothing to write home about. Everything leading up to the end is AMAZING, and then you get the final battle in the one place of the whole game where the age of the game is showing and you get two mediocre/straightforward boss fights. OTOH you can have companions you helped throughout the game assist you in the battle (similar to Witcher 3) and Aloy has hilarious sassy callback line in the first boss fight. And of course, nice emotional ending cinematic to save it. I'm torn on this.
- There is override and mount feature (riding machines, yay!) and it's useless because you get everywhere by foot, no problem (vast network of travel points too). But hey, more options for the player, thumbs up.
- Combat with human enemies is basically reduced to stealth executions or headshots. But who cares. The game is about fighting machines.
 

Vasa

Recommended
44.8 hrs on record
Posted: September 2, 2020
Earth is ours no more

2020 has been quite a year for video-games, we got a new Half-Life entry, a Persona game launched on PC since 1996 and we got the announcement of a Sony‚Äôs 1st Party flagship coming to PC, Horizon Zero Dawn. Truth be told, it‚Äôs not the first Sony exclusive game to come to Steam, we also got the Quantic Dream games and recently Death Stranding but none published by themselves, now Horizon is a completely different case, it‚Äôs their first published game on Steam and who knows, maybe the first of many, anyway, the day has come and it‚Äôs time to review this adventure, so let‚Äôs find out if it‚Äôs worthy, shall we?

Horizon Zero Dawn takes place in a distant future in which civilization has returned to the tribal era, the world has returned to a natural state and it‚Äôs populated by mechanical beasts, the machines. We play as Aloy, an outcast girl who wants to discover who‚Äôs her mother and why she is an outcast, her quest for the truth will lead Aloy into something much bigger that involves what happened to the world in the past and what‚Äôs happening between the tribes in the present. What happened to our world? That‚Äôs something we will find out.

The story is really interesting, it gives you two perspectives, the first one is the present tribal time in which we will see how the society works in such conditions. Religious vision, political movements, social behaviours, all those elements will be present all the way until the end of our adventure.
The Second perspective is the past, what happened to the world, why there are cities in ruins, why there are machines ruling the lands and not only big things but also we will see little fragments of the daily life of that society via documents, holograms and audio logs, don‚Äôt miss them, some are really good and there‚Äôs a lot of background content in this optional files.

As the story is divided in two main arcs with their own mission timeline and both can be merged due to the freedom of choice when it comes to choose what mission you want to do I think I should give an advice about how I think it‚Äôs the best way of experimenting the story, the first arc you should do is the one that it‚Äôs about the present () until the end of it and then go all-in to the arc that it‚Äôs about the past () as this will lead to the end and by how it is structured in terms of dialogues and choices, I think this makes more sense, the frozen wilds should be experimented after the main story for the same reason, dialogues and references make more sense.

Game has a lot of side-quests, they provide a good chunk of exposition about more details of the present and there are some worthy characters that will be found in this side-activities (hunting grounds, infected zones, etc), make no mistake, not everything is worth it and the map is full of marks, while it‚Äôs not difficult to complete the side objectives, it is time consuming and maybe it‚Äôs not something you want to do, if you want to focus on the important ones, follow the green exclamation marks once you discover them, there are side-stories that are really interesting.

Side-activities will unlock more points to get more abilities and get better parts to get better gear, it‚Äôs not something mandatory but I think it‚Äôs enjoyable thanks to the gameplay.

Speaking of gameplay, there‚Äôs a lot to discuss here, let‚Äôs see, base gameplay is what you would expect from a third person action/adventure game, everything is as standard as you can imagine, however, it works really well, climbing is guided but very fluid,combat is functional, etc... however the only playable system that feels strange compared to other similar games is riding the machines, it feels clunky and I guess they wanted to make it feel heavy because, well, you are riding a mechanical horse and not an organic animal but I don‚Äôt think it makes you feel that but that it‚Äôs a non-functional riding.

Now returning to the combat there‚Äôs this thing that makes it something stunning, machine hunting. Combat against humans is the standard, melee and distance attacks, however their actions make them predictable so it‚Äôs easy to win their encounters, machines tho, while predictable they offer a much higher challenge in combat and it‚Äôs spectacular and a big part of what makes this game something unique, if there‚Äôs titanic beings combat in it, there‚Äôs already something special.

Thunderjaw‚Äôs first combat is something remarkable.

There‚Äôs no better way than that combat to introduce the graphics as yes, both the Thunderjaw and Horizon Zero Dawn are juggernauts, but a different kind of juggernaut, one is an alpha predator in the game and the other is top tier in terms of visual quality.

HZD is probably one of the best looking games out there, a general look of the valley, the snowy mountains or the warm desert will make you say ‚Äúwoah‚Äù every single time you discover a new location, the lightning, the weather system, the forests and jungles and the ruins, everything looks absolutely fantastic, let‚Äôs keep in mind that this game came out in 2017, the fact that this can compete visually against more modern titles tells a lot in favor of this game, and not only in terms of world building but also in terms of character design, which is absolutely fantastic, aside of some weird animations from time to time when it‚Äôs time to talk, but overall it‚Äôs impossible to say this is not a good looking game and if you find it as one of the most beautiful games you have seen, well, I can feel you.

Even the little details are present, sure, it‚Äôs not a world as reactive as we are used to see nowadays but 3 years can make a huge difference.
Make no mistake, there are rough textures, some weird invisible walls and a few other little things that will be there but overall, I don‚Äôt think you will notice.

What I‚Äôm sure you will notice is the sound design too because it‚Äôs really great and the most impressive part of it is the machine sounds, so industrial, so metallic, I love it. Human voices are also really great and well integrated.

OST is really good, there are two or three themes that will stick with you for a long time, I‚Äôm sure.

And now that I have more or less expressed my opinion about the general aspects of the game, I think it‚Äôs important to jump into the PC specifics, aka, the PC port.

Horizon Zero Dawn launched in a very mixed state, while I had a really great experience in my system with no crashes or technical problems present during my adventure, I know I‚Äôm the exception and not the rule, in general a lot of people have been experiencing technical problems like stuttering or crashes and it‚Äôs something that must be acknowledged, even if you look for specific configurations performance there‚Äôs no warranty that it will run at the same quality as your installed programs might be interacting with the game too or some driver is different, I will say it pretty clear, while my experience was perfect I can‚Äôt assure you that you will have my same luck.

However looking at the bright side, Guerrilla is doing a really great job communicating with users and fixing with patches all the problems they find, it‚Äôs Sony‚Äôs first game on PC so I will give you the benefit of the doubt and give them time to learn, at the very least, they have been quite active for the fixing and the communication, so that‚Äôs something great.

And that‚Äôs pretty much it, my final thoughts is that this is an amazing game that will give you a lot of hours to explore and a really interesting story to follow, the machines are an absolutely main reason to get into this game. It still feels kind of surreal that we are able to play this on Steam but industry has changed a lot lately so anything is possible, I guess.

I just can say that I absolutely recommend this game and I surely hope you enjoy it as much as I did.

Posted: March 14
TL;DR:
I've finished this game already on my PS4 (both base game and DLC), and i've enjoyed it very much. It has its flaws, but still a solid game, with its own stunning world, lore and everything.


Longer version:
Just finished Forbidden West (sequel), which was great, and thanks to that, I just wanted to replay the first game again, so I bought it (again, i own the original on PS4) on PC, for two reasons - first, to support PlayStation games on Steam, so we would get more of them in the future, and second, was interested in how the game looks on PC, how is it to play it with keyboard. And I am not disappointed. I still prefer gamepad (PS4 dualshock connected to PC), but playing it with keyboard was also fine. I can imagine PC players will be satisfied, but I switched it from keyboard/mouse to PS4 controller, as it's connected to my PC anyway, and I am just used to it now. Many things are more natural for me, as I was recently playing sequel, and the controls are basically the same. Also, I love additional vibrations as a feedback, which is kinda missing with keyboard :) But that's just me, my aim is now quite perfect with controller, but there were times that I wasn't so confident and preferred keyboard :) And as I said, the game is just fine with keyboard.

Main story is great, nothing completely groundbreaking, but all the stories and the whole world around it, it is just amazing :) I loved the idea since first trailer, I was confident enough to pre-order the collector's edition, and it was great. It is still great. I definitely recommend this game to anybody. Many ways to customize your experience, to tweak the settings, many difficulty settings, so you can either just enjoy the story, or just have the biggest challenge ever. This version comes with the DLC, which is nice added bonus, but for me the DLC wasn't that good. But can still satisfy the need for more gameplay, more robo-monsters and everything, as it has it's own story, which is continuation of Aloy's quest (kinda) :)

Fights are the main part of this game, and it shows. Most of the enemies are those robo-monsters. There are various versions of them, every monster is different and requires different approach. It's just fun to discover what works against them and what's the best weapon for them. Many outfits and weapons will help you on your way. Interesting side quests, many characters (friendly or not) with their personalities, lot of secrets to find about the world, which may not be for everybody, but if you enjoy that kind of stuff, then it's there :)

Soundtrack is beautiful, fits the story and the world perfectly, and as a soundtrack/music lover, I was really satisfied :) Voice acting is great, but as I said, unfortunately animations could be better, which might ruin some moments.

Really looking for some flaws/cons, but there aren't that many. Probably just as I said earlier, if you played the sequel, then this game is just downgraded version of it. And graphics + animations and face expressions are just worse than in the sequel, but you will probably notice that even without playing sequel. Other than that, minor glitches can occurr here and there. And be careful, once you fall in love with the world, you may end up buying PlayStation 5 just to play the Forbidden West :)

Posted: May 12
I played Horizon Zero Dawn at a point where the many other open world games I've played (BotW, Witcher III, etc.) are a little more faded in my memory. In that space I certainly enjoyed this game, but I also simultaneously don't have much more interest in the sequel, or even finishing out the DLC. It's good fun for it's playtime, but the characters are boring and don't live up to the absolutely bonkers premise. Similarly, as someone who tends to side quest to the ends of the earth, I spent most of the game overpowered for most missions. So, if you're looking for the best of the best, I'd look elsewhere, but if you want something fun for 50 hours or so, go for it.

Posted: August 8, 2020
Editing this review, as promised:

Willing to give this a positive review now. I think performance still perhaps isn't what it should be for the port, and I have experienced 2 crashes since coming back to it after the Feb. patch, but for the most part the game is playable now.

And it is a pretty great game. To be honest I don't think it is quite the masterpiece some people make it out to be, but making open world games like this with an engaging story is incredibly difficult, and H:ZD is very distinctive, plus for the most part does what it sets out to do very well.

I'm giving all the credit for the game's now playable state to the original devs, Guerrilla. As far as I can tell, seems like they have done all the heavy lifting for fixing the port that the porting company neglected with QA. Blame for the sorry state the game was in at release falls more on Sony and the hired porting company, Virtuous.

(Yes I am aware that Guerrilla is a Sony owned studio. I don't think it's too much of a stretch though to assume that the deal/contracting for the port happened at the executive level with Sony. I doubt that the actually people who dev'd had much say or even work toward the port before release, especially since they have their own future games in development and were not being explicitly paid to do the port)

I still hope Sony learns from the experience though and ports Bloodbourne.

66.3 hrs on record
Posted: October 16, 2020
Spoiler free review, with a short and a longer version:

Buy this game if:

+ You're interested in open world games, where the main missions are the core of the gameplay and narrative rather rather than its secondary side quests;
+ you want to live in a post apocalyptic, "witcher-esque" gameplay
+ You have a good gaming pc;
+ You're interested in a challenge and you can bear some resource hunting;

Don't buy the game if those above points won't hold for you;

Verdict: 8 not including the PC port part in my rating but including the DLC: Frozen Wilds // 6,5 otherwise

Time required to finish the main game: 20/25 hours
Time required to complete it at 100%: around 65 hours (depending on luck, game performance and patience)

Longer version:
Let's see now the most important points, including the DLC, described in the end:

1) THE PC PORT: everyone had his own unique experience with it, personally with a i7-8700 CPU,16GB of RAM and a NVIDIA GEFORCE 960, i had to put all the settings on low, having as a result 45 stable FPS outside and stable 60 on closed areas and bunkers. Never had game breaking bugs or glitches, except when skipping through dialogues, weirdly enough. This was my experience, i'm not a tech expert so take it as it is.

2) SIGNIFICANT IMPACT OF THE DIFFICULTY SETTINGS and overall good progressing:


HZD 1 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Flipper Is A Dolphin


The game progression is stable and you'll rarely feel out of place or underleveled at the normal difficulty settings, raising up the difficulty bar though could be a good call, as the enemies' pattern and behaviour will change and widen a lot, really making you feel the vibe that a huntress should have during a deadly combat and really pushing the scavenging and machine hunting;

3) GOOD GAMEPLAY AND NARRATIVE during the main quests:


HZD3 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Flipper Is A Dolphin


The main quests are always important and fun, forcing you to explore a vast and thriving world, witnessing the changing inside Aloy- the main character- outside her and her tribe. Sadly the secondary missions, except a few ones don't offer that much in terms of being memorable and original, as the narrative during these quests is mostly carried through 1 to 1 conversations where the camera shifts abruptly from one talker to the other, lessing the narrative immersion and depth.

4) THE FROZEN WILDS DLC IS A MASTERPIECE:


HZD2 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Flipper Is A Dolphin


The DLC is extremely good as:
1- changes the way the narrative progresses;
2- the side characters you'll meet are unique and remarkable;
3- the new added enemies are a good challenge and they're tough to be dealt with (and fun!)
4- adds several weapons and upgrades which help diversifying the combat and the overall experience
5- introduces a new entire skill tree
6- the main story of the DLC is deep and well intertwined with the story and the dialogues in the end part of the base game;

5) THE COMBAT GAMEPLAY IS EXCELLENT AND FLUID:
even with my not optimal perfomance described above, fighting machines always feels fresh and compelling, as trying different strategies and approaches will always grant you good gameplay diversity and different loot from time to time, allowing also Aloy to improve her inventory and ammo capacity

Thanks for reading and for bearing up with me, leave a comment below if you have any questions or observations, have an amazing day/night, feel free to follow my other reviews at: https://store.steampowered.com/curator/32344423/

Recommended
89.5 hrs on record
Posted: July 5, 2021
To be honest, Horizon: Zero Dawn (HZD) was nowhere as good as the people were saying, and if I‚Äôm to count hits and misses, it missed a lot more marks than it hit. So why the thumbs up then? It‚Äôs simple, really, because where it hit, it absolutely nailed it!


Pros:
Combat has to be the best in any open world (OW) game I‚Äôve ever played
Graphics are breathtaking
Story was alright

Cons:
No exploration whatsoever. Just follow the map/compass icons
Upgrades, trading, and some crafting rely on randomized loot
Voices are compressed, and it‚Äôs pretty obvious
Side quests are all pretty generic chores and offer no unique rewards
Mounts are terrible
Some bugs here and there


A wonderful world with absolutely nothing to find in it
The first disappointment that became evident very early on, was the absolute lack of exploration. Considering that HZD is an OW game, I was hoping for at least some sense of adventure and player-driven exploration. It has none of that. You will never stumble upon something that wasn‚Äôt already marked on the map and has to be found by exploration or deduction. I did all of the side-quests and collected every single collectible, simply by going from one map-marker to another.

The world of Horizon: Zero Dawn is full of breathtaking vistas 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: ge√∏stigma

It means that there are no hidden items that you can find by exploring the world or following some sort of clue.
This is a huge missed opportunity as the world of HZD is beautiful. These are some of the best graphics that I‚Äôve seen in a video game, and I‚Äôve got screenshots to back that claim. Making the game a bit more about exploration, removing the lazy quest/item markers from the map, and replacing them with landmarks would encourage the player to look around and get absorbed in the wonderful world of HZD.

Oh and for the love of God, rework your mount controls, Guerilla. They‚Äôre atrocious! Whoever thought that it‚Äôs a good idea to do them this way made a terrible decision.


Random loot based progression with awful inventory system
Considering the amount of available gear, the randomized upgrade system is worse than it would normally be, as you‚Äôll need to get upgrades for multiple gear pieces. These items are something that you can have in your inventory at all times. Simply open it up and switch your loadout at any given time ‚Äì even during combat! This is why I‚Äôm confused why the devs didn‚Äôt think of some convenient way to swap between different loadouts on the fly. In fact, the entire UI is full of missed opportunities.

For example, why force us to go through a tubular inventory when picking items when there is a weapon wheel already in the game? Why not allow us to sort the items in the inventory, and include filters and search criteria in a game with 120 items in a single item category? Why couldn‚Äôt we get a comparison of the currently equipped item/upgrade versus the one that we‚Äôre highlighting? Why split equipping and modifying items into two separate inventory categories instead of just making a separate key for equipping and another one for modification of the selected item? These decisions make no sense, and it feels like the game was rushed.


Other than for the story fillers, side-quests are hardly worth your time
All of the side-quests are uninspiring. They come down to going from point A to point B and defeating the enemies that you find there. Sometimes you have to use your Focus gadget to follow the tracks or examine the surroundings for clues, but ultimately, they‚Äôre all the same in form.

To make matters worse, the only reward you will get from pretty much all of these quests (except one if I remember correctly) is a bit of XP and a loot-box containing random items that you can get or buy elsewhere.

The only thing that‚Äôs somewhat good about them is the extra lore that they all provide. We get to learn more about the world, factions, and machines through these quest stories so, if that‚Äôs something you care about, you might actually like them.

Combat is just fantastic
This single-handedly makes HZD a game worth picking up and playing through, and thankfully there's tons of it. It‚Äôs so good that I found it hard to let the game go until I‚Äôve beaten it, and then started and finished another playthrough.

I‚Äôm sure you‚Äôve seen footage of large, robotic beasts and how Aloy uses her bow to hunt and defeat them. They come in different shapes and sizes, from horses and rams that you can mount to a freaking raptors and basically T-Rex! While all of them are machines, they all require different approach to combat/hunt. The more you play and the more unique enemies you encounter, the better hunter you‚Äôll become.

From prey to apex predator. Aloy has a tool for every situation 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: ge√∏stigma

First off, there are numerous types of damage in this game. For example, Tear will deal less damage but will rip off parts of the machine more easily, like armor plating or its weapons. Once you do that, you can use its own weapon to hit it where it hurts the most, deal some massive damage and make short work of the otherwise deadly foe.

Then there are more specific weapons like the Ropecaster which is used to ensnare the machine and pinpoint it to the ground, allowing you to lob a couple of sticky grenades onto its vulnerable spot before it picks itself up.

Tripcasters make (elemental) traps, which can be used to prepare the terrain when you go up against some of the more dangerous foes. Aim and shoot two anchor points, and the weapon will make a rope between those two. Once tripped, it can trigger a simple booby-trap or exploit one of your enemies' elemental weaknesses - setting them ablaze or stunning them. Depending on the enemy and the situation, you might want to use one or the other.

There are also traps that you may place for extra advantage and control in a battle. Corruption arrows can make machines go berserk and attack everyone around them for a short time. Special elemental weapons similar to a flamethrower or its siblings of a different elemental affinity, Tearblast cannon, Rattler, and even more, but let's stop here.


So what about the story?
I actually liked it quite a bit and cared to see it through to the end. The overall presentation made it great, and the unique post-apocalyptic setting was rather refreshing to play in.

I did not read all of the logs that I found throughout the game, as most of those seemed irrelevant to the game or were some code excerpts. The main story, side-quest, and NPC dialogues were good enough to keep me going.

The part that could use quite a bit of improvement is character development, as there‚Äôs basically none of it. This isn‚Äôt a problem for me, but the game does offer you to speak in different tones on specific plot points, and it is implied that, depending on your choices, Aloy‚Äôs personality will also change. This turned out not to be the case. It is definitely not an RPG as it is stated by Steam tags, but an action-adventure with very minimal character progression, no character development, and a pretty basic level-up system, so keep that in mind.


Should you get it?
If you‚Äôre still unsure, here's what I‚Äôd boil it down to:
If dynamic, creative, and (potentially) challenging gameplay, with an original setting and an interesting story is what you value in a game, then definitely get Zero Dawn.
If you‚Äôre looking for an RPG game with a world to explore and adventures to be had above else, definitely skip it, as you‚Äôll find none of that here.

Recommended
98.0 hrs on record
Posted: August 13, 2021
Horizon Zero Dawn is a post-apocalyptic open-world RPG where you kill a bunch of machines and evil henchmen on your way to saving what remains of humanity.

Pros:
The graphics are beautiful.
The story line is fairly decent and has a very unique setting.
There is a fairly in-depth and explained historical background for the setting (though it requires some suspension of disbelief as it uses fantasy science).
It has an interesting and versatile combat system that is easy to pick up and difficult to master.
There is minimal to no grinding required.
It truly is an open-world game as you can basically go everywhere with minimal story line progression required.

Neutral:
I honestly cannot recall the background music for this game. So it clearly was not particularly memorable (neither for good nor bad reasons).
Available array of weapons was pretty bland and uninteresting. Upgrades/customization of said weaponry was also just unexciting (though still useful).
The DLC was not particularly interesting (more of the same stuff) but it did come with some new weapons, armor, and powerful new versions of existing weapons.

Cons:
The characters are rather boring - I honestly did not find any of the actual characters to be interesting and instead was more intrigued by the dead historical characters.
The combat grows stale after a while (like 20-30 hours in, combat was more of a chore than anything particularly difficult or interesting).
While this game is an RPG... it only fits that category very very loosely. The choices presented to the main character are basically inconsequential.
Side quests are repetitive, boring, unoriginal, and any other synonyms of the aforementioned.
Mounts are seriously limited and suck. With so many cool machines, you are limited to three very banal mounts (and none of them can fly).
Achievements require you to beat NG+, which is literally the same thing as NG except with better weapons available. Moreover, one of the achievements requires you to beat it on Ultra Hard (regardless of if you had beaten NG on Ultra Hard), making it even more of a chore.

Verdict:
Horizon Zero Dawn is a good game. I would be lying if I said that this game was anything spectacular, however I would also be lying if I did not admit that this game was a pretty fun journey overall. I recommend playing this game casually and at a reasonably quick pace rather than trying to do everything available (as the game will quickly feel repetitive after 20-30 hours). Essentially, if you play HZD at a casual pace while focusing primarily on the story, it is actually a really enjoyable adventure. However, if you try to finish everything (e.g. all achievements), the game will feel like a slow grind. I would 100% recommend getting this game if it goes on sale. Otherwise, you may want to consider what you are looking for in a game before you spend $50 on HZD.

Posted: May 19
Thank You

Let me start by saying "Thank You", to all those involved in delivering this game, you should all be proud of yourselves. The story, the unique interpretation of the world, the atmosphere, demonstrate your commitment, that you poured your soul into this one.

Actual Review

In this game you will play as Aloy, a curious young female who's been outcast by her tribe and finds shelter to another outcast, Rost, who will serve as her mentor and protector. After a big event, Aloy embarks into an adventure to find more about her origins and the truths of the world.
In the quest for truth, Aloy will have to face malicious humans and machines, with a spear and a bow as her main weapons. Some enemies may be too strong to face head-on, so Aloy will have to think of ways to wear out her enemies, before landing the finishing blow. As the story progresses, Aloy will be adding more situational weapons into her arsenal, that will add more depth into her combat ability.
During her journey, Aloy will have to make some choices, to show empathy (heart), be rational (brain) or aggressive (fist) in a situation. Her choices shape some responses, but no achievement or completion related events hinge upon particular options.

At the time of the review, I have completed the main game, along with the DLC ('The Frozen Wilds'), which is already included and does not need to be purchased separately.

This game is recommended for people that enjoy Action-Adventure games, and want to experience a unique interpretation of how the world may look in the distant future, accompanied by a fantastic story telling.

Tips

1. Do not enter the DLC zone (the snowy area in the north-east corner of the map) before having met a certain character named Sylens in person
2. You need to explicitly finish a NG+ run on Ultra Hard to unlock the achievements:
- New Game+ Completed
- Ultra Hard Completed
- All achievements obtained
so play whichever difficulty you fancy for the first run (I'd recommend Normal)
3. Always scan the area around you to find any possible secrets / items, they will be handy
4. Even though the Side Quests, the Errands and the additional content from the DLC are not required to complete the main story, they have helped me to get a better grasp of the world Aloy is surviving in
5. In case you play on Linux, use Proton Experimental, in my 80 hours gameplay, I didn't have a single issue

Horizon Zero Dawn is captivating, stunning, and a great ride.

Why you may ask, is it captivating?

It‚Äôs all about the story of Aloy. From the beginning you are drawn in and it keeps you intrigued and wanting to discover more...The character creation is in-depth, and well developed. A female protagonist character that has a personality and strength with no bounds that you can weave by the choices you make.

Why you may ask, is it stunning?

Visually it is one of the most beautiful games I have ever played. Its right up there with Red dead in graphics, but more than just that, the attention to details and the creativity of the atmosphere and environments, is simply superb. As a person who loves to take screen shots, this game had me snapping shots like a tourist every new place I went.

Why you may ask, is it such a great ride?

The game play, IS SO MUCH FUN! So many weapon choices, so you can be creative in how you want to take things down. If you want to be stealthy and ninja kill things, you can. Or you can set traps and bombs, and watch as things go down without much of a fight. You can even find a safe spot and sniper things from a far. You can even do a little of all above, whatever you enjoy. Although like in any game, certain areas or story may require specific methods.
I recommend this game without a doubt!

Recommended
164.4 hrs on record
Posted: August 24, 2020
8/10

Graphics
‚òë Beautiful (Great Graphics especially from a console port, textures are very well done)
‚òê Average
‚òê Outdated

Gameplay
‚òë Very Fun (Took me a while to get the hang of it, but once i did, i couldn't stop playing)
‚òê Average
‚òê Repetitive

Audio
‚òë High quality (Beautiful Soundtrack, one of the better ones in recent years to my mind)
‚òê Average
‚òê Repetitive

Difficulty
‚òë Hard (On the hardest difficulty, it posed quite the challenge, Both do-able and rewarding)
‚òê Average
‚òê Too Easy

Story
‚òë Amazing (Really well done voice acting, this carried the story which i found refreshing & enjoyable)
‚òê Average
‚òê Low quality

Bugs
‚òê None
‚òë A Couple (Lip syncing animations *can bug out, Movement can stop after looting, lag spikes occasionally)
‚òê Gamebreaking Bugs


Pros

-Beautiful Landscape, a destroyed decayed but beautiful paradise, from Snowy peeks, to tropical forests this world is beautiful from every angle, a stellar world design.
-Every Side mission feels unique, they all tell a different story, few fetch quests.
-Vantage points, these offer windows (literally) into the past showing a location before the setting of HZD, a lovely glimps into 'what was', Love this feature!
-Audio Logs, similar to The other collectables, offer viewpoints from previous ages past in good detail to really bring the world and lore to life.
-Crafting, quite a large focus of this exploration focused action/rpg, is finding resources out in the world to make bombs, traps, upgrades to help you survive in open world.
-Amazing Machine Designs, taking inspiration from real life animals mostly Jurassic/ Post, Really great designs and all feel Unique posing different challenges.
-Machines have armour plating which can be targeted to cause critical damage, these dynamically break and fall off as the battle continues, changing up the way you approach situations.
-Aloy reacts to different weather conditions and how she feels about it, a nice detail. When looting a downed enemy, parts and scrap are removed from the corpse visually.
-Photo-mode, always a great feature and as an avid screen-shotter myself extra points for this, though the camera movement could be improved, not as fluid as Ac Origins.
-As you clear corrupted zones, the weather effect changes in the region from a grey to colour, (not unlike the saboteur actually), nice detail.
-New Game + Mode which offers more weapons, gear and face paint unlocks as well as custom focus colours.


Cons

-Facial animations are capped at 30fps or at least perform under this code rule-set, often bugging out making for some, at times, odd moments.
-Eyes again seem to bug out above 30fps, moving wildly 'darting' as if a seizure might be coming on, not a good look especially breaking immersion.
-Hair has un-realistic physics (Think Assassin's Creed Unity) it just doesn't look like hair but paper, or a feather.
-Both Human Ai & Machine Ai can often bug out (Pathing mainly), sometimes failing to notice you at all or sometimes seeing you across the map, very inconsistent.
-Challenge Hunts often place other enemy types that get in the way of your hunt, messing up your times, poor design here, though a nice idea it's poorly executed.
-Stealth against human enemies flat-out doesn't work at times, often being seen behind rocks from 300 metres. Bad detection script here, assassin's creed & Splinter Cell did it better.
-Side missions wont show up on the map unless you walk within 100 or so metres of them, meaning you 'Could' miss some if you don't check the wiki.
-Snow Deformation doesn't work as intended, as the only item to work with snow deformation is The shield weaver outfit. (This could be fixed in a future patch)
-Not enough Weapon variation, and no legendary end-game weapons (not really anyway) would expect it with the Rpg mechanic Rng style.


Summery

Horizon zero dawn is a mixture of genres, an action 'Rpg' at heart with hunting mechanics and hack n' slash elements (targeting weak points etc).
It brings to mind memories of a couple of titles, 'Enslaved Odyssey to the West' in the post apocalyptic green and lush scenery, with destroyed buildings, parkour elements.
'Recore' an indie game with an action exploration setting, in a post apocalyptic setting, this time featuring machines not unlike HZD.
A great variety of enemies each with their own fighting styles, special powers and tactics, playing on ultra hard, the beginning is very tough, as cliche as it is, Dark souls would be a good example.
Even the weakest enemies can 1-2 hit you, until you start gearing up mid-game, after this + abilities you will soon be able to master your own techniques and styles for taking on each enemy.
One thing i do wish had more options was melee, you will only get 1 item, The spear with 1 mod slot to upgrade slightly (1 final one at end game that is more upgraded),
this to me isn't enough, especially on ultra-hard the spear doesn't do enough raw damage in open combat to be a viable option (in terms of larger enemies), though one can use it in stealth mode, as well as critical hits to do a little bit of damage.
Once you have the war bow, or power bow, with 3 arrow abilities, you wont be up and personal as much as early game i find, as it just does so much damage that its a bit of a handicap, in some ways not that it's a bad thing as it's still a lot of fun.
The graphics of HZD while demanding (often more than i would like, on a 2080ti getting under 50fps on medium/ultra) can look downright amazing, considering this is technically still from 2017.
The inclusion of the Photo-mode is a + though i would have liked a bit more fluidity with the camera as it seems to be locked to Aloy's player-model which isn't ideal.
The Hunting Lodge Club is a great set of side quests if a little short, would have loved it to have been a bigger focus in the narrative.
The world building in HDZ is flawless, the variety of Biomes (different atmospheres, weather patters, locations and temperatures. However, they fail to truly make a 'lived in' feel regarding NPC's and how they have an effect on the world itself. Animations while good, aren't varied enough, say compared to an assassin's creed game which offers 100's of full animation sets and activities tied to Npc's, so they feel like they are doing something at all times.
Here they will often just stand around doing pretty much nothing, (some do have custom animation sets but mostly not). If they worked on this for the sequel then i think the world would feel more alive and greatly benefit from it!

The Frozen Wilds DLC Summery

The side quests are very well written, all a blast to play, each offering small stories and extensive detail in each, branching off into their own little adventures with writing to boot.
I found myself often getting distracted planning on getting to an area, then forgetting about it for 3 hours and remembering i was going somewhere, this often happens in the base game too, just thought i'd mention it hear.
The story takes you up north 'beyond the wall', To the tribe of the Banuk, a fearless tribe of warriors, (some found in the base game).
The Dlc takes place in the real world location of Yellowstone national park, they have done a great job recreating the landmarks here, just like the base game.
IT gives more information and lore about the world of HZD, fleshing out these details with more audio logs, following the 'firebreak project' of the old world which links to the main story of frozen wilds. This really reminds me a bit of the fallout style narrative.


Overall horizon zero dawn is Lovely Game full of funny moments,a great location combined with both Primitive & futuristic themes which offers a great experience from start to finish, in mission or free roam and would highly recommend, even with its flaws it really has a lot to be commended for.


Time Played

Main Story: 35 Hours
Dlc: 20 Hours
Completionist: 60-80 Hours
Leasure: 130+ Hours

Recommended
57.5 hrs on record
Posted: April 2
Horizon: Zero Dawn is the living proof that you can make a great game if you have a great story, great writer and great designers. People can and will overlook even the most crazy and frustrating decisions of the game, if you have a spark of greatness in your game. Horizon: Zero Dawn has many great moments and even greater frustrations.

You will stay for two things in this game:

A) The visuals: Sometimes the visuals means artstyle, sometimes it means graphics. This time it means both. HZD is a beautiful game with great, realistic graphics, amazing models and great textures. The art style is also great. From snowy mountains to deserts, from the different types of machines, the cities and the plains, everything feels alive in this game and you will be immersed from the first moment you'll play.

B) The story. And what a story it is. It's structurally a masterpiece. You'll focus on the story of Aloy, a young huntress who is determined to find out about her ancestry. Simple. In this quest you'll discover gradually that her story is bigger than she was expecting, and bit by bit you will uncover the bigger picture that fills the gap of the lore of the world, plus you will take down the evil cult that wants to kill you. It feels a bit generic, but it does many things right: 1) the main quest is memorable and it has a lot of "wow" moments. 2) Great characters: the villains are a bit underutilized but other characters like Aloy, Sylens, Rost, Erend shine like diamonds. 3) the lore of the world is exceptional and it feels engaging.

Still the game has A TON of bad choices that will frustrated you. I wanted several times to quit but my will to see the story, made me pull through:

A) Over-aggro machines. I know it's intended, but it sucks in 2 major ways: First, the travelling of the world feels bad because you are constantly attacked by random packs of machines that roam the roads. So instead of going from A to B, you will be going from A to killing machines and from there to B. Secondly and most importantly, these over-aggro machines hinder your battle. Let's say you want to take out a big machine. You attack it but in doing so you alert EVERY machine in a radius of a hundred meters, so most of these battles end up in a clusterf@#$.

B) Bad levelgating: In addition to the above, sometimes you will aggro enemies that are way above your level. I just wanted to kill some scrappers and more times than none I ended up dying to a thunderjaw. Or the other time that a quest was indicated as a level 20, and the enemy inside was level 27.

C) Attrocious level tree: Level trees are about powering up and unlocking cool abilities, right? Well not in HZD. Here you will unlock the very basics like "stealth kill" or "have a mount". That's right. You have to spend 9 level points to just have a permanent mount. Or be able to strike from above. or to have more room in your inventory. Also Fast travel in this game is not free. You need resources or you will need to buy a certain item from a vendor.

D) Gear: The gear is bad because there is a small variety of it, just a couple of weapons and armor in uncommon, rare and epic. Nor the machines nor the humans drop armor as a loot which is strange, but fine. The problem is that the armor is exclusively found in vendors, which are paid in both currency and in resources, so if you want to have a better armor (as I late found in the game) you have to start taking hunting seriously.

E) Some bad combat mechanics; First the big machines (like thunderjaws and behemoths) are calibrated badly. They are huge, do a ton of damage, but also are insanely fast, like you can never outrun them in a battle and they can reach you in just a jump. Actually their animations are so fast, that even with the time-slow movement you will often miss because they move faster than the projectile.

Still HZD is great game despite the flaws I find. And I believe that this shows how great a game must be, if I am willing to overlook all these flaws that could be easily be avoided.

Posted: May 27
Really great game! The world is so beautiful. I really enjoyed exploring it through and through.

Pros:
- The combat takes some time to get used to, but once leveling up "Silent Strike" (one shot kill small enemies in stealth) early game, I found the game more enjoyable. While the early game has less combat options, I found that levelling up skills really made a difference and opened up so many options as the game went on.
- The beautiful world has huge variety - from snowy lands to deserts to lush jungles - not a moment felt boring while traversing.
- Learning the enemies' weak spots is incredibly important and really fun. The variety of enemies made me try out different tactics and bows. There's actually a reason to try out almost all the types of weapons and ammo types.

Good to know:
- The 2020 Steam launch seems to have had some bugs or crashes; I played in 2022 so it was 100% smooth for me, no issues and the game ran super smoothly.
- There's a while in the early/mid-game main story quest that I felt had a slow pace which made me a bit bored for a while. But the story really picked up after and got me even more engaged than before! I think the late game quests were all worth it.
- I feel that the stealth options were sometimes lacking, so it was hard for me to play in pure stealth, which I had wanted to sometimes. But perhaps it was due to early game lack of upgrades; I found myself getting mobbed less after getting more stealth upgrades.

Overall really enjoyed my time with this game - the exploration never had a boring moment, and while the early / mid-game quests had some slower pace, the late game quests really made up for it.

To start: Take the role of an outcast in a world where primitive tribes survive against rampaging machines.

The Positives
+ An impressive third-person action RPG in a post-apocalyptic setting with robot T-rexes.
+ The environments are stunning, biomes ranging from tundra to desert, with photo mode at the ready.
+ Strong female lead done right, defined by her strength and capabilities rather than physical attributes.
+ Combat is unique when it comes to the machines, nothing more satisfying than whittling them down by shooting off their individual components.
+ Enemies increase in size and difficulty at a gratifying pace, Aloy also getting stronger by unlocking new skills and obtaining new gear.
+ Wonderful, thought-provoking story, despite elements that are familiar in the science fiction genre.
+ Worldbuilding at its finest, depicting humans in a believable way (worshipping gods that don‚Äôt exist, splitting into separate tribes and fighting each other, etc).
+ Phenomenal soundtrack that fits perfectly with the theme.
+ The Frozen Wilds is a solid expansion with new enemies, stories, skills, as well as the most powerful weapons in the game.

The Negatives
- Open World Syndrome isn‚Äôt especially egregious, but there‚Äôs still bloat and meaningless content to distract from the rather short main questline.
- Consistent hand-holding that‚Äôs all too common in open world games, where the player is treated like they‚Äôre incompetent (an example being that Aloy will often comment on what to do / where to go).
- Forgettable characters apart from a select few, BUT a nice detail is the NPCs that Aloy helps throughout show up at the final battle. If their quests aren't completed, they don't show.

To end: Released on PC three years after console launch. Top-tier even with its flaws. Opinions are my own and reflect my experience. Full review can be found at Leviathan Libraries.

Recommended
87.1 hrs on record
Posted: June 12
Horizon Zero Dawn

First of all, don't get me wrong. It's a great game and well worth playing. Sony has managed to create one of the best and most memorable main characters in video game history. And certainly one of the the best female protagonist out there. Aloy is strong, intelligent, and kind. And has the right background to explain her epic skills in combat and survival. Not like some other female protagonist we all know. With abilities no human should have and that are never explained or those remembered mostly for their boobs.
But for this review, I will mainly focus on the game's bad side. And there's plenty of that in the game.

Concept:

Let's tackle the elephant in the room. HZD uses the typical Ubisoft formula. They've used it so many times in Far Cry and their hundreds of Assassin's Creed games. Square used the same formula with the new Tomb Raider series and the Thief game. And now Sony used it with Horizon Zero Dawn. In itself it's nothing bad. But if you've played any of these games, you've pretty much seen it all.
You have your main quest line, which takes around 5-6 hours if that's what you focus on mostly. And the rest is filled with all sorts of random things to artificially blow up playtime. Random loot you'll never really need unless you go on random animal and machine hunts, random vistas, random lore, random and repetitive side quests, random NPCs you'll never see again, random bandit camps, etc. That's a lot of random. It's enjoyable at first, but the more you play, you relize it just drags on and on and on.
And all the random lore pieces in the world don't help at all. Because most of the time it's about something very trivial. No explanation about the world you live in or how the tribes build their things and their society, how the tribes themselves evolved so differently besides living so close to each other. It's a story telling mess and all over the place. So much potential lost.

So you have about 5-7 hours for the main quest and about 60-70 hours of random stuff. That's 10-15% on the essential and world building and the rest is just random. I'm pretty sure some people will like this kind of concept for some crazy reason, but when you think of some of the greatest games of all time, you just have to be disappointed. In these games you have the complete opposite. You have 80 percent and more time to grapple with the story, the concept, and all the little things about the world you're playing in, and the rest are things that don't matter that much to the bigger picture.

Main story:

The main story is solid. Nothing new or unique. Nothing you haven't seen, read or heard. But it has a decent pacing, and just enough uniqueness to stand out from the rest. But there are no surprises and you will know everything in the middle of the main quest. Or even before that. Overall, the dialogues are not very well written and pretty basic at times.
That might sound a little harsh, but they ended up wasting 60 hours on random things instead of deepening the main story with a few more NPCs and lore. And it's not like the NPCs on the main path are very interesting either, apart from the main character and the "other" main character (I think you know who I mean). All others are very generic and interchangeable. You'll realize how basic everything is when you just rush a new game + for the achievements. I did this in 5 hours and I have no regrets missing out on any of the random things the game has to offer.


Honourable mention:

And besides how simple and straight forward the game already is, they really have implemented a hand holding system from start to the very end of the game. Why? Just why? Do they really think gamers are just stupid and need constant advice not to get lost? I mean, it's ok in the beginning, but later it gets extremely annoying.
You have to follow tracks but you will never lose them as they are highlighted like a Christmas tree in the evening. There is always a waypoint marker that points directly to the next quest step. There are almost 200 campfires (fast travel points and checkpoints) on the map, so you don't have to walk more than 50 meters. 200 of them! And Aloy is constantly commenting on things as you fight or walk around to remind you of the right path and tactics for specific enemies.
So, come on! Have a little faith in your customers. There are not deranged and certainly don't need constant guidance to beat your game. Do that!, Go there! I mean seriously!

And before I forget. The AI ‚Äã‚Äãis really, really bad. Especially for the machines, but also for humans.


Conclusion:

Those critics aside, the game is a wonderful pastime. But just don't expect any depth or great worldbuilding. It's wonderful for a first playthrough and maybe a second time for the story in a few years. But mostly I'm just disappointed with the lost potential and how bloated the game is. If you remove all that random stuff, you'll see that there just isn't much left.
But that's a problem of our time and people seemed content with this kind of games. Don't think much, don't ask much, just a time filler. Like a typical Hollywood action movie. You watch it and forget everything about it as soon as you leave the cinema. It's just not my thing. But stunning graphics and audio don't belie a thin concept and weak writting.

Personal Score: 8/10

Ps.: Here's just a reminder. I was just talking about the bad stuff here. Because everything else has already been discussed many times. Graphics, audio, combat, weapons and the various elementals, mods, DLC are mostly top notch.
