Horizon Zero Dawn 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: ZEBpai

System Specs
i5-9600k @ 4.3Ghz
32 GB DDR4 Memory
Gigabyte RTX 2060 Super
Samsung SSD 970 EVO

Played everyday since the release day on Steam and not a single crash like others have been experiencing. I have some frame drops when you are going through new areas mostly inside the Cauldrons. Aside from that I really enjoyed playing the game.

I finished the New Game on Very Hard Difficulty because I don't like the vendor price increase in Ultra Hard. Then I did NG+ Ultra Hard Difficulty. The difficulty is fair enough and not that hard. But the vendor increase price in Ultra Hard is so unreasonable, if it weren't for that I would go straight NG UH. The story and combat mechanics of the enemies are pretty good. I had a lot of fun fighting all of them especially the ones in the DLC. One thing that I wanna change though is how bright the machines eyes when it is night time. Especially the new machine in the DLC because when they are in front of you, the glare is really bad that you just want to close your eyes.

And speaking of having a hard time to see. If there is weather or it is night time it's pretty hard to see the human enemies. Although I am wondering if this is part of the difficulty design decision. If this is, then it's okay I guess.

Since I played all the Tomb Raider games reboot, some have similar elements from the franchise. Like the campfire save and travel points, resource gathering from wildlife, and plants, and the climbing explorations.

One QoL improvement they should implement on the plant gathering is have a different colored icon. Like when you loot wildlife if they drop higher rarity materials. Although it's easier to identify from afar if a plant is a wood resource, the other plants such as the medicine, shock, fire. etc are hard to differentiate.

Now the campfires, there are lot of campfires around the map. So there are lot of save points and fast travel points you could go to. But some of the campfires have also a respawn point of enemies, that's just pretty stupid design decision imo. Imagine travelling to a certain campfire and as soon as you load there's an enemy there on the campfire.

I am really getting some Tomb Raider vibes while playing the game and exploring the areas. There's one thing I noticed also is Aloy used her spear to pry through some doors just like Lara's climbing axe. I hope we could've expand the use as well of the other weapons to open up certain areas or remove some obstacle along the way.

There are only a few puzzles in this game but they are very easy. Although I like the ones in the DLC. I hope we could have more challenging puzzles on Forbidden West.

Map size and scale is very good design wise. Not so small, not too big. And you have a pretty amount of side quest with good stories to them. Not like other games, especially AC Origins. You have a very large open world map with lots of locations to uncover but they are all the same and boring.

Dialogue scenes, One thing I noticed about dialogue views is they aren't dynamic to every NPCs. The game have a specifc amount of different camera views of dialogue and used in all of the dialogues. Also the pose of a downed/dying NPC when you are talking to them. They have all the same pose. They could improve this in Forbidden West having dynamic camera views on every NPC dialogue. Different poses of downed NPCs depending on how they are injured. Adding more personality to NPC when they are talking not just the head animations.


100% Completion! Forbidden West here we go!!!!

ZEBpai

Recommended
71.0 hrs on record
Posted: January 29, 2021
Still wouldn't buy a console for this

TL;DR If you love open world action games then buy it. This is open world game done right.

You play as Alloy starting from childhood (which reminded me a little of Witcher 3 intro with Ciri). After a short tutorial Alloy is grown up and ready to uncover the truth setting the foot in a beautiful open world.

The gameplay consists of fighting enemies, doing quests and some other minor stuff.
The world is set far in the future and machines have taken over the world. I love the idea that ‚Äúancient world‚Äù is portrayed as our world (slightly in the future) and you can see fragments of ancient world which is a bit disturbing when you realize someday our world might look like that and archeologists will dig through the ruins of our skyscrapers.
But the whole idea of the story isn't new, it has been discussed by multiple games and movies. So don't expect a deep story here. But it's well written and you want to play more to find out the truth. I would compare it to a movie, take romance movie for example. There are thousands of movies with the same idea, but some are trash, some are great. So Horizon is the same, idea which has beaten to death presented well.
It takes multiple ideas and puts them together, yeah it's not innovative or very original but it's not a bad thing it's still a good game, taking existing ideas and making a good game out of it requires a lot of talent. Lot of games do the same but they are boring because people making those games just put everything together without any thought or effort. Horizon on the other hand polishes those ideas.

I'd say this game is a blend of some other games. Assassin's Creed, Enslaved and maybe a little of Witcher 3. Although AC has prettier world, their world design, architecture has no equals. Enslaved has better characters. Witcher 3 has better side quests.

Characters are average, including Alloy. I wish there would be more to Alloy. Like having fun in a feast, dancing, falling in love, sitting on the edge of the mountain thinking about existence. Remember Witcher's 3 HoS quest where you visited a feast, the boat scene? This is what I want. Alloy is pretty shallow character. Sure she's tough, helping, determined and a great fighter, but I haven't felt any connection with her.
Same applies to side characters. You get a lengthy dialogue and you hear a little story, learn about the lore and you like the character. But after you do that quest it's over. There were several characters I loved, I wanted quest chains, I wanted to sit with them at the table, maybe play some mini-game. The little stories are great but it just ends and you don't see those characters anymore.

I don't mean to look like i'm bashing the game here. Everything I said here is good, but its just good, not great.
But it has great things too. Combat is amazing. This game has one of the best combat i've ever seen. It's dynamic, fluid, responsive and fast. It never gets boring. There are different machines and multiple ways to beat them. Each machine has its weakpoints. You need to shoot the weakpoints with your bow to do more damage. Some machines are weak to electricity, cold or fire so you choose different arrows. There are also slings which shoot elemental bombs. You can tie machines with ropes and then swing at them with your weapon. You can set traps. You can play stealthy and lure them towards you and override them so they would fight along you. You can use them as mounts. With all these possibilities and a bunch of different machines the combat feels amazing.

Then there's Frozen Wilds location (included DLC) and machines there are much more challenging. I suggest doing the DLC before you finish the main quest. It affects the ending slightly.
Frozen wilds offers new weapons and new characters, you learn more about the lore and story of the region and its people.

The world is filled with Ubisoftish collectibles but it's almost just about the right amount of those. I wish there would be ~20% less. There are vantage points where you learn about an ancient world a bit and can see how it looked back then. Tallneck's which you climb and override which opens up more of the map. And some non-important trash collectibles.

While the combat is fast there's an easy mode so it should be suitable for everyone. You can't win by mashing same button and you will need to move but it's pretty easy to do. Difficulty levels are very flexible and will satisfy everyone. I've played on story mode and played NG+ on ultra hard. The one was easy and the other was extremely challenging. Want to torture yourself? Play on ultra hard from the start.

Graphically it's a beautiful game but a weird one. All the areas and environments look amazing. There are so many details everywhere. The world is beautiful. Trees, other vegetation, snow, machines and people. Machine are especially well detailed. Character models are high quality too, considering it's an open world game with lots of talking the character models are nearly perfect. It's really good game for screenshot lovers, especially with included photo mode which allows you to capture awesome screenshots.
There are a lot of graphics options to tune and great AA implementation.
One thing I found funny that those few pre-rendered cut-scenes look worse than in-game ones. Clearly captured on a console.
Now the weird parts. First one is minor issue but I found it weird that you don't always leave footprints on the snow (in non-frozen wilds areas). At first I thought maybe it's by design but then I noticed that sometimes footprints appear. And the moment I realized it's a glitch/bug was when I needed to follow an NPC and he left footprints and Alloy did not.
Now another one. This game has one of the best facial expressions and animations when you compare it to open world games. Most of the time they're awesome. Not only mouth movement but expressions, wrinkles moving, imperfect teeth, body language. All characters are high quality unlike in AC Origins where minor NPC's have lower quality textures and no facial animations. But sometimes (i'd say ~20%) of the time facial animations in Horizon do not work. You stare at a lifeless face. I thought maybe it's only some characters but it's not. Same character might say one sentence with great animation and then just barely move his mouth. What is even weirder is that Alloy has the worst facial animations in the game.
But overall the game is stunning graphically.

Performance is average. Considering how the game looks it's not bad but it could be better. I played on 3700x, 2070s, 32gb at 3440x1440 and had ~50fps. The good thing is that the framerate is very stable and the whole game felt very smooth. In closed locations fps increased to 60-70 for me.
There's no ultrawide support out of the box. Developers did false advertising saying it will have one. So you will need a simple fix to enable ultrawide support in cut-scenes. But I don't like when developers are lying. Having uw support in gameplay sections in a 3D game with free camera is not a feature.

The sound design is good. Soundtrack may not be memorable but music adds a nice layer of atmosphere. Voice acting is great. From main characters to the most minor ones it sounds enthusiastic and believable. For Fringe fans there's a nice surprise.

Overall a very good open world action game everyone should play. Maybe it lacks originality or character depth but the combat outweighs all the minor negative things.

Pros
Stunning graphics
Very good combat
Beautiful world
Great voice acting
Exploring is fun
Side quest backstories are good
Cons
Average performance
Developers lied about uw support
Character depth&development could be better
Side quests could have quest chains

Follow my curator page for more

Recommended
65.2 hrs on record
Posted: August 11, 2020
.STOP, IF YOU HAVE ISSUES TRY THESE. (Game has had patches, read game updates If your issue was within the realm of the patches notes, give it another try.)

With that said, I hope many people see this. It's going to be a long one. I could not to get the game to work for several days, and I started some testing to figure out some issues and problems. Ultimately I figured it had something to do with restributional packages, C++ and windows update. Upon doing a complete DDU clean install of my GPU drivers, and manually updating my computer to the current 2004 Windows Update, the game works perfectly, without crashes, without stutters. Allowing comments on this review, if anyone has any questions I'll answer them to the best of the ability of the steps I ran through. My previous Windows 10 version was 1709, make sure you're updated to 2004 ver. If anything, at least try updating to the Win 10 ver 2004 using the media creation tool.

With all that said, the game runs smooth, and now that it works I feel my effort has been rewarded and my eyes stream tears of joy into the depths that is Lord Gabin's wallet. Praise be the sun.

Edit: 0.7 hours when post the review. Currently at several hours in and no issues thus far. Will be posting findings later on in the forum section for the game.

Edit V.2: Aye, the version of windows I was using was the 1709 and wasn't updating to anything past. I manually downloaded the updates until I was at the 1909 update. At this point was then I actually got into the cinematic at the opening of the game. But the graphics were stuttering, or missing entirely. This was when I updated further into the 2004 Win 10 package. There were still roughly the same issues, but at this point it said my GPU drivers were out of date. The next step was use DDU (Display Driver Uninstaller) and did a full clean graphics install. Next step I installed C++ items to make sure it was installed. The final piece I did was make sure the .net framework was working properly and installed. To do this you just need to type in Windows Features in your bottom search bar. Click turn windows features on or off, and one of the first things listed is
.Net Framework 3.5 and below was .NET Framework 4.8 Advanced services. Under the 4.8 Framework I only have the TCP Port sharing turned on and the ASP.net 4.8. After which I played through windows update so it auto installed the .NET services and got the computer fully up to date. Loaded the game to see if it worked....And cried tears of joy and proceeded to stay up until 7 am Playing it.

Edit V.3: As a side note to this, it probably won't help everyone, but it might help some along the way in being able to enjoy this awesome game. Probably won't fix everyones issues, but it def fix mine. Last edit will be after a few more hours of gameplay about pros-cons.

Edit V.4: So with all this I did and finally being able to play the game...Here's my take on it.

Edit V.5: Alright, Ive had many people complaining in the comments of section of this, and that's fine, but overly toxic and unhelpful comments are being removed. If it doesn't work for you, just say it doesn't, and give specs. Ill throw the date back to the devs when I can.

Firstly, if you want a game that can give you immersion, feel as if you can connect with the main character then this is def the game for you. They brought her to life on many aspects, whether it be gathering, hunting, getting spotted when out of stealth, taking down targets, and minor choices during dialog/quests/side missions. It was rather well done to give you that connection.

HOWEVER, at the same time the game is so gorgeous that it suffers from a few noticable issues, primarily that of how facial animations translate emotions. Example: Mass effect andromeda was horrible at release because those animations were so elastic or hyper memey to the point it didn't feel like you were in a game at all. GreedFall also suffers from it to a degree, yet still a step up from Andromeda IMO. Those were blocky and sometimes the lips looked more like a fish than any real human could make. I would still say it's a big step up from there. To me it feels as if the game looks and feels good that the face's animations or portrayal of emotion is more set in the tone of voice than the actually characters themselves, or are very nuanced form of interpretation.

Secondly, Gameplay. It feels smooth, very reaction based or by preparing for the fight ahead. You get a plethora of options as far as weapons, some very situational, different types of traps that can be used, still experimenting with how well I enjoy that system.....But Hot sweet baby Jesus did they make the outfits/armor look more stylish than your grandmother going to a modern disco party

Third, Graphics. So I know many are having issues, still having problems with crashes, but with everything I did above and on my end now having no problems (I'm sorry for those stills struggling) It's clean, no stutters, Ultra graphics, even running it on bordless, without any frame loss. Why this is I've no idea. However, sometimes I feel the graphics is dummed down on certain textures such as rocks, like they were smashed together by a 5 year old playing with playdough for the first time?...Maybe? But in other places such as character design, outfits, Enemies, it looks very well down, the Mechs are cleanly made and got some really good glowy bits all around...Sometimes there can be a minor issue with Lights on an enemy called "The Watchers." Occasionally when they spot you it's like the wraith of God Almighty and Zeus have come together to smite the unholy heathen you are for being so technologically incapable, and might aswell be 50 feet away from a quasar with how BRIGHT AS HECK their eyeball beam is.

The game also takes away from a few others as far as certain designs, features, mainly a few of that of Skyrim with how markers work, which bring me to my last point. The biggest downfall and hyper annoyance, (For me) Is I want to say when I open the minimap it's like walking into a homeless shelter that has too much direction. There are markers just about everywhere, more campfires (Fast travel points) that it seems like there is just some random bloke who's a nomand but suffers from narcolepsy so he makes a fire every few feet to ward off the demons in his soul. To me there are just so many points on the map that I wish things were more spread out, maybe the map made bigger to trick me into thinking the place is bigger than it really is? Oh, and tutorials are not done by most normal expectations either. No No my good friends. They are quests with their own reaping rewards, didn't find that out until 16 hours in...So you could technically go through the whole game without even noticing it.

With all that I give this game an 7/10, and that's only because of the hassle that I sacrificed my first born child, gave blood to the blood gods, and purged the heretics out of my computer in order to play this game. As is until patch, unless you're dedicated like me to play this game...Just wait, be patient, or buy it and let it linger in your library until you see the patches being downloaded through your steam.

And if you want a game that will make you feel like you're a toddler with parkisans trying to hold a squirt gun on the hardest difficulty when you barely understand the game. This game is for you, cause I love to not understand ANYTHING about a game and punish myself for the sake of entertainment.

Posted: October 2, 2020
One of the best open-world games I have ever played!
Horizon Zero Dawn is arguably one of the best PC games of 2020.

The Story

It's the 31st century but people live in spiritual tribes. The world had an
apocalypse hundreds of years ago and all knowledge of the "old ones" was lost.
Or was it? There are still huge robotic machines roaming the planet and they
are about to be the cause of Apocalypse on Earth 2.0.

You play as Aloy. A young female who was cast out from her tribe for an unknown reason.
Even worse - A different tribe tries to kill you when Aloy becomes a young adult.
Why was she cast out? Why did the killers want her dead? Are these two things connected
(obviously)?
This and much more is up to you to discover. You must travel the HUGE world of Horizon
Zero Dawn, find buildings of the "Old Ones", learn about the machines and technology of
the past and maybe, just maybe, find out why and how did the apocalypse happen. Prevent
it from happening again and find out why you were cast out and get some well
deserved inner quacking peace.

The game also has lots of side-quests and each of those quests is actually quite fun and feels
like a little side-story. Nothing as great as in The Witcher 3 but still miles (or kilometers)
better than anything Assassin's Creed has tried to sell us as side-quests.


Gameplay

Horizon Zero Dawn is an open-world action platformer that lies about being an RPG.
Now don't get me wrong. I absolutely loved the gameplay and kept hunting machines even
if I didn't have to. It's just that choice making is very very scarce and even then it
barely has any effect on anything at all.

You can earn experience points and level up by slaying machines and men and by doing quests. Each time you gain a level or each time you finish a quest you gain skill points.
Now skill points can be spent on four different skill trees: Prowler, Brave, Forager and
Traveler. Some skill trees focus on melee or ranged combat. Some let you gather more resources and expand your medicine pouches and one skill tree even lets you repair tamed machines (Yes. You can tame machines. Wild, right?).

You can also carry four different weapons with you at all times. Now weapons can be bought, earned, or crafted. There are all sorts of slingshots, bows, and traps to choose from and you actually do have a 5th weapon that can not be equipped or unequipped. It's your spear and you carry it with you all the time. It's your basic default weapon that you use for either melee attacking enemies or overriding them.


Performance

I played on a 50" 4K TV and I have an RTX 2080 Super and the game ran super smooth on 4K resolution, everything on ultra and HDR Rendering on. I've seen some people having issues with the game but I can only talk about my own experience and my experience was awesome. I did experience one crash but I spent over 60 hours in the game and honestly, a crash or two is bound to happen in almost every video game so I guess I can say my experience has been pretty much flawless.

Definitely worth the full price.. In my humble opinion of course.

Problem Solving
Solving Graphic Stuttering Issue:
Change "render scale" from 100% to 90%. In-game v-sync and FPS lock doesn't work properly, you can try on your Nvidia Settings. And remember to restart the game in order to apply the settings.

To improve FPS:
THREE THINGS that matter: Clouds > Reflections > Ambient Occlusion. Try to adjust those settings. Like I said at the beginning, if you try to lower the graphic settings and it doesnt work, it is not your problem. This game has a poor optimization for some models of graphic card and CPU.

Comments
This is my last update on this game. I finished this game at around 80 hours with 6 hours problem solving and testing. Aside from the issues, this is definitely a good game. It‚Äôs one of my favorites. It always has an amazing view in the background.

However, I can't ignore all those problems that I experienced. I also can't hide my disappointment with the PC production team. I would rather buy a PS4+Horizon than buy this game on PC. This game worth around $35 to me on PC.

This game was originally released on Feb 28, 2017 on PS4. It supposed to run smoothly on PC in 2020. I‚Äôm glad someone can play this game smoothly without any problems, I really do, but this is not my case. I'm running an i7-7700K with a RTX 2080 in 1080p 60Hz monitor. I got a stable 85+ FPS under ultra-graphics setting, but graphical stuttering and game crashing are always the problems. Moreover, I can tell some of the settings are the "trouble makers"; e.g. the FPS lock, the in-game v-sync, etc. This game had terrible optimization when it released. I couldn‚Äôt even finish this game without lower the settings and went through all those problem-solving processes. I did a lot of research on google, reddit, steam review, youtube, mod forum, etc.

Anyway, I‚Äôm glad there are a bunch of nice gamers around here and reddit to exchange information with me, and they even taught me how to change the settings in order to run the game without crashing. Thank you all!

Posted: July 17, 2021
If I hadn't played Assassin's Creed Odyssey, this one would definitely have been my favourite game.

Overall- 9.5/10
Story - 9/10
-World building and concepts - 10/10
-Side quests - 7/10
Gameplay - 9/10
-Enemy AIs- 10/10
-Combat-9/10
-Inventory management- 4/10
Graphics - 10/10
-optimization and performance - 8/10


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This is going to be much more of comparison between the two games (AC Odyssey and HZD) than just the review.
Also, (being dumb) I played game in Ultra Hard difficulty right from start so experience would be slightly different. I would recommend to play it in easy mode to breeze through story instead and then have the real playthrough in full Ultra Hard glory in new game plus. (since last 3 achievements requires it anyways),
Also, I absolutely loved HZD so all the complaints are really the nitpicking. With the world HZD has built I am much more excited about its future games rather than AC series.


Worldbuilding, Characters and Story-
This is where the game really shines. Characters, tribes, side quests are all good enough but the overall concept and just world that is imagined in the game is amazing.



Exploring-
HZD is much more of a survival game- You cannot save from menu, instead have to find nearest campfire. Health depleted is not auto recovered. Your resources are finite (especially in Ultra hard difficulty), gathering them takes some time. And everywhere you go be prepared to be ganged up by ruthless machines.
Well all this does make exploring in the beginning difficult but eventually as you learn about the world it is fun.
I loved the different settings of the world but aside from achievements I didn't feel like exploring each corner (which I did in ACO2).
This is matter of personal taste, HZD's world is filled tight with things, every turn you take you are bound to find something. I prefer ACO2 vast world with lots of open spaces where it felt more rewarding coming across something.
Also, sliding off of edges is big issue and there is always big fall damage. I hope climbing is better in next one as well, I am not big fan of circling a mountain to find the way up or climbing it the SKYRIM way. ‚Äã


Combat-
Combat is something which really makes you want to act smart, but at the end of the day I couldn't master that part,
I would much rather just burn the machines down or freeze them to attack. There is scope to try a lot of things to bring down machines with HUGE variety of weapons.
I like bigger machines rather than the ones relying on numbers, I could only really master Thunderjaw whom I love fighting.
Most of it ends up being ranged combat instead and there really isn't much you can do in melee or stealth department.
Overall though this is the aspect I still want to explore more and I think is much too different (and maybe even better) than ACO2. AIs are much smarter in HZD, breaking line of sight won't be enough, stealth won't be easy.
And yes, as everyone keeps saying, fighting humans or camps isn't that much fun.
Ranged- 10/10
Melee- 4/10
Stealth- 1/10
Potion selection controls- 0/10 - It should have been part of quick select menu or similar, there is huge penalty mid fight if you click away from selected potion by mistake.


--Small inventory-
This is my BIG complaint in the game. All the items are kept in same inventory including the resources you need for fighting and rare items that you get.
AND THERE IS NO SECONDARY INVENTORY (like Inns in Witcher1 or Ship in Odyssey).
So even if I have tons of resources I have to get rid of them, only to go grind/gather them again.
OR risk selling of rare items and then just for a small upgrade go searching a freaking Racoon! Same with buying weapons/armors.


Optimization and Graphics-
Though both games are equally pretty, ACO2 worked better for me since I could play it at high settings comfortably, here I had to settle with medium settings.
Not requiring to restart the game if you change settings is great (unlike ACO2). The game still looks pretty even on lowest settings so I liked flexibility of changing settings on the go depending on whether I wanted the fps or prettier world.
Photo mode doesn't have a free camera, instead it centers on Aloy so movement requires a bit of getting used to. But poses and changing time - essentially controlling light angle is great. Good facial expressions would have made it better

so gorgeous 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Notsoperfect



Minor complaints-
-I feel bad killing watchers, they are too cute lol. Sawtooth's limping is too real as well, I feel bad hurting them sometimes (unless they are ganging up on me, in that case death to all of them).
-Wish there was day/night switch like Odyssey.
-Levels are really what decide attack/defense stats rather than weapons/armors. Also, no numbers for them in the selection menu. Stealth stat basically makes you invisible at higher upgrades but there is no invisible suit (like stalkers).
-Skill tree is meh. Additional levelling points go nowhere. (Odyssey was much better at this).


Overall-
A must play game.
Much more of a challenge compared to AC Odyssey and can be played for anywhere from 50 to 300 hours easily.


"Being smart will count for nothing if you don't make the world better. You have to user your smarts to count for something, to serve life, not death.

Recommended
109.2 hrs on record
Posted: August 14, 2020
This game's strengths come from really unexpected places, namely the wonderful strength and humility of Aloy, and the exceptional writing that reveals itself slowly through the archaeological snippets you locate in the world. The rest of the game is pretty run-of-the-mill 3rd person RPG (if you've played Witcher 3 or Assassins' Creed Odyssey you've played this), but those two aspects - character and story - make the game an instant classic and well worth your time and money.

Aloy is incredible. She's compassionate, stubborn, tenacious and resilient, and takes ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• from nobody. The choice to make her an outcast is a stroke of genius, it means she has the same flabbergasted and incredulous responses to the world as the player. Because of this, no matter what she does, it doesn't break immersion and fits with her character. The voice acting - by the same person, bizarrely, who voices Tiny Tina in the Borderlands games, is achingly good.

I'm a historian, and I absolutely adore the way the game builds its sense of the past. There's no obvious narrative buried in pieces in shallow graves, there's just endless snippets of pre-apocalyptic life scattered about - advertising, memoirs, trinkets. The way watches and keys show up in your inventory as "bracelets" and "chimes" is deeply endearing, and helps to make the pre-apocalypse material feel more and more alien. I particularly love the way the merchant who collects mugs describes them - a rare treat.

Capping it all off, the character models, while no Red Dead Redemption 2, are incredible and very relatable, and the music is just perfect - mournful but not without purpose, like the world it accompanies.

The combat is the good kind of frustrating - I'm playing on hard and die a lot, but the sense of accomplishment when you, say, shoot the gun off a Ravager and then use it to kill the same Ravager and all its friends, is great. The different damage types take a while to get your head around and are pretty poorly-explained in the game, but once they click you will feel hella badass in fights - exactly how 3rd person games should make you feel! Just make sure to upgrade your gear quickly - otherwise you'll quickly find yourself in grindy fights doing plink damage. There are only three tiers of armour and no level limits, so just buy the best thing you can ASAP.

A word about the port - I have an i7-9700KF, 2070 Super 8GB and 32GB RAM and I run it on Ultra capped at 60fps with no hiccups. Weirdly the benchmark feature had lower framerate than the game, but maybe that's what you want a benchmark feature to do? I experienced some very bad graphics bugs on day one but they were fixed by a driver update. I've have no dramas since.

Just absolutely do yourself a favour and buy this game.

EDIT: I've now finished the game, and experienced a few crashes - one when I and my enemy were both airborne, and two in cutscenes. One of them reset my settings, which was annoying. But on the whole, the port was fine.

Not Recommended
0.8 hrs on record
Posted: June 26, 2021
Product refunded

I've heard and read many good things about this game and decided to try grabbing it while it was on sale. Immediately after the intro cutscene, I was severely turned off by the list of terms spelled out in their data collection agreement.

It only provides two options: "Limited" or "Full" data collection. You can't opt out. After reading over it a few times, I consider even the Limited option to be providing too much information. They ask for access to much more info than would be needed for a developer to help with troubleshooting or bug fixes for a single-player game.

I looked around for justification and found none, so I felt that I had to conclude that the goal was to gather my (our) data simply to sell it...data that could possibly include identifying info and personal/private activities not related to the game.

I'm aware that I'm already feeding my info to other nefarious companies, though that's mostly out of necessity to live and work in the modern world. It's plain depressing when those invasive fishhooks are embedded in our simple pleasures too. I'm personally uncomfortable allowing a business to pull that level of info from me when they have no use for it aside from selling it.

It's a shame, but I've refunded the game and can't in good conscience recommend it while it sits behind this wall of telemetry. Same goes for any other games that follow the same profit-driven philosophy...data about your personal computer usage is not "trivial" or "useless" and don't let anyone tell you different.

Recommended
262.7 hrs on record
Posted: February 25
9/10 -- One of the best games I have ever played. Properly in my top 10 games of all time.
A modern open-world classic.

‚ö†Ô∏èThis review does ùó°ùó¢ùóß contain spoilers but other reviews might‚ö†Ô∏è

I have just completed my first ever playthrough of Horizon Zero Dawn. The game looked beautiful and intriguing to me but I admit I wasn't expecting to like it too much as I really struggle to stay immersed with third-person perspective games, and also this style of game; fire, dodge, role, counterattack, fire, dodge, role... but I realized quickly it's so much more than that.
I was very pleasantly surprised, it's truly fantastic! It is one of the most immersive, jaw-dropping, heartwarming, and moving games I have played.

‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ
‚Ä¢ Story:
The story is truly great and touches on many real-world issues such as where we and the world are heading, what might happen. It's brilliant and there is comfortably 30+ hours of gameplay even if only do the main story and blitz through it quickly. You take your time to explore and do many of the amazing side quests, there is comfortably 100 or 200 hours of gameplay. My first playthrough is 235 hours to 100% it.

‚Ä¢ Difficulty:
Sadly, after the first few hours even on ultra-hard difficulty the game does get quite easy. Especially once you start encountering the largest machines and play the Frozen Wilds DLC.
I highly recommend anyone plays on at least one difficulty level higher than you normally would otherwise it may get too easy and boring towards the end. Also, the HUD makes things very easy, and also it can be a little cluttered. Thankfully the settings menu for disabling and tweaking the HUD is really great, you can highly customize it to be disabled most of the time until you need it.
If you're like me and you like a real challenge, you might have to set yourself artificial limitations like not using the strongest weapons or armor to keep it challenging.

‚Ä¢ Settings / Menu Options:
This surprised me, for a console port the dev team behind this put a lot of time and effort into accommodating PC players. the amount of customization of the HUD, gameplay elements and tutorials, live representation of graphical settings so you visibly see what the graphics settings change and how it's improved.
I would say it feels like it was made for PC, it doesn't feel like a console port. Huge kudos to the dev team.

‚Ä¢ Graphics & Lighting:
The visuals are phenomenal. The world does feel completely open and full of wonder, and a lot of that is due to the visuals. High-res textures are nice but you need a lot more to really captivate and immerse someone in a world. I've never taken so many screenshots of a game in my life and found myself walking at a slow pace around the map just so I could look at the world. Although, I do highly recommend installing a re-shade filter as nighttime is way too bright and so are caves.
The only negative here is recent updates have caused some pop-in issues, but the devs are aware and still actively releasing hotfixes.

‚Ä¢ Sound & Music:
Whether the immersive reverb and echoes when in a valley surrounded by mountains, or the metallic binary but still somehow alive and sentient calls or cries of the animals/machines, to the breathtaking scores and music... it is one of the best parts of the game, I immediately downloaded the soundtrack for my phone when I want to relax and chill before bed.

‚Ä¢ Mod support:
Sadly, there is not much in the way of mods, of course, there are the obligatory naked and glamour mods to make women prettier for you thirsty mofos, haha. However, other than that it's just ReShade mods, which I would highly recommend as nighttime is way too bright and so are deep caves and ruins.

‚Ä¢ Bugs:
The latest update sadly introduced some pop-in issues but the devs have acknowledged it and are working to hotfix it. There are few LOD (distant terrain) textures that have Z-fighting (flickering) but it's not bad just the occasional one here and there. You can sometimes get a big hit from a machine that forces you inside a texture such as a rock, meaning you will either need to load a save or call for your rideable mount, which will come close enough for you to hop on pulling you out of the glitch. Again only happened to me twice in nearly 250 hours played so it's not common.
Only ever experienced a few crashes and that was while I was alt-tabbing in and out frequently.

‚Ä¢ Replayability:
Definitely replayable, there are enough weapons, outfits, modifications, upgrades, perks, and choices to make throughout the game that definitely make it replayable.

‚Ä¢ Performance & fps:
Very good, actually I was quite surprised it was so good. With an RTX 3080Ti my framerate never dropped below 60fps at 3840x2160 on maxed ultra settings, and even with a heavy ReShade filter enabled.
Even when in big battles with lots of particles, rain or snow, fog, and dozens of NPC's/machines I didn't notice any stuttering or hitching.

‚Ä¢ Game length:
Well, I just completed one single playthrough at nearly 250 hours, so yeah there's quite a lot to do. I was playing on ultra-hard and I do treat dying as a big deal, so I do play very slow and stealthy, if I get into serious trouble or realize I'm simply outgunned, I will run off and come back another time. Plus, as the world is so immersive and beautiful I do not fast travel.

If you prefer to run and gun, fast travel everywhere, and skip most of the peripheral and side quests, just blitzing through the main story I would say there is 30-hours of gameplay, but I highly recommend exploring and doing side quests as some of them are truly beautiful.

‚Ä¢ DLC (Frozen Wilds):
I was actually going to skip it, I'm so glad I didn't because it's actually really really good. New machines, a really good story, side quests, collectibles, weapons, and armor. I really highly recommend it.

‚ö†Ô∏èWARNING... I strongly suggest you play the Frozen Wilds DLC when you are around level 35-40 (you don't unlock it until level 30 anyway) and play through it before you beat the main game storyline. The story of the DLC overlaps with the main game storyline and mentions what's going on in the main game, so if you beat the main game first and then play the DLC the story might feel a little odd, some things might feel out the place.
Also... Be Prepared! The DLC is significantly more difficult as many players complained the main game is too easy, which it is in my opinion after the first few hours even on ultra-hard difficulty the main game is not challenging for experienced gamers, the DLC, however, is genuinely a challenge in places.
‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ

And finally, I massively encourage you to take your time and enjoy it, explore the whole map, seriously, it's beautifully laid out and designed you can tell a lot of time, effort, and love went into it, plus you will find lots of hidden resources, secrets, information, plus great stories and challenges.

I really do feel this is in my top 10 games of all time. Maybe it won't be for you but that's OK everyone is different, however, for me, it is truly one of the most heartwarming, immersive, captivating, and rich games I've played in my 30+ years of being a gamer.
Thank you to Sony for porting it to PC but a massive, gargantuan thank you to the dev team that clearly put the hearts into it.

Not Recommended
45.8 hrs on record
Posted: August 7, 2020
Incredible game I can finally recommend! Takes quite a bit of tinkering but an incredible play once/if you can manage to get it stable!

***09/13/2020 - Finally managed to get the game stable enough to enjoy on my RTX 2080 and AMD 3800x. Changed screen from a 4K 60 hz to a 1440p with Gsync. Game runs much better with Vsync disabled and FPS limit to unlimited.

Also set in Geforce Control Panel:
Max Frame Rate (slightly above your panel limit) - set mine to 150
Monitor Tech - G-sync Enabled
Power Management Mode - Prefer max performance
Preferred Refresh Rate - Highest Available
Threaded Optimization - SET ON (Game will crash on my cpu anyhow with it disabled or auto)
Vsync - Set to OFF

Performance TIPS:
START on the absolute lowest settings for your gpu and set your resolution to what your screen puts out. Up the settings one at a time until you find what causes the biggest frame drops on your hardware!
________________________________________________

**Below is the launch review

Runs like garbage on a RTX 2080 and 3800x. Obviously needs optimisation before they released it but they must've rushed the release date. Tons of frequent crashes leaves a bit to be desired. Hopefully they add DLSS 2.0 or release a patch soon cause playing on my system I should be getting better than 30-50 fps. Stuttery as hell too. Now negative aside it is an incredible game. Just can't recommend it until they fix the bugs with it. Even finding graphic glitches throughout the game as I play.(fixed by leaving Anisotropic filtering to - Application controlled).



***Update - So played with the settings and I just can't get it to run on anything smooth on 4k. However... turning down the resolution to 1440p with the settings below fixed it... kinda. Smooth enough now to play and enjoy although still quite stuttery sometimes. Game is still crashing frequently leaving it unplayable.

Full Screen Mode
Refresh Rate - 60 hz
Vsync - ON (I know people say to disable it but I HATE screen tearing)
FPS Limit - SET TO UNLIMITED

Graphics Settings:
Textures - Ultra
Models - Ultra
AA Filtering - Medium
Shadows - High
Reflections - Medium
Clouds - High
AA- SMAA
Motion blur - Off (does anyone even like it?)
Ambient Occlusion - Medium

Changing those settings for my RTX 2080 and Ryzen 3800x seems to be a nice medium. Give it a try and see if that works for you. 4K seems pretty buggy even with adaptive performance or render scale adjusted. Uses roughly about 55-70% of my GPU with those settings at 1440p. Crashes did NOT happen until about 2 hours in.

***08/08/2020 - Game is running decently on the settings listed above still but constantly crashing every 30-60 minutes... Simply unplayable trying to enjoy constantly worrying about when it'll crash again. "Unfortunately the game has crashed."

Horizon Zero Dawn is a must play game

I had already platinumed this game on PS4 when it originally released and it was one of my favourite games of the last generation of consoles. So with Forbidden West just about to release on PS5 I thought it was well worth another playthrough. Well the game is still amazing and even better on PC. Superb varied combat, an enthralling story, great characters (especially Aloy), great soundtrack and best of all the incredible world - there are a few minor flaws but over all Horizon Zero Dawn is a must play

PROS

- The story really is great, video game stories rarely have me hooked form start to finish. HZD has me fully invested.
- When I first heard of the game I thought the premise of robots in a post-apopolypic world sounded ridiculous, but I was so wrong, the world is incredible. Huge sense of scale.
- HZD is absolutely stunning to look at and it runs very well on my system
- Varied enemies, weapons and combat. There are so many robots, all with strengths and weaknesses and lots of different ways to tackle them
- The characters - Aloy and Sylens in particular are top tier
- The game respects your time - there are optional things to do but the game does not go overboard. Everything has a purpose, when you compare this to Ubisoft games, HZD is how to do open world games - varied and no bloat, Ubisoft is how not to.
- The game is a good length, around 40-50 hours to do everything is a perfect length for an open world game. This obsession with 100+ games needs to stop.
- Music and sound design is great

CONS

- Some side quests are a bit lame and the writing in them suffers when compared to the main quest
- Facial animations aren't bad, but can be off sometimes, especially the eyes
- I wish the facility locations you went in were a little more varied

OVERALL ‚Äì RECOMMENDED ‚Äì A must play for single player fans, this game excels in every area

Posted: June 3
(No Spoilers + TLDR at the end)

If you are the type of person who gets really into backstory and ‚Äòlore‚Äô then you will love this game. I was blown away by this element of the game and was not expecting things to unfold as they did. This game has some incredible mind-blowing reveals which shocked me and got me so much more engaged in the whole experience, there are dozens of diary entries and audio logs which really enhance the narrative and set the scene so well, I would highly recommend reading/listening to them all. I won‚Äôt go into details as I want to be spoiler free but specifically the reveals and details of Operation Enduring Victory and Operation Zero Dawn were incredible and were delivered masterfully, I was on the edge of my seat and HAD to know more and what happens next!

Graphically the game is incredible, one of the prettiest games I have ever played. The level of detail is wonderful even things that usually suffer like foliage look great, the weather effects and lighting are stunning enhancing every scene/ environment, the level of facial detail and animations are impeccable (especially with Aloy) I‚Äôm not sure I‚Äôve ever seen better in any other game. Truly a beautiful experience, I cannot wait to see how good the sequel will look on PC! It already looks insane on the PS5.

Combat focuses on working smarter not harder with targets having many specific weak spots such as gaps in Armor plating to pierce machines ‚Äòlungs‚Äô, going for the ‚Äòeyes‚Äô, casting ropes to trip large enemies, destroying mounted weapons on beasts etc. The ‚Äòelements‚Äô play a huge role too such as for example fire and ice being more effective against certain enemy types which really adds to the strategy of combat. Stealth works well too and was enjoyable, the mechanics for stealth are fairly barebones (crouch and hide in foliage) but it is a viable and recommended strategy especially on higher difficulties, mounting the machines and using them to traverse ground quicker and fight for you is pretty cool too. I must admit the human vs human combat is fairly bland unfortunately, it is very generic 3rd person shooter/action but the beast combat more than makes up for this negative in my opinion and the vast majority of the game is beast combat.

The most common complaint is definitely the idea of this game falling under the ‚ÄúUbisoft open world formula‚Äù which I completely disagree with. I have seen people say that Horizon: ZD is ‚Äújust Sci-Fi Assassin‚Äôs Creed‚Äù. For starters AC Origins and Odyssey were both great games and largely addressed the stagnation problems with the Assassins Creed series, people just love to hate circlejerk anything Ubisoft touch, but also just because a game is open world it is automatically trash to a certain group of people. This game‚Äôs world is engaging and interesting with huge differences in the game‚Äôs established cultures in different districts displayed through the environment but also through the different tribes and groups (E.g., the Nora villages differing greatly to the Meridian capital being more ‚Äòwild/savage‚Äô, differing to the mountain dwelling Banuk tribe ‚Äòembracing technology‚Äô more with their wire threading and views toward the beasts etc). Further the remnants of the ‚ÄúOld Ones‚Äù are really interesting and I loved coming across ruins of structures from the past and piecing together what they were e.g., ruins of a sports stadium. The world itself almost feels like a character at times, I don‚Äôt see how it can be seen as boring and formulaic at all. I will admit although I liked AC Odyssey it definitely had some padding and was way too big and directly suffered from that, H:ZD doesn‚Äôt suffer from this at all and there isn‚Äôt any (noticeable to me at least) ‚Äòcopy paste‚Äô content to make it seem bigger, everything has a purpose and flows well together.

The Frozen Wilds DLC (free and included with the game) was also brilliant. Following on from the main story (I think canonically just before the final battle iirc) it includes : a deeper look at the Banuk tribe, a vastly different environment (snow and ice), some great new characters, cool new powerful weaponry providing more of an ‚Äòend game‚Äô and of course new machines! It also expands upon many of the core elements of the main story too and gives more context, backstory and explanation behind some of the core events (trying to stay spoiler free). Definitely worth playing, was very fun and I imagine it heavily plays into the sequel.

I am really looking forward to the sequel hitting PC. I will 100% buy it Day 1, I loved this game and can‚Äôt wait to see what happens next in the story as well as see the improved new mechanics and new beasts!

TLDR: The game is fun for everyone, very solid smart fun combat and great graphics. If you are the type of person who gets really into detail and lore then you will get so much more out of this game and probably love it.

Recommended
55.5 hrs on record
Posted: April 16
I'm in two minds about Horizon Zero Dawn: on the one hand, I love the setting, the world building is great, a lot of love has obviously been put into the game. Fighting robot dinos is fun and varied. On the other hand, while the setting is unique, the game is conventional open world fare in many ways. Even if the fiction this is set in is very different from the Far Cries and Assassin's Creeds, you're still doing pretty much the same over and over again. Missions have a lot of thought put into the stories they tell, but the actual gameplay quickly becomes repetitive. And the story itself would've benefited from being told in a much tighter way. Nonetheless, if you're still in the market for open world games and you don't mind repeating the same kind of gameplay loops for 50+ hours, there's a lot to like here. I replayed this on PC after first playing it on PS4, and knowing what I'd enjoy and what I'd like less about the game made it easier to focus on the former. I'm glad I replayed it, but I also have to say that I'm glad to take a break from what is in the end a gorgeous, lovingly made but still, at its core, fairly conventional open world game.

MoonKnight
88 products in account
0
121 people found this review helpful
12 people found this review funny 12

Recommended
150.0 hrs on record
Posted: June 27, 2021
Finally, the day came, and so did I - Horizon Zero Dawn is available on PC. So let's see if saving myself for this long-awaited moment was worth it.

Interesting lore can't save bad writing
I don't understand why the main plot gets so much praise. It's a tired "You are the chosen one, save the world" plot.

Aloy was such a colossal letdown. She didn't face any hardship during my time with her and did no wrong, ever. There is no character arc; It's more of a character upwards line. Sprinkle in a little does of moral superiority, and we have a completely (un)relatable protagonist. She is essentially a one-dimensional Mary Sue who is the be-all and end-all.

Since the main plot is so uninteresting, one would hope that, at least, Aloy's friends are memorable. I can recall everyone from the Normandy's crew, Geralt's friends and my Grey Warden's companions. Here...I only remember one - Rost. He is the only one with some depth to his character, with a past shrouded in secrets. The rest just point you to the nearest place in need of your assistance and sing your praise. As a result, none of the emotional moments delivers, and not a single side character is memorable (except papa Rost).

Then there's the DLC. Although it doesn't add anything to Aloy's character, the plot and supporting cast are far superior to that of the base game. The conflict between the chieftain and shaman drives the story forward, rather than some generic villain. It's fleshed out, believable, and you understand both perspectives, so it's not as black and white as the base game story.

Same-same, but different...But still same
As a masochist, I chose Ultra Hard for my first playthrough. This difficulty introduces two new features - simultaneous enemy attacks and higher prices for items. As a result, you must carefully plan your attack, avoid wasting ammo and unnecessary conflicts. So, push it to the limit! and play New Game on Ultra Hard instead of "saving it" for New Game+. I say this because NG+ on UH is lacklustre for a simple reason - no enemy scaling. You have OP gear, but the enemies retain their NG health and damage. It seems Guerrilla Games devs need to attend an NG+ 101 course.

Now let's talk combat (*Spoiler* It's awesome). It focuses on figuring out your opponent's vulnerabilities and attack patterns. Each machine is weak and resistant to different types of elemental damage, such as fire, freeze, corruption, or shock, so it's always a good idea to first scan them with Aloy's focus. Not only that, but they also have weak spots you can target for massive damage. Some are exposed, while others have a strong shell guarding them. Enter tear damage. It can tear the machine's armour clean off. But wait, there's more! Machines also have external components (guns, fire tanks, etc.) that allow them to use specific attacks. By removing these components with tear arrows, you also eliminate attacks tied to those components from the enemy's repertoire.


Could probably rack up another 150h by just exploring this beautiful world and "playing" with its wildlife 
Community Created Artwork for Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Sv. Prolivije
Shoutout to my brazilian boah DRo for helping me, after my GPU went to greener pastures, by capturing the second gameplay part


From bows, traps to slingshots, and icicle canons, there are plenty of tools at your disposal, each excelling in a specific situation. Do you need a machine immobilized? Use the rope caster. Does the enemy have a fire canister exposed? Set them ablaze with a fire arrow. For any problem, there is always a solution. And now, the best part - gear has fixed stats. There is no difference in damage between a tier 1 bow and a tier 3 bow. But, it does have more arrow types and more mod slots. This is why the better gear is, well, better. Getting better gear felt like I became a slightly more capable hunter, as it provides more options for dealing with enemies. Maybe set them ablaze? Tear off their armour first and expose their weak spots? Or corrupt them and cause distress among their ranks. The DLC also adds tier 4 weapons, but instead of new arrow types, they have a slight damage boost.

The RPG stuff it's pretty much just "higher number wins" and dull resource management. The skill tree also could use some work. It only adds two new gameplay changes, with the rest being stat boosts. Still, they did make the gameplay fun and engaging even after 100 hours. Slow-motion was unquestionably the best. Harnessing the 4000-year-old teachings of Max Payne, you'll glide through the air, delivering critical hits while looking fabulous. Melee combat and stealth are present and pretty basic. Overall, the AI is good; humans behave like humans, so expect some dumb decisions from time to time, with the machines following a pre-established path.


Photo Mode + Bugs = hours of fun 
Community Created Artwork for Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Sv. Prolivije


Surprisingly, the game isn't bloated with copy-pasted side-content, so they never felt tedious. The cauldrons were the best of the lot. They mix platforming and combat with a very nifty reward at the end - a new tier of machines to hack. Other side activities include clearing enemy camps, climbing vantage points, as well as Hunters Lodge trails. I loved these trails, as they offer a nice challenge, requiring you to use a specific weapon to eliminate machines in a particular manner as quickly as possible.

However, there are a couple of issues. The parkour can be iffy at times, and jumping onto specific ledges requires a prayer beforehand. Riding "horses" was fine when taking in the scenery, but as soon as they start galloping, tank mode initiates. As a result, my Aloy became a marathoner, and quite a decent one.

"Sorry, my face is tired"
Without a doubt, one of the most beautiful open-world games I've ever played. You already know what to expect in terms of biomes - desert, snowy areas, some mountain underpasses and jungles. But still, all of the locations you visit exude love and great care that went into breathing life to them. The creative vision behind each tribes design was also excellent. They all felt unique and have an intriguing backstory for their design choice. I especially loved the Banuk shamans, who had blue, glowing, wires threaded through their skin. Looks weird and cool at the same time.


The world of Horizon Zero Dawns is simply stunning 
Community Created Artwork for Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Sv. Prolivije


The machines are highly detailed and have an animal-like appearance. I loved getting close-up and personal, so I could admire all their tiny nuts and bolts. Their sound design was also outstanding. Each step they make emits a distinct SFX, which plays a crucial role in letting you know when ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• is about to go down. Add to that how information about machines is conveyed visually, and playing this with HUD completely off was pure heaven. Also, I just want to take this moment to thank my former GPU, the GTX 970, for providing me with a stable 30fps, with mostly high settings, on an ultrawide 1080p monitor.
You da real MVP.

But...there are problems. The base game has bad lip-synching and an all-in-your-face camera, strange face and brow twitching, lifeless eyes, and stiff characters during conversations. But, the facial animations...my god, the facial animations. They can occasionally exceed even the legendary ones from Mass Effect Andromeda. The DLC did fix these issues; the camera is moved further back, characters now move while talking, lip-synching is better and facial expressions are greatly improved.

Final Thoughts
So, was my 4-year abstinence worthwhile? Kinda. The main plot, characters, and Aloy were all disappointing. But I just couldn't put my controller down thanks to its engaging combat and serene experience while exploring the world. So if all of those nice things tickle your fancy, Horizon Zero Dawn should already be in your cart.

If you enjoyed this review, come and read more wisdom from the Gospel of Sv. Prolivije.
 

Sv. Prolivije

Okay, the game is undoubtedly great, it looks beautiful even in Medium aka Original PS4 graphic settings but the real issue lies here with the optimization, it's very poor. Starting with Clouds, the ultra just trashes your FPS. The texture filtering is weird, seems not working as mentioned by Digital Foundry. Most of the issues has been covered by them and I'm using their optimized settings for better performance with less to none visual forfeit. But the stuttering here and there just makes this a real bad experience. The in-game benchmark tool is garbage, so far what I've played the benchmark tool stats has no relevance with real performance. Needs some serious patches, there's tons of issues to fix. If you can wait, I'd recommend you to do so until patches deal with this issues to have an utmost experience.

Optimized settings:-
Texture: Ultra
Model: Ultra
Anisotropic Filtering: 16x from Nvidia control panel (All in-game settings broken atm)** [Update: Forcing x16 causing weird artifacts issue sometimes, turning that off fixed the problem]
Shadows: High (Medium looks nice too, ultra is not worth it for the FPS hit)
Reflection: Medium (High has a major performance hit)
Clouds: High (Ultra decimates FPS)
AA: TAA
Motion Blur: Off (Personal preference, not my cup of tea)
Ambient Occlusion: Medium (This seems broken too, Ultra looks more awful)

TLDR: Performance wise Not recommended at current state.

Will update the review once this issues are being fixed.

Posted: February 28, 2021
So, Horizon Zero Dawn was an experience. I initially bought it when it came out on PC because it had cool robot-dinosaurs, and I'm all for both robots and dinosaurs. Turns out, upon playing it, it's an absolutely fantastic game.
The major plusses for me, as an experienced RPG player:
- The story is incredible. The main story is perfectly written, the details of the world tie in extremely well with the storyline (what the robots are for, how each works, etc), and the stories told by the collectibles is just as great. I genuinely shed a tear at the end of the story shared by the Vantage Points collectibles.
- The gameplay is on point. Combat is very dynamic, and offers multiple ways to face the danger.
- Visually, the game is a journey. It's a mix of both stunning graphics, and lore taught through design. The machines design, the outfit design, the environment design. All of it makes sense, and is absolutely delightful to wander through.
- The size of the world is on point. Yes, it's open a free to explore. But they also made it so that it feels large enough while being rather small and dense.

I'll point out a downside that I met while playing, the difficulty doesn't scale well with New Game+. I finished a run in Normal difficulty (albeit finished it at 100%, platinumed and all) but the New Game+ run in Ultra Hard difficulty was... Not specifically challenging. I will however say that that second run took me about 5 to 6 hours, I believe, and I have played a total of about 82 hours to finish the game and DLC at 100%, gather all collectibles, and finish all Steam achievements. If you plan on finishing it, it's pretty great value for the money.

My advice: get this game. It's a gem.

Posted: August 15, 2020
I bought it despite of the on going issues. So far I have not encountered any unplayable stuttering, or significant FPS drops. The only issue I have been seeing is that cutscenes lose audio. I feel sorry for those who have a lot of performance issues. I am not trying to downplay those problems, but I've seen that it really depends on your components. There are people trying to play this with a GTX 1070 at 1440p, expecting to get 100 fps, but that's just unrealistic. Others make it sound like their game is unplayable, period. But they don't really offer any context. So I'd take that with a grain of salt.

Just for reference, I'm running a RTX 2070 Super, and a Ryzen 7 3700x. I play at 1440p, and the FPS does not go below 60fps, though it lingers between 65-75. Truth is: the game is not well optimized because a 2070 Super should handle 100+ FPS. However, it is very much playable at 60fps, especially if you have a 4k TV 60hz. I keep it at 1080p since I dont see any major differences between 1080p and higher resolutions. That's just me.

As far as the game itself, I had gotten its platinum on PS4, and there are far better reviews out there. This game should've been released on PC during its launch. This game was meant for higher frames, and not the horrific 30fps on PS4, and especially not the 60fps with extremely low textures and dynamic resolution on the Pro version. This game was meant for the master race.

Recommended

Posted: August 8, 2020
Horizon Zero Dawn is one of the few PS4 exclusive games that I've ever "envied" our console cousins for having, since I was attracted by both its looks and story.
However, I have to say that I have a bitter taste in my mouth, because the PC port isn't as polished as I expected it to be.

Right from the start, we stumble upon an optimization screen that can take over 10-15 minutes to complete, depending on your system (in my case it was relatively quick, but I've read tons of reports from other users who had to wait for quite a while for it to complete).
After sitting there waiting for the automatic optimization,
I went into the options menu to adjust settings to my liking, and while I got a decently performing game after that, I have to say that there are still small drops here and there (stuttering), that, while not making the game unplayable, as I'm always over the cherished 60FPS mark, they are noticeable.
The game's mouse and keyboard support seems to be good, though I personally prefer to play with a controller in this particular case.

To sum up, I believe that the game has a lot to offer thanks to its hunting/collection systems, and I hope that the developers will update the game to improve performance.

Posted: June 30
Horizon Zero Dawn is a captivating post-apocalyptic story centered around the adventures of Aloy as she searches for answers concerning her origins & past events while preventing a rogue AI known as "Hades" from using a malicious ancient horde of robots to destroy all life on the planet. Aloy's fierce beauty, lethal skills & witty charm definitely makes her one of the greatest female video-game heroines of all time.

Pros:
+Excellent Story: The story does an excellent job portraying humanity's struggle for survival in a post-apocalyptic dystopian world overrun with machines. The emotional events of the past, their relation to Aloy's origin & her importance in saving the world are masterfully revealed as Aloy progresses in her journey.
+Excellent Graphics: The many unique landscapes, settlements, wildlife & machines which make up this post-apocalyptic world are all beautifully rendered & feels alive, creating some of the most gorgeous scenery in gaming.
+Great Combat: The combat makes great use of Aloy's range of skills & weapons. Combat feels fluid when taking on large menacing machines or human enemies. Aloy's range of projectile weapons, traps & armor can be used to take advantage of enemy weaknesses to lethal effect.
+Great Controls: The controls are precise & responsive when traversing the in-game environment or in combat further complementing gameplay.
+Great Soundtrack: The somber soundtrack definitely complements the post-apocalyptic look & feel of the game, adding to its depth & emotion while exploring the open world on your mount or fighting angry machines.

Cons:
-Some of the side missions follow the same routine pattern which may get repetitive after some time.
-Certain areas of the map are too densely populated with machines which may lead to many unnecessarily hostile interactions which can become annoying especially when just exploring.

Recommended
46.0 hrs on record
Posted: August 10, 2020
Never touched this game on the PlayStation, therefore this review will be as genuine as it can get. This is also my first time playing a Guerrilla dev game.

Performance:
On its own, the game runs absolutely great. I have followed multiple complaints regarding the PC port, but I haven't experienced a SINGLE issue running the game with a 1080 TI at full ULTRA with all possible settings maxed out. FPS is at a stable 80-90, with an occasional (and I mean, ONCE since I started the playthrough) dip under 60, during a clusterf*ck of fire particles caused by a less than successful hunt of a Trampler herd (I play on Ultra Hard, and it's extremely punishing). If I were to be pedantic and pick at every visual and performance aspect - I would only wish the HD textures were worked a little better on PC. Photo mode blurs everything on close-up.

Gameplay: Overall, very fluid and fun. Combat extremely rewarding and punishing on higher difficulties.
Not a huge fan of the fact that all the weapons and armor I have encountered so far needed to be purchased. Would be cool to have some of these looted from machine carcasses and/or lootboxes.
Huge issue with human head hitboxes - arrows sometimes fly through the side of the mask or don't register the hit. I hope a fix will come soon. Don't know if it's the same on the Play Station.

Story:
Aloy is a cool protagonist as they come - very sure of herself - gives off a bit of a Wonderwoman/Brave had a weird baby. Cool as main characters come.
Support characters are bland and voice acting is half-assed.

TLDR:
Pros:
Looks and runs beautifully (Nvidia GeForce 1080ti 11gb)
Stable FPS
Fantastic and rewarding Combat

Cons:
Head hitboxes...
Support characters and voice acting are lame
Seems like a percentage of PC players have tons of problems and some don't.

I hope that most of the PC player base will be able to have a pretty much flawless performance experience after a patch or two!

To keep this short & sweet, I was very pleased to see this make its way to PC and have had a blast playing through both the game and its expansion. What I want to specifically pin point are the fighting mechanics - they're simply outstanding. Horizon enables you to methodically take down a range of machines through various weaponry - planning, crafting and executing your plans to fruition. It is some of the most satisfying combat I've ever had. Ripping machines apart bit by bit (with shrapnel/armour/parts flying all over the place), exposing their weaknesses and trapping them.. very satisfying and very rewarding. Corrupted machines (base game) and Daemonic machines in particular (dlc) provide excellent opportunities for you to hone your skills later on in the game.

The rich environment and sound quality throughout have been nothing short of exceptional. I am not one to revisit games after completion but this has been so good, that I'm sure it will tempt me. In the mean time, I will be impatiently waiting for Horizon Forbidden West.

I just haven't experienced anything that is particularly memorable or awe-inspiring, and that is really what I need from a gaming experience at my age.

The story just isn't crafted as well as I think it could have been. I like a story that keeps me thinking, guessing, and coming back for more. In the 8 hours I've played Horizon, it hasn't managed to do any of those things.

It is tough for me to say that I don't recommend this game, because I have no doubt that a lot of people will (and clearly do) love it. But speaking as a middle-age man nearing 40, I can't recommend it. I've played several games in the last few years alone that have managed to blow me away. So I know they are out there, this just isn't one of them.

However, since I take my time playing and I enjoy the world, I don't mind running there on my mount. I do play on Normal because I like to enjoy myself without being too easy. Enjoyable game, enjoyable experience, one of the few games I am actually trying to play through from start to finish.

I've bought this upon release mainly to support Playstation Games on STEAM so we can see more from this coming to PC via Steam. I was getting told that this Game is a Gem so I've tried it myself and Spoiler alert: They were right holy

First things first - My Specs:

i9 9900k
RTX 2080Ti
32GB DDR4 RAM
Installed on an SSD

Runs smooth on 1440p with 70-100 FPS on my 144hz Monitor.

TL;DR at the bottom:

The story grips you right out of the gate. Storylines have always been convoluted in open world games because of how sidetracked the player can get with other tasks and side quests. I was level 43 when I had main story quests for level 17 lmao. While this does have side quests, they can be resolved relatively quickly (though at the expense of character depth in side quest givers, but that's not necessarily a bad thing).

There isn't much that can be said about the graphics that haven't been said already. This is probably the only game out so far that wanted me to get a PS4 Pro, but it isn't necessary anymore since its on STEAM. The environments are incredibly detailed and the lightning is outstanding - for example:


Amazing! 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: Saibot


What really makes this game stand out above many others in its genre is the crafting system. I am tired of crafting systems that feel like a chore, to where it's impossible to craft something useful without going well out of your way to gather the components. It turns crafting into some side quest time sink. Horizon eliminates all of that. I've continued to be able to craft anything I need with just items I collect on my routes through the story. No hours spent farming materials just so I don't run short on supplies further along, THIS IS WHAT QUALITY OF LIFE IS ABOUT FOLKS! It's still a diverse crafting system with many options.

The UI is crystal clear (You can also edit the Screen UI size), the menu system is perfectly organized, and everything seems to have just the right depth. I'm convinced that Horizon was the product of meticulously analyzing its predecessors and pinpointing what works really well and what didn't work so well, and perfecting nearly everything.

Anyone saying this is just another Far Cry Primal has the analytical abilities of a toddler. This is more like Witcher 3's kid sister, and she is a total badass.

Horizon Zero Dawn is a perfect proof, that if you give developers creative freedom and time, it will get you a sweet reward. For fans of action adventures and wonderful worlds Horizon is the obvious choice.


What a beautiful Game!

I haven't finished yet, but the story line is pretty good. In game action is way intense. I'm pretty sure I have forgotten to blink for several minutes at a time during battles with some new robot.
There are places to farm for materials and exp as well.
There are plenty of side quests.
The only negative I really have on this game is this: Sometimes, when hiding in the grass so the robots can't see you, you start to aim and suddenly can't see squat because there is a blade of grass or a branch taking up the whole screen.
But that's it. That's the only bad.
Traps are super important. Like really, really, really important. So get good at using them.
This game is what people wished Monster Hunter World had been.
