Recommended
61.1 hrs on record
Posted: September 5
I have been trying to figure out how to write this review for a few years. I first played this game on my PS4, and fell completely in love with it. The story is one of the best for an RPG I've played in a good many years and the worst part of the game was having to see the end, but... with that said, it did leave open the possibility of a sequel, which later was made, so the sadness turned to unbridled joy, until I found out it was going to be a playstation exclusive, when my joy was shattered. I refused to upgrade to a PS5 due to pricing issues and the fact that I was sick of Sony making us pay for the same games we already bought over and over again for newer consoles. Anyway, enough of my sony-bashing, back to the review!

The story starts out with a mystery. The young woman you play is an outcast, with a mysterious origin, you learn through the later story. You play in a world where there are remnants of the modern world, left in ruins, abandoned, and scrapped, with various tribes and sects that seem primitive by modern standards. To top off this weirdness, you encounter, fight, "Tame" and scavenge robotic animals, some that resemble well known creatures, others that seem to be hybrids or plays on well known creatures and you learn what they are for and why they are there.

You can complete trials, collections, and other types of side-quests that give you more powerful weapons and equipment, and scattered throughout the world are fragments of the past that help you understand what happened to the world and why it is the way it is now. The characters are interesting, the story is mind-blowing, and graphically speaking, the game is very visually appealing. I have played this game through to completion a half a dozen times, enjoyed completing all the achievements on the PS4 and have been working on completing them again on the PC.

For an indie company based in the Netherlands, they made a dynamite game, it's just a shame they went Sony Exclusive with the sequel. It was devastating to find this out and made me even more jaded toward Sony, as I feel they robbed millions of the chance to further enjoy this world and the characters we've come to love and care about. Hopefully, if a few years this exclusivity will end and it will eventually have the sequel available for the PC, at which time, I will dust off Horizon Zero Dawn once again and enjoy it all over again, before falling in love with the sequel!

If you love RPG's, don't mind a lack of character creation and limited customization of weapons and armor, more of a Static RPG, but with an amazing story and fun combat, beautiful graphics, and rich, intriguing characters, I think you will love this game and encourage you strongly to give it a chance. If you are put off by the sequel being console exclusive, I feel your pain, but I will say this game by itself is worth getting and playing or replaying again.

Recommended
117.0 hrs on record
Posted: October 14, 2021
Horizon Zero Dawn is set in a post-apocalyptic world in the near future where humanity has been able to master advanced technology such as robotics. However, some unknown disaster caused the end of civilization and humans went back to primitive tribes. Fortunately, they managed to maintain some use of advanced technologies thanks to the old civilizations, which were destroyed. While the robotic dinosaurs have become the dominant species, both have been able to live together peacefully, that is until a new phenomenon called The Derangement started to make the robotic creatures more aggressive.

You play as Aloy, an outcast from birth for reasons that she does not know. She was put into the care of another outcast named Rost by the Nora Matriarchs. As an outcast Aloy is shunned by the other members of the Nora tribe, a fact perpetuated due to it literally being outlawed by the group. As a child Aloy wants to find out who her mother was and why she was cast out, so she teams up with Rost to get her training montage on so she can enter a competition called The Proving. The winner of The Proving receives the right to ask the Nora Matriarchs anything they wish. While I don‚Äôt want to say much more than the basics, Horizon Zero Dawn has one of the best stories in years that I have seen. It‚Äôs supremely intriguing and made me want to find out what happened to the old civilizations and why Aloy was cast out. Running all those ruins of old world and collecting every bit of information about them i could find was so addictive. The only other RPG I have thought this highly of the story was The Witcher 3. Even the side quests in Horizon I have enjoyed, and while they don‚Äôt matter as much as in The Witcher 3, they are still a big part of the game.

Horizon Zero Dawn is an open world RPG, and its also the best open world RPG I have played when it comes to its gameplay which is fast, fluid and incredibly fun. Using an old-world tool called a Focus, Aloy can see past the gnashing metal jaws of machines and at their components ‚Äì specifically their weak spots and vulnerabilities. Every enemy has one, you can strike with a fire arrow to cause an explosion, an exposed battery shoot with an electric arrow can stun the creature. Knowing these weaknesses is key to battle especially on higher difficulties. The game offers also large set of tools starting from different kind of bows, traps, bombs, guns to tear apart metal parts and line launchers which can be used to pin enemy to the ground preventing it from moving. Some of the weapons can deal multiple types of damage and can be additionaly upgraded to boost specific type. We can have for example bow designed for physical damage, fire damage etc. All this give us freedom to approach every battle with multiple ways.

The game is huge, with a sprawling map that covers miles of land across various environments, from forests to frozen steppes to deserts. Thanks to the inclusion of The Frozen Wilds DLC, Horizon Zero Dawn: Complete Edition is larger than the original game, with a frosty region added to the map that becomes accessible partway through the game. It‚Äôs nicely dense, filled with settlements, ruins, machine grazing areas, and bandit camps you can explore on your own or jump between while performing quests. Presented in spectacular immersive graphic, atmospheric music and brathtaking views will give you unforgetable experience.

Horizon Zero Dawn is nothing short of a masterpiece. Absolute must to play for RPG fun.

Recommended
137.6 hrs on record
Posted: September 6, 2020
*Edited*

Exclusives
Bad Console Ports
Crashes

Anyone who's a gamer *HATES* those three words & what they mean for us all. The fact that HZD was *ONLY* available on consoles originally was *DEEPLY* disappointing. Sorry Sony, I will never buy a Playstation. Not going to happen. I'm a gamer on PC only. PC's are my weapon of choice and that's not going to change anytime soon. There's a substantial segment of the market just like me - so cut us out if you want, but accept what you lose by doing that.

Horizon: Zero Dawn *is* a great game. It really is. One of the classics I'm going to say. However, the game was NOT tested properly before release. Likely, a release deadline had to be hit - and that deadline arrived before the porting team were ready. Upon the PC release, the game crashed regularly for many people, and many also reported performance issues with stuttering and nasty slowdowns as the game loaded assets in intensive areas. Now however, most crashes seem fixed, although the odd one *does* still occur. Updating to Windows 10 Build 2004 and enabling the GPU optimisation setting did the trick for me. Until that gem surfaced - I crashed a *LOT*. I run a Gigabyte 1080TI.

The game itself has a decent storyline. This world where a modern time is years in the past - with decaying remnants of that time scattered all over the place is a compelling narrative. What happened? What are those animal machines? Just who IS Aloy?? It just cements the importance of good writing and plot lines into games. Not all agree if you read many forums - but that's ok. Game production is an art, and you don't always like every piece in the gallery. I found myself wanting to unlock Aloy's story and that of the world around her more and more as the game went on, which I admit is a relatively rare thing these days in PC gaming. High end visuals can only go so far if the story is dead boring.

Free exploration is always good. That feeling of true freedom is just great, and this game I feel hits that mark pretty well. The world is open and I can go where I want without feeling forced or funnelled into it. Invisible walls do exist, but are rare. Hidden pockets abound, which is great stuff.

The fighting mechanincs seem ok to me. Learn to dodge and *when* to dodge and you'll be ok. Keep on top of weapon upgrades and you just may live to see another day. Not too hard - not too easy. Fights are rewarding. That said - I often find normal mode a challenge in a lot of games. Gears 5 for example - I found run of the mill mode in that quite a challenge. I will also say that later in HZD, I've found the fights a little easier against the various common machines. In a way that's nice, but does start to feel old. Same old machines for same old reward.

Definitely worth a play.

Posted: August 8, 2020
After several crashes, restarts and tweaks I finally got the game to run on my 1080Ti, i7 7700 and 16GB of RAM, however the game still has issues. 4K is a no go on my rig which is sad because this is a game that ran at 4K (checkerboard 4K but still) on much much weaker hardware.

Even at 1440p I am still only getting around 50-60FPS and at best 70 FPS at a mix of medium/high settings (with minimal gains even when i turn down to on par or lower than console settings which defeats the purpose of a PC port). but there is a really alarming amount of stutter that occurs during gameplay, cutscenes. The stutter is especially bad when when the cutscenes begin and end. Some graphical features like anisotropic filtering don't even work at all, forcing you to apply it in your control panel to get it to work in the game.

My peers who have even stronger rigs are experiencing similar results or even worse than mine. Weird flickering and graphical glitches plagued the beginning area. Some cutscenes and character/environment animations are locked at 30FPS which looks weird when the rest of the game is at a higher framerate. The list goes on and on.

TLDR: This is a very beautiful game that has a ton of potential to really shine on PC at max settings and maybe mods in the future will make it look even better and provide more content to keep it alive for years to come. But we can't get to that point when the base port of this game was done with seemingly little to no care at all. I cannot recommend this game in it's current state. Will check back after some patches.

Regardless, I really enjoy playing Horizon Zero Dawn. The visual is stunning, the story is intriguing. And the combat system is rather simple, but still can be very fun because of how well made the enemies are. Now about performance issue, I only experienced framerate drop when entering settlement area. Even then it's just for a brief of time and doesn't really affect the gameplay that much.
In conclusion, for the price I think this game is worth to buy.

Milk or Be Milked

187 people found this review helpful
19 people found this review funny 20

Recommended
7.7 hrs on record
Posted: August 7, 2020
Product received for free

Oh boy. Horizon: Zero Dawn is a fantastic game, and the Complete Edition is a great deal. Together with the included DLC the Complete Edition offers dozens and dozens of hours of really good open world Monster Hunter-esque robot hunting and gathering. One of my favourite games of the current generation, and as a GAME a very easy and very big recommendation. However -- and this is a pretty big however: the PC version isn't great.

On my system (Core i7-8700, RTX 2080 Super, 32 gigs of DDR4-3200MHz and a Samsung 970 EVO Plus) the game theoretically runs well. On 1440p at the game's auto-detected "prefer quality" settings it runs at a fairly solid 60-70 FPS. This is of course a lot less than in Death Stranding (a game that kind of runs on the same engine), which easily maintains a solid 150FPS at maximum details and a lot less than I was hoping for. But hey, 60-70 FPS is still pretty good, right? Well, yes and no.

While the framerate is technically decent, the game has constant and very irritating stuttering. Sometimes it's micro-stuttering, other times it's macro stuttering. The animations often look weird and the whole game has this very awkward stuttering feel to it. This doesn't outright RUIN the game, because you can still play it just fine. I was delighted to find out that the game of course works just fine on a controller, but also on a mouse and keyboard. I was really missing the precision of mouse aiming on the PS4 original, so this is a very welcome discovery.

So would I recommend Horizon: Zero Dawn? Yes and no. As a game, absolutely. It's still an excellent and very modern open world game with a good story, an engaging world and tons of very entertaining gameplay. But this PC conversion isn't good. It's borderline bad. I of course have every hope that the dev team keeps updating the game to patch out the performance issues, but come on, guys: how the hell did the game even launch in this state to begin with? The game is still playable, but the PC port is overall far rougher than you'd hope for, so whether or not that is something you want to support with your money is up to you.

For me, the game itself is still good enough to make dealing with the technical issues worthwhile.

FaithCzech‚Ñ¢
4,532 products in account
0
376 people found this review helpful
45 people found this review funny 36

Not Recommended
64.2 hrs on record
Posted: January 9, 2021
I'll start off by saying that I played through it entire and ended up getting 100% completion in 60ish hours
I picked the game up on the last winter sale and managed to play through it entirely so I can't say I didn't get my money's worth out of it
With that being said, I'm not so sure that I'd really "recommend" this to anybody... That's not to say it's a bad game, I didn't think it was "bad" and I'll hopefully be able to explain that a bit

To start with the good, I think the world that this game has is phenomenal. I'm a sucker for post-apocalyptic environments and I think the world itself is designed really well. I found myself using the photo mode a lot and I normally never touch it but some of the area's are just beautiful. I spent a lot of time running around just picking up everything I could because I'm a loot hoarder.
The Machine creatures are also pretty interesting to me, I thought it was a nice twist instead of having just normal dinosaurs or whatever.
The combat was probably the one and only thing that kept me playing throughout the entire time. I ended up playing through on ultra hard mode and considering you could get pretty much one shot, you had to really focus on hitting each machines weak points and using the right equipment to take them down. I thought it was pretty enjoyable, even if frustrating sometimes but that was probably just down to me enjoying the spear more than the bow. I remember reading that people thought the Thunderjaw was the hardest enemy in the game, I didn't think this was the case. Those damned glint hawks and Stormbird thing were an absolute nightmare for me.

Unfortunately, that's where the "good" really ends for me.

I picked the game up because I was looking for a pretty heavy story focused game to sink some time into... Considering it was nominated for story rich game in the 2020 Steam Awards, I figured it had a pretty good shot to be exactly what I was looking for. I didn't end up enjoying it like most, if not all of the positive reviews say.
I can't tell if I played through the game "wrong" or what, but I ended up doing what I do in most games with questing, and that is go to a new town/area, completing all the side quests for that area and then moving on to the next area with the main storyline. I ended up over-leveling the main storyline quest by like 30 levels, even though the levels don't really have any impact on the game (as far as I could tell anyway)

To start with the main story (spoiler free), I was pretty bored by the time I really "started getting into it". I wanted to learn more about the machines but I wasn't invested in *any* of the characters the game had to offer, aside from the first one you meet and then the character named "Sylense", and that was just because I recognized the VA from his other work/games.
I felt like most, if not all of the characters I met were pretty lifeless and uninteresting. Aloy, the character you play as had a good voice to her but her facial expressions/eyes didn't match what the energy of her voice was giving off.
The first 10 hours I was in the game I didn't have any issues with this, about 10/15hrs in I started to noticing long gaps in dialog during cutscenes (like a full second or two where both the people were just staring at each other instead of talking) and it just seemed really awkward and almost unfinished. I also saw some cutscenes where the characters in the scene were essentially teleporting between transitions like a jump cut... I wasn't really happy seeing this considering the animations and stuff were really good and then all of a sudden the characters were jumping around... Just seemed kind of lame but I'm sure most people just look past this kind of thing.
I was pretty surprised that a lot of people, if not most, praise the story of this game but maybe that just comes down to a me thing.

Moving onto the other questlines-

I spent the first 40 hours of my time in the game completing all of the side quests that I had come across and I was about ready to just give up and uninstall the game just due to how repetitive they are. The characters you meet have almost no significance to anything that happens in the game (aside from maybe a couple) and the side quests/errands are almost all the same layout.

> New NPC with quest > lost item/person > go to where it/they were last seen > follow tracks/examine blood/item > find person or item/fight machine for item > backtrack to original NPC

I know most games with a side questline aren't the most interesting but it just felt like such a chore to keep doing when it had no impact on the game at the end of the playthrough. I think in total for the main story there's only like 20 missions? The side stuff just seemed completely pointless to do unless you were going for a 100% completion... but I suppose that's kind of the point? I don't know. I just wasn't happy having to do the same almost brainless task of following tracks and pressing "e" on the item to "examine" it and then just be done and only getting a few shards as rewards. Eventually during the DLC area you do come across an NPC with some side quests that offers to upgrade your weapons and I feel like even that would have made them less annoying and more rewarding if they were in the base game.

Moving away from the story elements to try and wrap it up a bit

When you learn how to override the machines to use them against other machines, I was super hyped because this meant you were able to use them as mounts to move about the pretty large world. That was almost immediately shattered for me. I don't know if it's a keyboard/mouse issue, but the mounts felt SUPER clunky the entire time to where I pretty much opted to do the entire game on foot. They would randomly stray from going in a straight line and suddenly start jumping over objects and rocks that I wasn't even really near. Going up even some of the smallest hills that, you, as the character, could walk up just fine, the mounts just wouldn't walk up at all.

Hunter's Lodge challenges..... I might be the only one that thinks this, maybe not... These were the most annoying things in the entire game. The only real reason they're "challenging" is down to the utterly ridiculous short timer that they throw at you to increase the difficulty to get the golden box rewards. I had the most frustrations in the entire game just trying to get these out of the way. The rewards should have been a lot better, at least for the first time you get the blazing sun box. I wouldn't mind if you got the current rewards you get now if you just kept on repeating them, but I normally spent more than I got back trying to attempt the challenges that I failed over and over again. Some of them were a little too easy, some of them were a nightmare and made me want to pull my hair out.

This is starting to get pretty long and I feel a little bad since just from a glance, the bad stuff (imo) kind of overpowers the good but honestly, I don't really have much good to say other than the world/machines designs. If you've read this far, great. I hope I explained it good enough, if not oh well. I tried. If you're anything like me and enjoy post-apocalyptic worlds to explore, you might find something with this but otherwise I couldn't really say that I think it's worth getting. Nothing else really kept me other than the world and combat.

> TLDR

World Design, good, very beautiful
Characters/expressions seem lifeless and uninteresting
Story wasn't all that captivating for me
Side quests were extremely boring and most had no effect on the end game story
Mounts were extremely clunky
Hunter's Lodge Challenges were extremely annoying and felt unrewarding

I hope to see things I mentioned improved in a second game, assuming they decide to make one. Even though most of the is negative points, it was no means a "bad" game. I at least managed to get my money's worth out of it.

TIL steam has a review character limit....

I really want to recommend this game. I do. It is an absolute masterpiece and I loved playing it‚Ä¶ on the PS4. The stuttering, the huge 20-30fps drops in places, the nearly 15 minutes you have to wait for shaders to load EVERY TIME YOU START THE GAME. It‚Äôs a mess. Now, will I remove my review if the Devs fix these issues? Absolutely. That hand will flip to a thumbs up and I will get to write a review about the gameplay itself. But, as it stands, you might be better off picking this game up on the PS4/5. And that pains me to say as a proud member of PCMR.

--Edit as of 11/27/20--
The dev is proving to be committed to this game and is patching it at a fast pace. Some issues have been fixed but many more remain. FPS is still very jittery and can rip you right out of the experience. While there is improvement, it might be many more months till this is what I consider playable.

--Edit as of 12/04/20--
I have 100% this game now, and let me tell you it was much easier on the PS4. The game would crash at the worst times and the frame lag would make some battles more about where could I lure the enemy where I could get a smoother framerate rather than just trying to take down the enemy. A 40+ frame drop at the wrong time could mean having to reload a save.

--Edit as of 12/12/20--
For the record, my rig doesn't even have integrated graphics (for the person that asked) and drivers are up to date. This isn't my first rodeo and I have been building/repairing/maintaining PC's for over 25 years now. I am not an idiot with a 'gaming craptop' that doesn't understand the capabilities of my machine and how games should run on it. --Edit as of 4/5/21--

Tabajara
494 products in account
0
135 people found this review helpful
7 people found this review funny 28

Recommended
75.4 hrs on record
Posted: August 7, 2020
Information

Horizon Zero Dawn ‚Ñ¢ Complete Edition is an Action / RPG developed by Guerrilla. First of all, it should be mentioned that most of the negative Reviews about the game have to do with hardware problems, but I cannot share their opinion, as I haven't had a single game crash or any other problem in my playing time so far.

System

CPU: Intel Core I7-8700K
GPU: GeForce GTX 1070ti
RAM: 16 GB DDR4

Gameplay

Back then I had traveled the gaming world with Aloy on PS4 for more than 60 hours and had reached player level 57. I played through both the main game and the expansion "The Frozen Wilds". However, this game really fascinated me. Unlike in many other reviews, I don't want to give a single rating for story, graphics, audio, control, but rather combine these elements. After all, who can help "5 * graphics" when an overall package of games is bad? I will not give any story spoilers and I will be reluctant to comment on the game world.
First of all, I would like to note that the game designers certainly used a best-of from games like "Tomb Raider", "Skyrim", "Mass Effect" and "Assassins Creed". This applies to perspectives and camera work, effects, controls, elements of the narrative, level and character design. I find this absolutely okay - a valuable, good game does not necessarily result from doing everything differently. However, Horizon only uses these elements ("use" was the word, not copy) and creates something new from it. The game is essentially divided into story elements and combat situations. Both, together with the "new discovery drive", are the main drivers that always lead you back to the console and into the gaming world. The story is presented in an elaborate way: there are many cut scenes, but they are seamlessly integrated. The setting of Aloy and all NPCs in the game is absolutely flawless, especially in German/English (apart from the lack of lip sync, which didn't bother me). In many dialogues, mere pixels become lively characters, whose names and history are not to be forgotten. You can enjoy the dialogues like a movie, but the options in the dialog are limited (i.e. you do not form a relationship with any of the NPCs that results from the dialog behavior).The combat situations, which are partly initiated by side quests, have always spurred me on. The machines, especially in new areas that you have only recently entered, remain really dangerous for a long time until you have the "bow". Based on this: the bow is far from the only weapon in Horizon: Zero Dawn. There are three bows with different types of arrows and different "levels". There are slingshots, traps, etc. so that you can develop a personal style, in my opinion the bows play the main role. The machines each have their own weak points, which you only learn in several battles against them, furthermore you have to think very carefully about when you initiate battles. Because as soon as there are too many machines in the vicinity, that's it - maybe you just manage to escape. But that is exactly what always creates a certain tension and challenge that is fun.
The control, which is of course really important in the fights, I think is good. However, this may be a point of criticism: due to the extremely high choice of ammunition and types of weapons, you can sometimes get into the selection.
For me, the background music for the game is not only suitable for the fights. Linked to areas and quests, this changes according to the respective event. If there is a fight, the music becomes more dynamic and it is not always the same. Together with the other sounds of the game, such as the trampling of the machines, the sounds of the animals, the rustling of the leaves in the wind, the comments that Aloy occasionally makes on their own, and the great dialogues already mentioned, the entire tonal range is absolutely identical on one high level like the graphically presented world.
The main story is conclusive, although of course not really realistic. As the main character, Aloy makes a thoroughly credible idea. The expansion "The Frozen Wilds" is really worth it and adds another important aspect to the overall world with the Banuk, which live on average.

Certainly not all of the side quests that result from this are totally different, but every effort has been made to ensure variety. Variety is a key word that deserves special mention, especially in terms of world design and graphic splendor. From the day / night changes that really have a big impact, especially on fights because you simply can't see your opponents, to weather changes, sunsets, auroras, etc. and simply a breathtaking variety of vegetation or none. There are forests, jungles, steppes, desert, ice tundra, mountains, valleys, glacier landscapes ... I have definitely forgotten something. All of this is presented very elaborately and therefore deserves enormous praise to the development team. Not just for "the graphics" but for the design of the areas with the available elements.

Pro

+ atmospheric entry takes time
+ interesting world mixes stone age & high-tech
+ fantastic looking game world
+ a lot of details
+ atmospheric lighting moods and weather effects
+ excellently animated machines
+ great German/English setting
+ beautifully designed tutorial
+ four levels of difficulty
+ fair reset points within the missions
+ lots of campfires for quick travel
+ Game scales fairly
+ long main quest with about 30 hours of playing time
+ numerous side missions and additional orders
+ Bandit camps and machine hatcheries
+ lots of weapons and outfits
+ a lot of collecting stuff
+ Steam Achievements

Kontra

- feels a bit generic in places
- History starts relatively late
- skill tree not mature
- Treasure maps very cheap

Conclusion

The PC version of the visually stunning open world adventure Horizon Zero Dawn has been implemented convincingly and scores with a varied / captivating open world with a unique SciFi story, battles against unprecedented robots and a merciless heroine who is somewhat reminiscent of Lara Croft, but tells its own story.

Recommended
104.9 hrs on record
Posted: April 3
Short review: Overall 7.5 / 10. Good Open World game. But don't expect RDR2 (2018), AC, Far Cry or Tomb Raider levels of quality. Bow combat, sneaking around (if you want to), and taking down large mechanical animals, this game is definitely worth a sale price. But some sloppiness in certain areas cause it to fall short in overall quality compared to other games of similar age.

Long Review:
Positives: Good story (inc. dlc), and lore. Enjoyable bow / sling combat with different types of ammo. Traps are cool but didn't use them outside of "hunter challenges" that much. Corruption ammo was useless. The Open world is massive with varied biomes. Side stories and quests can be interesting. And the terrain looks great. Nice touch being able to harvest when on a mount. Some aspects feel familiar to Far Cry games (do a particular thing to unlock an area map, take down a bandit camp so locals can move in).

Negatives: Overall quality is "sloppy". Issues aren't game breaking but definitely lower immersion. In cut scenes characters have very little facial expressions, constantly twitch in odd ways, and move their arms around similar to how the original Thunderbirds puppets used to act. And the dialogue is often out of sync with the lips. Staff combat can feel clunky with long "heavy" swing animations taking way too long resulting in you missing your target. Terrain traversal is a little disappointing. Climbing can result in Aloy doing massively high leaps just to grab the first rung of a ladder that is not that high off the ground. The moment you hit a small rock when sprinting, Aloy stops dead until you get her to sprint again. Which is annoying when trying to get away from large machines. The same happens does refilling your health. The npcs sometimes cheat, seeing through the terrain (even those without in-built radar).

I have completed the game and the expansion content. I did most of the side activities and errands. I think I have about 90% completion. I waited till I was done to review the game.

First thing first - This port has issues, I was able to play with a smooth 4K60 using digital foundry's optomized settings and some NVCP tweaks (Vsync and Forced AF as well as setting to max performance mode) I still got occasional framedrops but for the most part was a smooth 60 for me - I know I am the exception to this and I think I was just able to brute force my way through it (3700x/2080ti/32GB 3600mhz overclocked and watercooled all devices) I wish it ran better for most people. And there are other weird issues like the hair physics and spotty snow deformation in the frozen north. I know they are working on patches and I hope they can resolve the issues. I didn't have a single crash throughout my entire 50+ hours of playtime. I know a lot of others are suffering crashes.

The game itself is amazing, I played about 8 hours on the PS4 pro when it came out and stopped due to the 30fps. Playing it at 60fps and native 4k it feels like the way the game should be played. It's a wonderful open world game with an interesting progression system and great writing and acting. The world feels like a real place. The lore is very well thought out and comes to you as the player in a very organic and natural way. I kept wanting to figure out more.

This game is amazing. I hope they patch it to make it run better without issues for more people as it's a shame such a great game has gotten such a mediocre port.

I highly recommend the game - but go in aware of the issues at this current time.

This game is an absolute blast and definitely recommended. That being said, performance is really an issue. My specs exceed the recommended ones but the game still crashed constantly (almost every ten minutes) when I first started playing. I tried all of the fixes recommended online - none of them worked. Eventually, I found that the default CPU and memory boost programme that came with my laptop fixed it. Given how many complaints there are about this game's performance problems, I'm guessing this game is not well optimised. However, once this problem was solved (although I still had the rare crash), this game was incredibly fun.

The good:
- great story and interesting world
- engaging combat (I don't usually like third person combat but it felt fluid once I got the hang of it)
- exploration is a lot of fun - I am not a completionist but I actually went looking for the collectibles (something I almost never do) as the world was fun to explore (aside from the annoying abundance of enemies - see below)
- great music, good voice acting and beautiful graphics
- good learning curve and progression system

The bad:
- performance problems (but enough said about that)

- too many enemies in the base game (but this was pulled back in the DLC) - this might sound like an odd complaint but you could barely walk a few metres without running into yet another group of angry machines. This was fun when I was looking for combat but an annoyance when I wanted to explore or just walk from A to B without being mobbed every few minutes. This was made worse by the fact that the enemies respawned or healed fully if you walked just a few metres away from them. It was quite immersion breaking to clear a small area of machines, walk literally a few metres away and then backtrack only to find everything had come back

- annoying UI and resource management when it comes to potions and traps - you need to scroll through a long list of items one by one to find what you need which can be lethal in combat. Some type of wheel which slows down time (like the weapon wheel maybe) would have been preferable

Posted: August 7, 2020
Horizon Zero Dawn, one of a few Sony exclusives to get a PC port, a great game in a beautiful package.

Already got the platinium on the PS4 Pro version (25h for the story/50h if you want the 100%, DLC is on another map and takes around 15h.)

Horizon Zero Dawn is a classic 3rd person view open world with a great story (including the DLC too), on the graphics side it's one of the most beautiful games of the PS4 (beaten by TLOU2 and RDR2).

In my opinion Horizon Zero Dawn is a mixture between Tomb Raider (3rd person view, gameplay mechanics, craft), FarCry Primal (atmosphere), The Witcher 3 (3rd person view, atmosphere, RPG mechanics), and some Assassins Creed (3rd person view, climbing).

The story takes place in the 31st century and follows Aloy. The world is dominated by robotics creatures : the "machines", humans on the other sides try to survive in different small groups.
Aloy is a hunter trying to discover what happen to mankind, especially why the machines are becoming more aggressive over the years and on the other side why humans have such limited access to technology.

Gameplay is where this game is really good, the battles against the machines are a lot of fun and got a lot of possibilities (especially the big one like the Thunderjaw or Stormbird), combats with humans are on the other side really poor.
The games has no vehicle except that Aloy can ride some machines like a horse (yay).
The game has a lot of collectibles, but there are not required to progress in the story.
OST and sounds are also great.

The game consumes a lot GPU power, Ryzen 3700X + 32Gb RAM + GTX1080 here and I got like 45fps average with the high settings on a 21/9 screen at 3440*1440.
For the moment it also got a lot of stuttering, and it crash randomly (I bet a patch we'll be released soon).
You can expect to gain some FPS if you tweak some useless options (wait for a full guide like RDR2 got), or to the devs to increase the performance.


Benchmark 3440*1440 / Mix High-Ultra / GTX1080 WC @ 2.1Ghz

By: Greta Thundberg


At 50‚Ç¨ if you are looking for this game since it was released on the PS4 or if you want a great story/gameplay/graphics then it's worth it. If not, then wait for a discount.

Overall this game is my TOP5 PS4 exclusive games, among God Of War, TLOU2, Ghost of Tsushima, and Days Gone, maybe one day we'll get these on Steam.

Not Recommended
53.8 hrs on record
Posted: June 16, 2021
Look, I'm a guy who LOVES open world RPG's. I mean my favorite games are RDR2, Witcher 3, and Skyrim. So when I heard that a open world RPG with a supposed great story, awesome characters and engaging gameply was coming out, I was ecstatic. But... I just couldn't get into it.

The characters: One of the main things I had heard was that Aloy the protagonist was an enjoyable protagonist. Yet throughout the entire game I could never connect with her. It seems like she both has 3 personalities and 1 at the same time. I think this is due to the fact that sometimes in the game it will give you one of 3 options for dialogue: the agressive option, the intelligent option, and the compassionate option. Because they do this it means that in other dialogue points where you don't chose what to say they try and incorporate all of the personalities at once this leads the character to feeling unrealistic and like someone you can't connect with. Now there was really only one character I liked in the game, because he was the only person who had any personality. Erend was fun and reminded me of Patrick Star weilding a War Hammer. Other than that characters also just interacted weirdly, at the begining in her home tribe everybody hates Aloy, and it makes it interesting as you feel like she's constantly trying to fit in, while also hating the people she wants to fit in with. But... This is ruined after a couple hours in the game. As soon as you leave the main village literally EVERYONE except for like 2 people in the whole game just kiss the ground beneath Aloy's feet and act like she is the second coming of Christ. But that's enough about characters.

World: The world is pretty meh. For an open world game there isn't very much to do throughout your travels. I mean sure you'll run into a herd of machines every 10 seconds but most of the time you can just run past them. However, I think there were only 3 side quests I came across organically while traveling the world. All the others were just by rando mcgee in some city town or village just asking wonderful Aloy for help because she can do everything. And then all of the side quests are boring as hell. The only side quest I found remotely interesting was Erend's, and that's listed under main missions so it doesn't even count. All the other side quests are just fetch quests, or going to a place using your focus, going to the next place using your focus, etc... Eventually I got tired of side ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• and decided to do the main mission as that was what I had heard the most praise for.

The story: The story just feels bland. I was really intrigued by the beginning as it gave Aloy obvious ways to change, and a reason to do what she was doing. But as I said, after about 2 hours they ruin it and remove any personal motivation. Now it's just about saving the world, but she has no personal stakes in the matter. Imagine if Geralt didn't have Ciri to save, and he was just fighting the Wild Hunt because that's how he saves the world. Imagine if Frodo didn't have the need to protect his friends. Imagine if Luke didn't have to save his father. That's how this game feels, Aloy just needs to save the world because... she's the protagonist I guess. The story would have been much more interesting if: So yea I couldn't care less for the story.

graphics: the graphics are nice, but because the PC port was a bit ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• unless you turn down the graphics and do a bunch of ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• even if you have a super high end PC it is very difficult to get 60 fps.

Gameplay: The combat is meh. It's a primarily ranged system that incorporates dodge rolls. You basically just dodge enemy attacks and shoot the week spots highlighted for you by the focus, and use whatever element the enemy is week to until their health reaches zero (this was on hard difficulty maybe on the hardest it's more enjoyable). Personally I couldn't really get into it but I was kind of expecting that since I tend to prefer melee combat (which is pretty ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• in this game). Overall it's just a boring system. Then we get into override, the main thing I was hyped for was riding robot dinosaurs. So imagine my disappointment when there are only 3 mounts in the game, but in actuality there is only 1 as the other 2 are literally only different by their horns on their head which do zero in the gameplay department. Not to mention that the mount system is awful in this game. The mounts barely turn, can't jump at all, and won't go on pretty much any incline, not to mention you have to completely stop just to pick up some plants (even if you have the perk that lets you gather while mounted you still stop completely) and mounts make it impossible to stealth. It's cool overriding other machines to fight for you but half the time it's just better to kill everything in stealth mode (the only fun part of the gameplay) and just skip overriding in general. And then there's the parkour, it has classic playstation parkour where the character can only climb specific yellow colored objects and NOTHING else for no reason, making world traversing way more annoying considering all the mountains and cliffs all around. It would've been better had they either not added a parkour system, made one similar to games like Witcher 3 where it is very minor and just works on anything to move a bit better, or had a fully fledged out system like AC or Dying Light. Again another meh for this department.

Overall opinion and review: 5/10, it's average at best. It seems to work for a lot of people, but I can't get into it for the life of me. I really wanted to like this game but I just couldn't. It was so mediocre in every department that it honestly felt like a chore to complete. It's not a bad game, but I can't recommend that you buy a game for $60 that's just average when there are so many better games for the same or lower price. If you want a good game with any of these then buy one of these games instead:

Not Recommended
27.0 hrs on record
Posted: July 4, 2021
I found that Horizon Zero Dawn suffers from the same problems that most open world games have. The main problem being the lack of actual exploration. It feels like the game is open world for the sake of being open world, and not because the game wouldn't have worked otherwise. It has the classic Assassin's Creed tower system, which removes all sense of discovery from the player. "Towers" are already marked on the map and, once you climb them, everything in that area is also put onto your map. Because of this, you look at the map and pick a marker instead of looking at the landscape and going to a point of interest. The game has beautiful scenery, but I had no reason to study and admire the scenery because the map already had everything I needed to see.
Another issue I had with the game was the combat. You're provided with several tools to strategize before you engage the enemy, and to adapt if things don't go to plan. Unfortunately, most of the ten or so weapon types are simply not as good as others. Throughout the entire game, I only used two different weapons and was never met with an enemy that forced me to change my approach (this was on the second highest difficulty setting). Even worse than this weapon imbalance, in my opinion, was the lack of variety in melee weapons. By this I mean that there is literally no variety. You start with a spear and that's it for the rest of the game. This wouldn't be so bad if the spear had some actual depth to it, but it doesn't. You're better off not even using it in most encounters.
Those issues aside, Horizon Zero Dawn is a beautifully crafted game with breathtaking scenes and creative, unique creature designs. The world itself pulls you in and keeps you captivated. It's truly a work of art. Shame the gameplay isn't on the same level.

Splootch
326 products in account

7 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
34.7 hrs on record
Posted: December 25, 2020
I beat HZD on PS4 and I'm very happy to revisit it on the PC. Most of the major issues have been sorted, leaving behind a solid PC port. I would say overall the port is a bit heavier than it should be still (a PC that can usually match the PS4 or PS4 Pro would probably struggle at equivalent settings), but at least the issues reported at launch have been addressed.

Graphically, the game was fine tuned for the PS4 specifically and plays to its strengths. You'll see this everywhere, in the way the geometry is very detailed but mostly static, with clothing and hair clipping into character models as they move. The world is carefully designed to push detail as high as possible on a CPU limited platform. The extra level of detail the PC port can bring will lift only a few of the console limitations - the poor texture filtering and LOD systems can be brute forced here, leading to a more consistent image. But it's merely a step up, not revelatory. Don't expect the PC version here to look like the Forbidden West trailers.

I'll also note that the original game seemed to have a weakness in animation across the board, which was largely addressed in the Frozen Wilds DLC content but was not backported to the rest of the game. Once you enter the DLC region, you'll notice conversations and cutscenes look a solid step above the main game. While I would have liked to see the weaker animations polished up in the main game, especially addressing facial animation and the static-feeling conversations, it's still servicable as-is.

That being said, this game still has substantial strengths that make it one of the best of the generation. The writing and plot is among the best in video games - information is doled out at a perfect pace, and I found myself genuinely compelled and curious about not just the past but the present. The game's lore and world building are top tier, and the way it allows the player to delve into the details is second to none. It's rare we see a first game in a franchise where all of the major questions and world details are addressed, while also delivering on an epic sweeping main quest with both solid protagonists and antagonists. The game spends most of its time constrained in scope, building up to a truly epic final act. This is a masterclass and manages to pull off an incredible amount and quality of story work in merely 30 hours.

The combat and exploration also feel great. At 60 fps the game feels even better, with a great variety of combat options and satisfying animations. The traversal tends to feel pretty small scope and intimate - the game strikes a great balance between a world with vast possibilities while remaining digestable in a small amount of time.

I love to see this game on PC where improved hardware can improve the graphical quality, if only marginally. But regardless, this is a fantastic game and I'm extremely happy to see that more people will be able to play it.

BaconBoy

14 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 1

Recommended
187.3 hrs on record
Posted: January 30, 2021
The most pleasant surprise to me in 2020, Horizon Zero Dawn went beyond my expectations. Although plagued by technical issues upon release, I luckily didn't experience many of those, and had a great journey with the game. Since then, many of those issues were ironed out with patches. I don't want to write a full review here, as many already did in better quality as I could, so I'll just point out some things that were highlights for me
The story:
Although starts off slow, and a bit clunky at parts, overall it's a satisfying tale, and it really picks up around the middle. From then on, I was playing almost without stop, because I wanted to know the conclusion. And the conclusion is great too, which in no small part stems from the fact...
The characters:
...the player character, Aloy, actually has a character arc, and if you become invested in the story, she grows on you, and you root for her. She is easily the best written female protagonist in years, without any preachy feminist undertones. She is strong and determined, but has flaws and a softer side to her as well, so as much as in this genre possible, the writers made her relateable and likable. Another great character is Sylens, but I won't spoil his role here
Also, the voicework for these two are also nailed. The VAs are Ashly Burch and Lance Reddick, respectively, and add to the characters significantly.
The gameplay and graphics:
The game belongs to the nowadays oh-so-popular action adventure genre, but I don't say that as a downside. It's also open world, and has RPG elements, which are also rather frequent qualities nowadays. With that said, Horizon delivers, with a beautifully crafted open world, that is probably the best looking game in years. In 4K, it's truly stunning, with breathtaking vistas, and gorgeous lighting effects. Post-apocaliptic America never looked better. The design for the machine creatures are creative, and they are richly detailed.
And here I will say that the combat in HZD is sick, and if you play on at least normal, it will challange you. It's a healthy challange though, and this is a thinking man's game. You won't survive against the toughest machines with just using your bow and arrows, you have to use all your tools at your disposal to down, say, a Ravager or a Trampler. To say nothing about the feared Thunderjaw. The one notable criticism I have is the melee combat. Aloy has a spear that she can strike enemies with, but the hit detection is imprecise, and overall feels rather clunky. I also missed some sort of parry or block against human enemies, as these are the ones where I felt I could spare my arrows and just strike them down without dying in the process, but I often found myself running away, and using my bow from some distance anyway. It's almost as if close combat was an afterthought from the devs, and was added at the last moment
Overall:
The game was fun, and it still is, as I didn't even touch the DLC yet. If the main game was any indication, it will be a doozy as well, but it's still a big RECOMMEND even if I only look at the base game. Although for my personal GOTY2020 Doom Eternal and Ori were already contenders, now there is another. I can only hope the incoming sequel, The Forbidden West, will come for PC too some time down the line
 

BIG GUY 4YOU
80 products in account
0
51 people found this review helpful
6 people found this review funny 4

Recommended
86.8 hrs on record
Posted: August 19, 2020
DISCLAIMER
The review you are about to read is based on my own experience with the game, my judgment, and the rating system! No third party has impacted anything said in this review. This review is also 100% spoiler-free, so you don't need to worry about that either.

Gameplay and Interaction (16 out of 20)
The gameplay is probably the most enjoyable part. Most of the encounters require preparation to get through, which might be frustrating for people that are used to the button-mashing. As far as the interaction goes, there's nothing groundbreaking, it's the typical stuff you're most likely already tired of seeing. Unlocking a specific area of the map, hunting grounds, collectibles, focus mode, bandit camps - everything you'll find in other games as well, so, there's nothing new like I was told there would be. A lot of people told me that there's a lot of new gameplay mechanics they haven't seen before, which is wrong on so many levels.

I haven't discovered a single thing that has not been already overused in other games, which only tells me that the people I got this intel from are either very biased or haven't played many similar games. There are a ton of objectives to complete throughout the map, but most of the less important ones are oversimplified. I jumped into this game with high expectations of encountering something I haven't seen before, which initially lead to a lot of disappointment. Please, just don't expect groundbreaking gameplay mechanics or diverse side quests. Most of the side quests emphasize the slow and methodical approach just to prolong the playtime and are used for a more pleasant level-up. Fast travel packs are thankfully a thing and are easy to obtain, which saved me a lot of worthless traversals.

Graphics and Sound Quality (18 out of 20)
I was truly impressed at the amount of detail on display. The world is split into sections: foliage dense regions with a ton of grass swinging around, waste desert areas with nothing but rocks as far as the eye can see, snowy areas with limited visibility, etc. The render distance of foliage is bearable while traversing the world on foot, but as soon as you override a machine and start moving a tad bit faster - all you'll be able to see is foliage growing instantly from the ground. The sound design and effects are pretty good. The score is memorable enough that you'll be able to pinpoint which game it's from even in ten years.

Performance and Optimization (18 out of 20)
This is a tricky part. There are a ton of people that have experienced all sorts of issues regarding performance. Yes, these issues have been resolved by various updates by now, so there's nothing to worry about. I, on the other hand, haven't had a single game-breaking issue. The game crashed only once during the first boot. I hate stutters and all sorts of things that make my game freeze, but at this point, all of the stutter issues that have been present at release are fixed. As far as the rest of the stuff goes, I haven't had any major issues, thus I can't say that I've had a bad time regardless of what other people were experiencing. The only thing that I don't understand is how demanding the game is, but since the world is massive and mostly full of detail - I can accept it. I hope DLSS will be implemented in one of the future updates as it would be very useful to achieve higher FPS.

Story and Content Value (18 out of 20)
The story is another segment of the game I kind of expected more from. It started strongly, and I thought it would set the pace for what comes after. Once the initial sequence came to an end, everything slowed down, and all the excitement disappeared. Everyone who had played the game on PS4 before the PC release has told me that this game has the best story of any video game. The story isn't all that uninteresting but does feel flat at times - like nothing is happening. Keep an eye on all these collectibles and data-thingies, otherwise, you might completely lose interest. I think the problem lies in uninteresting characters that you meet at the very start, not that the later ones are any better, but the first couple of them you meet are dull. There simply wasn't enough drive in the first portion of the story to push me to continue pursuing the main quests since most of the outcomes are highly predictable. What's the point of uncovering what the future has to offer if 10/10 times I was able to predict the outcome? 90% of the characters are lifeless, and it seems like someone drained every single aspect of life out of their bodies. They'll just look you in the eyes and spit some dialogue like zombies.

Some of the main quests are very interesting later on, but most of the time it is: go from point A-to-B, discover something, then returning to point A and report back. There's not much along the way to entertain you either other than the machines that are just standing there waiting for your attack turn so they can respond. Side quests are mostly repetitive stuff, doing the same thing over and over again, but at least you get to explore the world and hunt collectibles. Some quests in the game reminded me of ReCore: Definitive Edition, which felt odd - considering that the same types of quests were (in my opinion) often better handled in ReCore. I know I keep comparing Horizon: Zero Dawn to other games, but I'm just sharing my own experience, considering that whatever I've heard from other people - the game time and time again proves to me otherwise.

The value you're getting from this game is enough to justify even the full price. The fact is that the game itself isn't too long to grow tired of overtime, which is a huge bonus in my opinion. It should take anywhere between 20-30 hours to finish just the story, and between 60-80 hours to complete the game twice and 100% it. I was told to pick the normal difficulty level for my first playthrough, and I've made a mistake. All the games I play, I just crank up to the highest difficulty level and almost effortlessly progress through it, in this case, I thought the game is on the Dark Souls level of hard, but it isn't. The encounters aren't challenging if you strategize just a little bit, and running right into encounters without a second of prior planning will most definitely get you killed. I just wish people would stop hyping and being so biased towards certain brands' exclusive games when they don't offer anything superior to other 3rd party titles. Seems like it's forbidden to criticize these games like they're some kind of a national treasure.

Animations and Movement Controls (16 out of 20)
Now, let's talk about animations. I'm so sad to say it like this, but the animation work in dialogue is just... let me use an adequate word here: wicked. I won't be too harsh, but some things are just horrifying to look at. I've also experienced weird glitches such as Aloy's eyes growing to the point of an anime girl when it's raining and some weird hand & face movements on other characters during dialogue. Some of these issues have been resolved though, but from time to time a few still find their way into the gameplay. At least the controls are perfect, and you won't find yourself jumping into certain death.

Final Score and Conclusion (86 out of 100)
Horizon: Zero Dawn is a great game if you ignore all the hype Sony warriors created. It's a decent game, but simply not as good as some people believe it to be. Do yourself a favor and don't expect miracles. I, myself have fallen victim to other people constantly bragging about how good the game is, while it's just another immersive open-world title. In the end, all that matters is that the game has finally come to the PC, and I'm hoping that Sony will finally realize that there are PC gamers that don't buy consoles just to play one or two games.

58.5 hrs on record
Posted: August 24, 2020
I know that this may end up as a unpopular opinion, but I was not impressed at all by Horizon Zero Dawn.

Sure, the game had some good moments, but overall I found it very plain and boring. Let me start by saying that I played close to 60 hours (main game + DLC) and managed to see and touch almost everything the game has to offer. I will try to keep the spoilers to a minimum.

Graphically the game looks great, there are a good amount of graphical options included and I‚Äôm glad that they caved in and included the FOV slider because it really helps (at least for me). There are the unfortunate texture pop-ins, but it doesn‚Äôt happen often enough for it to be a problem.

The story starts great, but the more you play, the more watered down it gets. Halfway through, the game goes full ‚Äúman bad, women good‚Äù which seems like a forced narrative. While I generally have no issues with the thought of it, this trope should be used extremely carefully as it can be detrimental to the lore and world-building. The story gets better in the Frozen Wilds DLC and it‚Äôs one of the only parts that I found interesting and enjoyable.

Gameplay wise it suffers from the Assassin‚Äôs Creed syndrome a little bit, where most of the tasks are the same, the only difference is the location on the map. There are touches of lazy writing, the most apparent of them being the couple of side (and main) characters that die as soon as you meet them. I swear this happened like 6 times in my playthrough, I was notified of a character who was already presumed ‚Äúdead‚Äù, then we find out that the said character is actually alive. We go through hell and back, kill a ton of people to rescue them, only so they can die immediately in a cutscene. This is an easy exit that the developers decided to take because before the DLC the game didn‚Äôt allow for you to have a companion that can follow you back to your destination, so they just decide to‚Ä¶kill them off. This ruins the character impact on the story, even making them insignificant in the eyes of the player.
I have to say that the DLC majorly improves on all these points, including a more diverse side quest selection. The game also suffers from a ‚Äúno decision policy‚Äù, you would think that in a title of this magnitude your choices will actually matter? Well, too bad, because the game holds your hand during the whole experience. The only exception being the couple of times when you decide whether to kill or spare a selected character. I think the freedom of choice would‚Äôve greatly improved the gameplay experience as there were couple of moments in which I found myself asking the game to please let me make my own decisions and not follow the linear path that it had already set for me.

The PC port is horrendous, it has numerous issues with optimization, bugs, crashes and overall bad performance which are yet to be solved as of this post. Guerilla released 2 patches, but none of the big issues were fully addressed. I don‚Äôt think they will be able to fully fix this title if they don‚Äôt decide to release like a 30GB+ patch. In my experience during the 58 hours that I have played, I had 1 crash, but the performance was really poor at some locations. It is strange that a game that came out in 2017 is faced with such issues.

I had this on the PS4 for the longest time, never really had time to try it, so when I saw that it‚Äôs coming out on PC couple of months ago, I was excited to try it with M&K and 144 fps. Sad to say that this didn‚Äôt work out and I don‚Äôt fully understand the hype that it gets from the PlayStation community. Horizon Zero Dawn could‚Äôve been something great, but it falls short off the mark. If you are interested in this title, please follow the situation with the updates that it‚Äôs getting or at least wait for a Steam sale.

(In the words of Angry Joe)- I ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• love this game. Had my eye on this one since it came out in 2017 for the PS as there was a lot of hype and positivity surrounding the game. So as soon as it was announced for PC, i knew i had to get this one.

First things first, the game is beautiful. Environment wise, this is one of the best well designed and detailed open world in a game ever. The blending of nature with the remnants of the so called "metal world" is some really good stuff and well melded together. Next the overall gameplay and combat is very satisfying and hard hitting and the designs and varieties of the different robots you can find out in the world are really cool. Exploration of the world is overall a very fun experience in the game.

The story/plot of the game is overall really well done and handled and Aloy is hands down one of the best female protagonists of recent times. The story had a sort of mystery feeling to it and it made me wanna keep playing so i could unveil the secrets of the world and of Aloy. Some of the side characters are quite interesting too but not quite on the level of Aloy. The side quests also are a hit or miss sometimes and not quite on the level of the other top tier open world games.
By the time i finished the story, it left me satisfied and complete and made me more excited for the sequel which i pray comes to PC too.(note: as of this moment i haven't yet started the expansion yet so i look forward to see how that goes)

Now on to the technical issues the game come out to. I was luckily one of the few who did not have issues specifically the crashes which a lot of people were having including some of my friends. But i did have instances of low fps and stuttering at the initial release. But with the release of the patches the game seems to be working quite smooth now. With all that being said i think this game is definitely worth a purchase. Its one of the better open world games of recent time.

Overall Rating - 8.5/10

FURY_WiNTER
496 products in account
0
99 people found this review helpful
10 people found this review funny 15

Recommended
67.6 hrs on record
Posted: August 19, 2020
I waited till i have finished the game with all the quests, the DLC included before writing a review.
I think i first need to give the specs, for comparison :
- 32Gb Ram
- 2x 1080TI (one dedicated to games, one for the rest)
- i7-6700K 4Ghz
- 4K display
- Game on a SSD
- Win 10
- Latest drivers
- All settings to maximum

TlDR : A very mixed experience

1. Warning :
- I noticed that this game has a very strong anti-patriarchy tones in many dialogues. Even though Aloy was raised in a matriarchal society, she spouts a lot of lines that make me wonder how she was raised. Now, i don't really care about that. There are many ways to explain her behaviour and same for all the female characters' behaviour when they are talking. However, i do know that there are people that don't like being preached at in games and will want to avoid games with such content, so consider yourselves warned.

2. Performance :
- The performance of the game is rather nice. The game was running smoothly almost all the time. Had a few FPS drops here and there but nothing major or game breaking. From that side, it was surprisingly enjoyable.

3. Story :
- Fortunately, or unfortunately, depending on how you are looking at it, the story isn't anything new. It's a typical post-apocalyptic story where the main character has to save the day. I've seen/read/played these a lot so for me it's nothing new. That being said, since it's something quite usual, the game tells its story quite well and as such it's quite enjoyable to play trough. There was one plot-twist that i didn't expect and i was rather pleased with it. So on this side i'm feeling satisfied with it.

4. Graphics :
- I must say that the game's graphics are nothing to spit at, they are beautiful. Some places have really breathtaking vistas and exploring the world is enjoyable as such.
- That being said, this is standard for PC. Many games have graphics as good if not even better, though not the same performance to attain such graphics. One of them being Witcher 3, and another being Warframe (for the sake of comparing with a game of different kind).

5. Bugs :
- Setting aside the minor bugs that do not impact the game much, there is only one big major bug that everyone is talking about and might deter people from buying the game : the crashing bug. Now, i did have crashes, but although it was rather infuriating, especially when the game crashed in the middle of a cut scene or some other important game moment, it wasn't as bad as some people say it is. by reading the forums, i discovered that the crash "timer" can be reset by rebooting the PC, which i tried and it seems to work. Now, why do i consider this as not that bad? Well that is because i tried to play the game in sessions as long as possible and usually the game would crash after 10+ hours of play for me. So if you play in sessions of 2-4 hours, you might not even see a single crash. Also, it might be the game's way of telling you to take a break.

Now, for the obligatory comparison :
- I played the Mass Effect, Assassin's Creed, and the Witcher series, so my opinion of this game was heavily influenced by it's predecessors.
- This game feels like an Assassin's Creed game mixed with The Witcher in a world similar to Mass Effect.
- The graphics are similar to The Witcher
- The exploration and platforming remind me of Assassin's Creed
- This game seems to have the main theme as a world destroyed by a race's greed (similar to Mass Effect's story).

All in all, this game is not bad. If there were no crashes it would be more enjoyable, but it already is a lot.
I am recommending this game because the game contains the DLC for free and this gives enough value to the game for the price they are asking.

If you are concerned about the performance and the crashes, you might want to wait for the game to be on sale before buying, but after 70 hours i feel that i got my money's worth out of this game.

Not Recommended
33.6 hrs on record
Posted: July 4, 2021
This was a very narrow un-recommend, but ultimately I decided that the things I liked about this game were directly overshadowed by its failings.

It's beautiful, but empty. Aloy is extremely well modeled, animated, etc, but 95% of her interactions will be with dead-eyed puppet people with poor voice acting, which the quality of her "performance" only highlights.

The game systems in general feel like a mashup of AAA open world games from 2012-2015, and yet amazingly manage to be a step backwards in a lot of ways, despite coming out in 2017. Like I swear if these machines could talk, they would say "Must have been my imagination" and "just the wind" when I pick one of them off and then hide in the tall grass for 5 seconds. I must add that the tall grass is a very binary stealth system. You're invisible if you crouch in it, and outside of it you get spotted from 100m away all the time.

The robot AI is very predictable and so prone to getting confused by the terrain that I found myself exploiting it when I didn't even mean to.

All in all, I felt like this was a game that presented itself as being more than it was, both with its directorial choices, and especially with how tightly crafted the first 3-4 hours were, before it fell off a cliff and became an empty world full of non-characters, peppered only with collectables to justify itself.

Recommended
71.8 hrs on record
Posted: January 22, 2021
Is this just Far Cry: Primal with robots?
Honestly, a little bit ‚Äî being very reductive. I think a rather concise, yet salient description would be something like ‚Äî ‚ÄúFar Cry: Primal mixed with elements of Assassin's Creed and Witcher having significant Mass Effect overtones with some Generation Zero sprinkled in.‚Äù As in, Aloy, the protagonist is rather young and as such the narrative is explained or perhaps experienced through the lens of a young adult. Feels a lot like the books ‚ÄúDivergent‚Äù, ‚ÄúMaze Runner‚Äù or ‚ÄúPark Service‚Äù.

Combat preparation.
A significant portion of the game is spent gathering resources and traveling. Capacity upgrades are obtained through hunting animals for bones and skin, similar to Far Cry.
Universal Constants ‚Äî The game attempts to suggest that all the robots have strengths and weaknesses of some variety. However, there are a few things that are true for most if not all robots. Tear damage removes components more easily. And generally speaking, everything is weak to either fire, ice or shock damage. Typically stunning, knocking over or revealing a power core to be shot for more damage. Other weapons beyond bows generally involve trapping or impediment of movement ‚Äî area of effect damage from weapons like slings. You're also able to craft any supplies on the fly akin to Lara Croft in the rebooted series provided you've got the resources. Weapons mods can alter damage types.

Fast Travel and Merchants ‚Äî The game actively dissuades the use of fast travel by having it cost ‚Äúfast travel packs‚Äù; these are relatively expensive, costing not just shards but meat and other supplies. I actually LOVE this... narratively. It makes sense that merchants would not only take shards but take other goods as well. It's not like they could just stop at McDonalds coming home from work. But in practice it can make the game feel rather slow in the beginning. 

Mounts leave much to desired ‚Äî You have to override them in order to use them. More are unlocked through Cauldrons. But this is not that useful outside of combat as other robots will still chase you. It's much more prudent to stealth around and take your time to get to destinations. Not to mention healing the mount costs metal shards but doesn't increase a bond or anything.

Maker's Breath...
Aloy is appointed Seeker of the Chantry, herald of Andraste no... she's appointed an N7 Spectre for the Alliance Navy noo... She's IS appointed Seeker, but for her own Nora tribe. After being exiled for venturing into the forbidden metal lands. This is after proceeding to prevail at the Proving to become a Brave. That's just the intro to the game.

Look, everything is derivative. What makes a story ‚Äútake hold‚Äù of you is how it's able to relate to the player/viewer/reader. What I think Horizon: Zero Dawn does wrong is that it doesn't trick you that well. A really good story will will make you forget that it's derivative. It'll obfuscate its influences and alter them. And in the case of homages there are usually nods to these influences, but I don't see many here. It purports to be unique despite its overt theme. There is mild uniqueness but it takes some time to uncover.


Is this the ‚ÄúOutpost Takedown/Tower Climb‚Äù Ubisoft formula?
Personally, I believe Ubisoft perfected the ‚Äúmap is a checklist‚Äù formula. However, I'd make the contention that the map is too convoluted to actually use beyond setting way points or selecting a fast travel point in Horizon. But the sentiment remains. You'll take down outposts, hunt certain robots, climb towers Tallnecks.

Tallneck ascension. 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: SpaceCouncil

Climbing these reveals more locations of on the map. And it certainly feels like a Ubisoft game, the climbing even feels like an Assassin's Creed game.

That said, something clicked for me during one of the missions. Before this point I had viewed the game as slightly obtuse, mildly tedious ‚Äî bordering on annoying ‚Äî but when I found myself tying down a Corrupter with a ropecaster, using fire arrows to overheat and subsequently reveal its power core to then use slow down to nail it with a hardpoint precision arrow ‚Äî I said to myself... there might be something to this...

Some regular fights can be quite epic feeling. 
A Screenshot of Horizon Zero Dawn
By: SpaceCouncil

This was coupled with the fact that more of the story was being revealed as to why these specific robots were even there in the first place.

The game is very pretty but I feel that it doesn't ultimately serve the narrative.
The robots actually feel like they fit into the world. It seems, at least to me, there was supposed to be this very extreme juxtaposition between the humans against the mechanical giants that roam the land. But the robots actually behave like animals so they don't, in essence, seem out of place. There's no real reason to explore. Just more common resources or a collectible. It felt like a big place I needlessly spent a lot of time running around in just to get to the next objective. Much of the world feels like filler.

This is anecdotal, but the game feels a lot like We Happy Few outside of cities at nighttime. Moreover, ‚ÄúSir, you are being hunted‚Äù.

The Gist:
It's a pretty generic triple A game, in all honesty. What else can you expect? But it's a pretty good one. And it's got a lot of stuff to do. Especially if you enjoy killing big monsters or taking down outposts in a big open space. I ended up really liking it in the end. This version includes all the DLC as well.

If you've read this far, consider following my curation ‚Äî Station Argus

Spoiler Zone!!!
Let me further explain this Mass Effect connection that I propose:
Hover over the square.







Now, these things aren't inherently unique to Horizon or Mass Effect but when in relation with all the other aspects I mentioned, I believe the comparison is just.

Regardless of how easy or prevalent it is, these remain effective as story-telling devices. Kind of like amnesia being used as much as it is as a plot device to relay information to the player.

Now give me Killzone on PC, Guerrilla. Also let Insomniac bring more stuff to PC like Ratchet & Clank, Sony. Stop being silly. Resistance: Fall of Man

43.3 hrs on record
Posted: October 19, 2021
Honestly, I'm happy that Playstation has decided to release some of their exclusive only games, Days Gone, Predator, and Horizon Zero Dawn.

Horizon Zero Dawn has a pretty unique atmosphere, taking place after a catastrophic event that left the human race brace on extinction in the 31st century United States. You start out as an outcast Aloy and the main goal in the story is to uncover her past. Oh, and machines have basically taken over the world too. The rest is up to you since you should give this game a try!

The combat is good. Bow & arrow there are different types of bows (fast and less powerful or slow and strong damage), you can use shock, fire, ice traps to surprise your enemy and you can use the stealth mechanics (bushes, high-ground, etc..) to your advantage. Elemental slingshots, and also a spear for close combat.

There are plenty of side quests, trials, and collectibles to keep you busy if you are looking else instead of the main story which is at least 20-30 hours. There are also bandit camps and cauldrons that you can explore too.

The skill tree is pretty average compared to other RPG games. Divided into 3 sections. First focuses on stealth. The second focuses on combat and improving weapon damage. The third helps Aloy's health, passive skills, and resource management.

Pretty big map, there are different areas on the map ranging from, forests, deserts, mountains, ice regions. All beautiful regions where I barely fast traveled because I was too busy taking it all in.

The good thing about this is it comes with all DLC for an honestly good price where I would pay full.

Not Recommended
42.5 hrs on record
Posted: August 8, 2020
Simply a great game! Somehow made me feel like playing The Witcher 3 for the first time, which is a very good thing for sure :D

BTW people cry about crashes, bugs, etc but if you have a stable system and the latest drivers installed, you'll be alright. CPU, GPU and memory are all heavily overclocked on my system but I haven't had a crash playing this game so far, cause I actually wasted a few hours to fine-tune my system with correct voltages and timings. You can't just pray to All-Mother and expect all your tech problems to be magically gone.

Edit: Guerilla have been ignoring the texture problem with 4GB VRAM AMD cards for months, so I'll just change my review to negative and go pray to All-Mother.

Edit 2: Texture bug got fixed with 1.10 patch (6 months after the initial release), but I ain't removing my negative review. Sorry but not sorry Guerilla.
